Waqf — Endowment
beginner
4 min
Rebuilding a Collapsed Wall Between Waqf and Private Property
Ruling on rebuilding a collapsed wall encroaching on waqf land.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the obligation of a private owner to demolish a wall built on waqf land without permission, and state that the mutawalli cannot accept compensation.

Core Idea
A wall built by a private owner on waqf land must be demolished and rebuilt on his own land; the mutawalli cannot allow it to remain for payment.

When a shared wall collapses, the private owner may rebuild on the waqf side. This ruling clarifies that he must demolish it and rebuild on his own land, and the mutawalli has no authority to let it stay even if compensated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A wall between a waqf house and a private house collapses. The private owner rebuilds it on the waqf's side of the boundary.
2
State the initial ruling
Abu al-Qasim says: The trustee (qayyim) must raise the matter to the judge to compel the owner to demolish the wall and rebuild it where it originally stood (i.e., on the owner's side).
3
Reject the alternative
If the trustee offers to pay for the construction and let it stay, that is not allowed. The owner must demolish and rebuild on his own land.
4
Understand the principle
The waqf land cannot be encroached upon permanently. The mutawalli cannot accept something in exchange for allowing the encroachment.

الضمان
مال تساوي ألفي درهم فإن المتولي يتبع الغاصب الثاني إن كان ملياً على قول من يرى جعل العقار مضموناً بالغصب لأن تضمين الثاني أنفع للوقف وإن كان الأول أملأ من الثاني يتبع الأول لأن تضمين الأول يكون أنفع للوقف، وإذا اتبع القيم أحدهما برئ الآخر خر عن كالمالك إذا اختار تضمين الغاصب الأول أو الثاني برئ الآخر اهـ. ومنها أكار تناول من الوقف فصالحه المتولي على شيء والأكار غني لا يجوز الحط من مال الوقف وإن كان الأكار فقيراً جاز ذلك اهـ. وهو محمول على ما إذا كان الوقف على الفقراء كما قيده به فيما إذا سكن الفقير دار الوقف وسامحه المتولي بالأجر، وأما إذا كان على أرباب معلومين ومستحقين مخصوصين لا تجوز المسامحة والحط بالصلح مطلقاً، وعلى هذا لا تجوز الإجارة بأقل من أجر المثل بغبن فاحش من فقير إذا كان الوقف على معينين وإن كان وقف الفقراء جاز. وفي الإسعاف : ولو اشترى بغلته ثوباً ودفعه إلى المساكين يضمن ما نقد من مال الوقف لوقوع الشراء له. حائط بين دارين إحداهما وقف والأخرى ملك فانهدم وبناه صاحب الملك في حد دار الوقف قال أبو القاسم : يرفع القيم الأمر إلى القاضي ليجبره على نقضه ثم يبنيه حيث كان في القديم، ولو قال القيم للباني أنا أعطيك قيمة البناء وأقره حيث بنيت وابن أنت لنفسك حائطاً آخر في حدك قال أبو القاسم : ليس للقيم ذلك بل يأمره بنقضه وبنائه حيث كان في القديم اهـ. ولو أخذ متولي الوقف من غلته شيئاً ثم مات بلا بيان لا يكون ضامناً هكذا قالوا، وقيده الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل بحثاً بما إذا لم يطالب المستحق، أما إذا طالبه المستحق ولم يدفع له ثم مات بلا بيان فإنه يكون ضامناً .اهـ. ومقتضاه أنه لو ادعى في حياته الهلاك لا يقبل قوله لأنه صار ضامناً بمنع المستحق بعد الطلب. وفي القنية : وينبغي للقاضي لنفسي ببذري ونفقتي وقال أهل الوقف بل زرعتها لنا فالقول قوله من قبل أن البذر له، فما حدث من الزرع من هذا البذر فهو لصاحب البذر ، وهو في ذلك بمنزلة الواقف فيما يزرع له . قلت : فترى إخراجه من يده بما فعل ؟ قال : نعم ويضمن نقصان الأرض .اهـ. قوله : (وقيده الطرسوسي الخ) نص عبارته ينبغي أن يكون التفصيل فيها أنه إن حصل طلب المستحقين منه المال وأخر ثم مات مجهلاً أنه يضمن، وإن لم يحصل طلب منهم ومات مجهلاً فينبغي أن يقال أيضاً إن كان محموداً بين الناس معروفاً بالديانة والأمانة أنه لا ضمان عليه، وإن لم يكن كذلك ومضى زمن والمال بيده ولم يفرقه ولم يمنعه من ذلك مانع شرعي أنه يضمن اهـ وكان قوله وينبغي أن يكون التفصيل الخ من نسخة الرملي فاعترض على المؤلف بأنه غير مطابق لما نقله عنه ثم قال : والعمل بإطلاقهم متعين ولا نظر لما قاله الطرسوسي ! بحثاً ويكفي المانع احتماله. وقد قيل في حق الطرسوسي إنه ليس من أهل الفقه والقائل فيه ذلك الكمال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى .اهـ. تأمل. ثم اعلم أن البيري في شرح الأشباه ذكر أن قوله غلات الوقف وقع هكذا مطلقاً في الولوالجية والبزازية، وقيده قاضيخان

الانفاق
أن يحاسب أمناءه فيما في أيديهم من أموال اليتامى ليعرف الخائن فيستبدله، وكذا القوام على الأوقاف ويقبل قولهم في مقدار ما حصل في أيديهم من مقدار الغلات الوصي والقيم فيه سواء. والأصل فيه أن القول قول القابض في مقدار المقبوض وفيما يخبر من الانفاق على اليتيم أو على الضيعة ومؤنات الأراضي. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف: ويقبل قول الوصي في المحتمل دون القيم لأن الوصي من فوض إليه الحفظ والتصرف والقيم من فوض إليه الحفظ دون التصرف، وكثير من مشايخنا سووا بين الوصي والقيم فيما لا بد فيه من وقالوا: ويقبل قولهما فيه وقاسوه على قيم المسجد أو واحد من أهل المحلة إذا اشترى للمسجد ما لا بد منه كالحصير والحشيش والدهن وأجر الخادم ونحوه لا يضمن للإذن دلالة ولا يتعطل المسجد كذا هذا وبه يفتي في زماننا قال رضي الله عنه : والصحيح والصواب في عرفنا بخوارزم هذا أنه لا فرق بينهما. (ط) وإن اتهمه القاضي يحلفه وإن كان أميناً كالمودع يدعي هلاك الوديعة أو ردها قيل إنما يستحلف إذا ادعى عليه شيئاً معلوماً، وقيل يحلف على كل حال وإن أخبروا أنهم أنفقوا على اليتيم والضيعة من إنزال الأرض كذا وبقي في أيدينا كذا، فإن عرف بالأمانة يقبل القاضي الإجمال ولا يجبره على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً، وإن كان متهماً يجبره القاضي على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً ولا يحبسه ولكن يحضره يومين أو ثلاثة أو يخوفه ويهدده إن لم يفسره، فإن فعل وإلا يكتفي منه باليمين ولو عزل القاضي ونصب غيره فقال الوصي للمنصوب حاسبني المعزول لا يقبل منه إلا ببينة وفي وقف الناصحي إذا أجر الواقف أو قيمه أو وصيه أو أمينه ثم قال قبضت الغلة فضاعت أو فرقته على الموقوف عليهم وأنكروا فالقول له مع يمينه . اهـ ما في القنية فقد علمت أن مشروعية المحاسبات للنظار إنما هي ليعرف القاضي الخائن من الأمين لا لأخذ شيء من النظار للقاضي واتباعه، والواقع بالقاهرة في زماننا الثاني وقد شاهدنا فيها من الفساد للأوقاف كثيراً بحيث يقدم كلفة المحاسبة على العمارة والمستحقين، وكل ذلك من علامات الساعة المصدقة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام كما رواه البخاري في أول كتاب العلم إذا وسد الأمر لغير أهله فانتظروا الساعة»(۱) بمتولي المسجد إذا أخذ غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان .اهـ. أقول : أما إذا كانت الغلة مستحقة لقوم بالشرط فيضمن مطلقاً ثم ذكر الاستدلال عليه فراجعه قلت ويؤيده قولهم إن غلة الوقف يملكها الموقوف عليه وإن لم يقبل وما سيأتي في باب دعوى الرجلين من أن دعوی من قبيل دعوى الملك المطلق، وحينئذ فتكون في حكم سائر الأمانات فتنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل كشريك ومفاوض والله أعلم. قوله : ( وفي وقف الناصحي الخ قال الرملي: سئل مولانا شيخ (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب العلم باب ٢.
الغلة
Book of Waqf. Liability: Property equal to two thousand dirhams, then the trustee follows the second usurper if he is solvent, according to the view that makes real estate liable through usurpation, because holding the second liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the first is more solvent than the second, he follows the first, because holding the first liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the trustee follows one of them, the other is discharged, just as if the owner chooses to hold the first or second usurper liable, the other is discharged. End. Among them: A tenant farmer (akar) took from the endowment and the trustee settled with him for something; if the farmer is rich, it is not permissible to reduce from the endowment property; if the farmer is poor, that is permissible. End. It is interpreted as referring to when the endowment is for the poor, as he restricted it, regarding when a poor person lives in the endowment house and the trustee waives the rent for him. But if it is for known beneficiaries and specific entitled persons, it is not permissible to waive or reduce through settlement absolutely. On this basis, it is not permissible to lease for less than the fair rent with a significant loss from a poor person if the endowment is for specific individuals, but if it is an endowment for the poor, it is permissible. In al-Is'af: And if he bought a garment with his mule and gave it to the poor, he is liable for what he paid from the endowment property because the purchase was for him. A wall between two houses, one being an endowment and the other private property, it collapsed and the owner of the property built it within the boundary of the endowment house. Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee raises the matter to the judge to compel him to demolish it, then build it where it was originally. And if the trustee says to the builder: I will give you the value of the construction and let it stay where you built, and you build another wall for yourself on your boundary, Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee does not have that; rather, he orders him to demolish it and build it where it was originally. End. And if the trustee of the endowment takes something from its produce and then dies without explanation, he is not liable; thus they said. Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il restricted it as a research: if the beneficiary did not demand, but if the beneficiary demanded and he did not pay and then died without explanation, then he is liable. End. Its implication is that if he claimed during his lifetime that it perished, his statement is not accepted, because he became liable by preventing the beneficiary after demand. In al-Qunyah: And it is appropriate for the judge... (a dispute about sowing). His statement: (And al-Tarsusi restricted it...) The text of his wording: The detail should be that if the beneficiaries demanded the money from him and he delayed and then died without specifying, then he is liable. And if there was no demand from them and he died without specification, then it should also be said that if he was praiseworthy among the people, known for religiosity and trustworthiness, then there is no liability. And if he was not like that and time passed with the money in his hand and he did not distribute it and there was no legal impediment, then he is liable. End. And his statement that the detail should be from the copy of al-Ramli, he objected to the author that it does not match what he transmitted from him. Then he said: Acting on their absolute statements is determined, and no regard is given to what al-Tarsusi said as a research; the impediment's possibility is sufficient. And it has been said about al-Tarsusi that he is not among the scholars of fiqh, and the one who said that is al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him. End. Reflect. Then know that al-Bayri in Sharh al-Ashbah mentioned that his statement 'produce of the endowment' occurred absolutely in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Bazzaziyyah, and Qadikhan restricted it. [Missing text] Book of Waqf. Spending: That he should audit his trustees regarding what is in their hands of orphans' property to know the treacherous one and replace him, and similarly the supervisors of endowments, and their statement is accepted regarding the amount that came into their hands from the amount of produce. The executor and the caretaker are the same in this. The principle is that the statement of the holder is accepted regarding the amount received and regarding what he reports of spending on the orphan or on the estate and expenses of lands. In Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: The statement of the executor is accepted in what is plausible, but not the caretaker, because the executor is delegated with preservation and disposal, while the caretaker is delegated with preservation without disposal. Many of our shaykhs equated the executor and the caretaker in what is indispensable and said: Their statement is accepted in it, and they analogized it to the caretaker of a mosque or one of the neighborhood residents if he buys for the mosque what is indispensable, like a mat, grass, oil, wages of a servant, etc.; he is not liable because of implicit permission and the mosque should not be left idle; similarly this, and according to this fatwa is given in our time. He said, may Allah be pleased with him: The correct and proper in our custom in Khwarazm is that there is no difference between them. (T) And if the judge suspects him, he swears him, even if he is trustworthy, like a depositary who claims loss of the deposit or return. It is said that he is only sworn if a known thing is claimed against him. And it is said he is sworn in any case. And if they report that they spent on the orphan and the estate from the produce of the land such and such and in our hands remains such, if he is known for trustworthiness, the judge accepts the summary and does not compel him to detail it item by item. And if he is suspected, the judge compels him to detail it item by item, and does not imprison him, but summons him for two or three days, or threatens and intimidates him if he does not detail it. If he does, otherwise he suffices with an oath. And if the judge is removed and another appointed, and the executor says to the appointed: The removed one settled accounts with me, it is not accepted from him except with evidence. And in Waqf al-Nasihi: If the founder or his caretaker or executor or trustee leases, then says I received the produce and it was lost or I distributed it to the beneficiaries and they deny, then his statement is accepted with his oath. End of what is in al-Qunyah. So you know that the legislation of audits for supervisors is only for the judge to know the treacherous from the trustworthy, not to take anything from the supervisors for the judge and his followers. The reality in Cairo in our time is the second; we have witnessed much corruption of endowments therein, such that the expense of accounting is given priority over building and beneficiaries. All of that is from the signs of the hour, confirming his saying, peace be upon him, as narrated by al-Bukhari in the beginning of Kitab al-Ilm: 'When a matter is entrusted to other than its people, then await the Hour' regarding the trustee of a mosque if he takes the mosque's produce and dies without explanation. End. I say: As for when the produce is due to a people by condition, he is liable absolutely. Then he mentioned the evidence for it, so refer to it. I said: And it is supported by their statement that the produce of an endowment is owned by the beneficiary even if not accepted, and what will come in the chapter on the claim of two men, that such a claim is like a claim of absolute ownership. Thus it is in the ruling of other trusts, so it becomes liable through death without specification, like a partner and a participant. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And in Waqf al-Nasihi…) al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh was asked…

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presenting multiple rulings related to waqf (endowment). The author, Ibn Nujaym, addresses the liability of the mutawalli (trustee) and procedures. The passage begins with a ruling on following a guarantor (ضمان) in case of usurpation, stating that the trustee should pursue the more beneficial option for the endowment. Then comes a ruling about a tenant farmer (أكار) who takes from the endowment: if the farmer is rich, a settlement reducing the endowment's property is not allowed; if poor, it is allowed, but this is restricted to endowments for the poor. For endowments with specified beneficiaries, no reduction is permitted. Next is a ruling about a collapsed wall between an endowment house and a private house: the private owner who rebuilds on endowment land must demolish and rebuild on his own land; the trustee cannot accept compensation. Then a ruling on a mutawalli who takes produce and dies without explanation: generally not liable unless the beneficiary demanded payment. Al-Tarsusi's detailed view is discussed, and al-Ramli criticizes it, upholding the absolute view. The passage then discusses accounting procedures: the judge should audit trustees to identify the treacherous, accepting their statements in plausible matters. A distinction between an executor (وصي) and a caretaker (قيم) is noted from al-Khassaf: the executor's word is accepted in plausible matters, but not the caretaker's, though many later scholars equated them, and fatwa is given accordingly. Finally, a ruling from Waqf al-Nasihi: if the founder or his agent claims to have received and distributed produce, his word is accepted with oath. The author comments on the corruption of audits in his time. Throughout, the Hanafi school's positions are presented with details and differences.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The trustee or caretaker of the waqf.
النقض (al-naqḍ): Demolition of the wall built on waqf land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the trustee do when a private owner builds a wall on waqf land after a collapse?
A) Accept payment and let it stay
B) Order demolition and report to judge
C) Build a new wall on waqf land
D) Divide the land between them

Key Takeaway
Encroachment on waqf land by permanent structures must be removed; the trustee cannot accept compensation in lieu.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Mutawalli's Liability Upon Death Without Explaining Produce
Ruling on mutawalli's liability for unreported waqf produce at death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a mutawalli who dies without explaining the waqf produce is liable, applying the condition of beneficiary demand and the mutawalli's trustworthiness.

Core Idea
A mutawalli is not automatically liable for unreported produce at death; liability arises only if beneficiaries demanded payment and he withheld, or if he was untrustworthy.

A mutawalli takes waqf produce and dies without specifying what he did with it. Is he liable? The passage presents the general view (no liability) and al-Tarsusi's detailed condition, but the later preferred view is the absolute one. This lesson breaks down the debate and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The earlier Hanafis said: If the mutawalli takes produce and dies without explanation, he is not liable (ḍāmin).
2
Examine al-Tarsusi's restriction
Al-Tarsusi (in Anfa' al-Wasa'il) restricted: If beneficiaries did not demand, no liability; but if they demanded and he did not pay, then he becomes liable, and his claim of loss after death is not accepted.
3
Note al-Ramli's critique
Al-Ramli objected, saying the general view should be followed, and al-Tarsusi's opinion is not accepted. The mufta bihi is the absolute view (no liability without demand).
The passage also mentions that if the produce is due to specified beneficiaries by condition, he is liable absolutely.
4
Apply the rule
The mutawalli is like a trustee (amīn). His statement is accepted regarding receipt and disbursement, but if he dies without explanation, liability only arises if there was demand or if he was untrustworthy.
The analogy to a partner or participant (sharīk, mufāwaḍ) is mentioned for cases of death without specification.

غلته شيئاً ثم مات بلا بيان لا يكون ضامناً هكذا قالوا، وقيده الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل بحثاً بما إذا لم يطالب المستحق، أما إذا طالبه المستحق ولم يدفع له ثم مات بلا بيان فإنه يكون ضامناً .اهـ. ومقتضاه أنه لو ادعى في حياته الهلاك لا يقبل قوله لأنه صار ضامناً بمنع المستحق بعد الطلب. وفي القنية : وينبغي للقاضي لنفسي ببذري ونفقتي وقال أهل الوقف بل زرعتها لنا فالقول قوله من قبل أن البذر له، فما حدث من الزرع من هذا البذر فهو لصاحب البذر ، وهو في ذلك بمنزلة الواقف فيما يزرع له . قلت : فترى إخراجه من يده بما فعل ؟ قال : نعم ويضمن نقصان الأرض .اهـ. قوله : (وقيده الطرسوسي الخ) نص عبارته ينبغي أن يكون التفصيل فيها أنه إن حصل طلب المستحقين منه المال وأخر ثم مات مجهلاً أنه يضمن، وإن لم يحصل طلب منهم ومات مجهلاً فينبغي أن يقال أيضاً إن كان محموداً بين الناس معروفاً بالديانة والأمانة أنه لا ضمان عليه، وإن لم يكن كذلك ومضى زمن والمال بيده ولم يفرقه ولم يمنعه من ذلك مانع شرعي أنه يضمن اهـ وكان قوله وينبغي أن يكون التفصيل الخ من نسخة الرملي فاعترض على المؤلف بأنه غير مطابق لما نقله عنه ثم قال : والعمل بإطلاقهم متعين ولا نظر لما قاله الطرسوسي ! بحثاً ويكفي المانع احتماله. وقد قيل في حق الطرسوسي إنه ليس من أهل الفقه والقائل فيه ذلك الكمال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى .اهـ. تأمل. ثم اعلم أن البيري في شرح الأشباه ذكر أن قوله غلات الوقف وقع هكذا مطلقاً في الولوالجية والبزازية، وقيده قاضيخان
سقط

كتاب الوقف
٤٠٧
الانفاق
أن يحاسب أمناءه فيما في أيديهم من أموال اليتامى ليعرف الخائن فيستبدله، وكذا القوام على الأوقاف ويقبل قولهم في مقدار ما حصل في أيديهم من مقدار الغلات الوصي والقيم فيه سواء. والأصل فيه أن القول قول القابض في مقدار المقبوض وفيما يخبر من الانفاق على اليتيم أو على الضيعة ومؤنات الأراضي. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف: ويقبل قول الوصي في المحتمل دون القيم لأن الوصي من فوض إليه الحفظ والتصرف والقيم من فوض إليه الحفظ دون التصرف، وكثير من مشايخنا سووا بين الوصي والقيم فيما لا بد فيه من وقالوا: ويقبل قولهما فيه وقاسوه على قيم المسجد أو واحد من أهل المحلة إذا اشترى للمسجد ما لا بد منه كالحصير والحشيش والدهن وأجر الخادم ونحوه لا يضمن للإذن دلالة ولا يتعطل المسجد كذا هذا وبه يفتي في زماننا قال رضي الله عنه : والصحيح والصواب في عرفنا بخوارزم هذا أنه لا فرق بينهما. (ط) وإن اتهمه القاضي يحلفه وإن كان أميناً كالمودع يدعي هلاك الوديعة أو ردها قيل إنما يستحلف إذا ادعى عليه شيئاً معلوماً، وقيل يحلف على كل حال وإن أخبروا أنهم أنفقوا على اليتيم والضيعة من إنزال الأرض كذا وبقي في أيدينا كذا، فإن عرف بالأمانة يقبل القاضي الإجمال ولا يجبره على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً، وإن كان متهماً يجبره القاضي على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً ولا يحبسه ولكن يحضره يومين أو ثلاثة أو يخوفه ويهدده إن لم يفسره، فإن فعل وإلا يكتفي منه باليمين ولو عزل القاضي ونصب غيره فقال الوصي للمنصوب حاسبني المعزول لا يقبل منه إلا ببينة وفي وقف الناصحي إذا أجر الواقف أو قيمه أو وصيه أو أمينه ثم قال قبضت الغلة فضاعت أو فرقته على الموقوف عليهم وأنكروا فالقول له مع يمينه . اهـ ما في القنية فقد علمت أن مشروعية المحاسبات للنظار إنما هي ليعرف القاضي الخائن من الأمين لا لأخذ شيء من النظار للقاضي واتباعه، والواقع بالقاهرة في زماننا الثاني وقد شاهدنا فيها من الفساد للأوقاف كثيراً بحيث يقدم كلفة المحاسبة على العمارة والمستحقين، وكل ذلك من علامات الساعة المصدقة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام كما رواه البخاري في أول كتاب العلم إذا وسد الأمر لغير أهله فانتظروا الساعة»(۱) بمتولي المسجد إذا أخذ غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان .اهـ. أقول : أما إذا كانت الغلة مستحقة لقوم بالشرط فيضمن مطلقاً ثم ذكر الاستدلال عليه فراجعه قلت ويؤيده قولهم إن غلة الوقف يملكها الموقوف عليه وإن لم يقبل وما سيأتي في باب دعوى الرجلين من أن دعوی من قبيل دعوى الملك المطلق، وحينئذ فتكون في حكم سائر الأمانات فتنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل كشريك ومفاوض والله أعلم. قوله : ( وفي وقف الناصحي الخ قال الرملي: سئل مولانا شيخ (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب العلم باب ٢.
الغلة
Book of Waqf. Liability: Property equal to two thousand dirhams, then the trustee follows the second usurper if he is solvent, according to the view that makes real estate liable through usurpation, because holding the second liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the first is more solvent than the second, he follows the first, because holding the first liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the trustee follows one of them, the other is discharged, just as if the owner chooses to hold the first or second usurper liable, the other is discharged. End. Among them: A tenant farmer (akar) took from the endowment and the trustee settled with him for something; if the farmer is rich, it is not permissible to reduce from the endowment property; if the farmer is poor, that is permissible. End. It is interpreted as referring to when the endowment is for the poor, as he restricted it, regarding when a poor person lives in the endowment house and the trustee waives the rent for him. But if it is for known beneficiaries and specific entitled persons, it is not permissible to waive or reduce through settlement absolutely. On this basis, it is not permissible to lease for less than the fair rent with a significant loss from a poor person if the endowment is for specific individuals, but if it is an endowment for the poor, it is permissible. In al-Is'af: And if he bought a garment with his mule and gave it to the poor, he is liable for what he paid from the endowment property because the purchase was for him. A wall between two houses, one being an endowment and the other private property, it collapsed and the owner of the property built it within the boundary of the endowment house. Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee raises the matter to the judge to compel him to demolish it, then build it where it was originally. And if the trustee says to the builder: I will give you the value of the construction and let it stay where you built, and you build another wall for yourself on your boundary, Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee does not have that; rather, he orders him to demolish it and build it where it was originally. End. And if the trustee of the endowment takes something from its produce and then dies without explanation, he is not liable; thus they said. Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il restricted it as a research: if the beneficiary did not demand, but if the beneficiary demanded and he did not pay and then died without explanation, then he is liable. End. Its implication is that if he claimed during his lifetime that it perished, his statement is not accepted, because he became liable by preventing the beneficiary after demand. In al-Qunyah: And it is appropriate for the judge... (a dispute about sowing). His statement: (And al-Tarsusi restricted it...) The text of his wording: The detail should be that if the beneficiaries demanded the money from him and he delayed and then died without specifying, then he is liable. And if there was no demand from them and he died without specification, then it should also be said that if he was praiseworthy among the people, known for religiosity and trustworthiness, then there is no liability. And if he was not like that and time passed with the money in his hand and he did not distribute it and there was no legal impediment, then he is liable. End. And his statement that the detail should be from the copy of al-Ramli, he objected to the author that it does not match what he transmitted from him. Then he said: Acting on their absolute statements is determined, and no regard is given to what al-Tarsusi said as a research; the impediment's possibility is sufficient. And it has been said about al-Tarsusi that he is not among the scholars of fiqh, and the one who said that is al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him. End. Reflect. Then know that al-Bayri in Sharh al-Ashbah mentioned that his statement 'produce of the endowment' occurred absolutely in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Bazzaziyyah, and Qadikhan restricted it. [Missing text] Book of Waqf. Spending: That he should audit his trustees regarding what is in their hands of orphans' property to know the treacherous one and replace him, and similarly the supervisors of endowments, and their statement is accepted regarding the amount that came into their hands from the amount of produce. The executor and the caretaker are the same in this. The principle is that the statement of the holder is accepted regarding the amount received and regarding what he reports of spending on the orphan or on the estate and expenses of lands. In Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: The statement of the executor is accepted in what is plausible, but not the caretaker, because the executor is delegated with preservation and disposal, while the caretaker is delegated with preservation without disposal. Many of our shaykhs equated the executor and the caretaker in what is indispensable and said: Their statement is accepted in it, and they analogized it to the caretaker of a mosque or one of the neighborhood residents if he buys for the mosque what is indispensable, like a mat, grass, oil, wages of a servant, etc.; he is not liable because of implicit permission and the mosque should not be left idle; similarly this, and according to this fatwa is given in our time. He said, may Allah be pleased with him: The correct and proper in our custom in Khwarazm is that there is no difference between them. (T) And if the judge suspects him, he swears him, even if he is trustworthy, like a depositary who claims loss of the deposit or return. It is said that he is only sworn if a known thing is claimed against him. And it is said he is sworn in any case. And if they report that they spent on the orphan and the estate from the produce of the land such and such and in our hands remains such, if he is known for trustworthiness, the judge accepts the summary and does not compel him to detail it item by item. And if he is suspected, the judge compels him to detail it item by item, and does not imprison him, but summons him for two or three days, or threatens and intimidates him if he does not detail it. If he does, otherwise he suffices with an oath. And if the judge is removed and another appointed, and the executor says to the appointed: The removed one settled accounts with me, it is not accepted from him except with evidence. And in Waqf al-Nasihi: If the founder or his caretaker or executor or trustee leases, then says I received the produce and it was lost or I distributed it to the beneficiaries and they deny, then his statement is accepted with his oath. End of what is in al-Qunyah. So you know that the legislation of audits for supervisors is only for the judge to know the treacherous from the trustworthy, not to take anything from the supervisors for the judge and his followers. The reality in Cairo in our time is the second; we have witnessed much corruption of endowments therein, such that the expense of accounting is given priority over building and beneficiaries. All of that is from the signs of the hour, confirming his saying, peace be upon him, as narrated by al-Bukhari in the beginning of Kitab al-Ilm: 'When a matter is entrusted to other than its people, then await the Hour' regarding the trustee of a mosque if he takes the mosque's produce and dies without explanation. End. I say: As for when the produce is due to a people by condition, he is liable absolutely. Then he mentioned the evidence for it, so refer to it. I said: And it is supported by their statement that the produce of an endowment is owned by the beneficiary even if not accepted, and what will come in the chapter on the claim of two men, that such a claim is like a claim of absolute ownership. Thus it is in the ruling of other trusts, so it becomes liable through death without specification, like a partner and a participant. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And in Waqf al-Nasihi…) al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh was asked…
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presenting multiple rulings related to waqf (endowment). The author, Ibn Nujaym, addresses the liability of the mutawalli (trustee) and procedures. The passage begins with a ruling on following a guarantor (ضمان) in case of usurpation, stating that the trustee should pursue the more beneficial option for the endowment. Then comes a ruling about a tenant farmer (أكار) who takes from the endowment: if the farmer is rich, a settlement reducing the endowment's property is not allowed; if poor, it is allowed, but this is restricted to endowments for the poor. For endowments with specified beneficiaries, no reduction is permitted. Next is a ruling about a collapsed wall between an endowment house and a private house: the private owner who rebuilds on endowment land must demolish and rebuild on his own land; the trustee cannot accept compensation. Then a ruling on a mutawalli who takes produce and dies without explanation: generally not liable unless the beneficiary demanded payment. Al-Tarsusi's detailed view is discussed, and al-Ramli criticizes it, upholding the absolute view. The passage then discusses accounting procedures: the judge should audit trustees to identify the treacherous, accepting their statements in plausible matters. A distinction between an executor (وصي) and a caretaker (قيم) is noted from al-Khassaf: the executor's word is accepted in plausible matters, but not the caretaker's, though many later scholars equated them, and fatwa is given accordingly. Finally, a ruling from Waqf al-Nasihi: if the founder or his agent claims to have received and distributed produce, his word is accepted with oath. The author comments on the corruption of audits in his time. Throughout, the Hanafi school's positions are presented with details and differences.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability for monetary loss; here, whether the mutawalli's estate must compensate.
الغلة (al-ghallah): Produce or income from waqf property.
المستحق (al-mustaḥiqq): The entitled beneficiary of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred fatwa view, when is a mutawalli liable for waqf produce taken before his death?
A) Always, if he dies without explanation
B) Only if beneficiaries demanded and he refused
C) Only if he was untrustworthy, regardless of demand
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
A mutawalli dying without explaining produce is not automatically liable; liability depends on demand and trustworthiness.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
10 min
Accounting and the Distinction Between Executor and Caretaker in Waqf
Rulings on accounting and the distinction between executor and caretaker in waqf management.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules on accepting the word of waqf supervisors regarding disbursements, and distinguish between the executor (wasi) and caretaker (qayyim) according to the later Hanafi view.

Core Idea
The word of a waqf supervisor is accepted in plausible expenses; the distinction between executor and caretaker is abandoned in practice, and both are treated alike.

The passage addresses how waqf supervisors account for funds. Initially, a distinction was made between an executor (wasi) with full disposal and a caretaker (qayyim) with only preservation, but later scholars equated them for practical reasons. This lesson covers the rules of accounting, acceptance of statements, and the modern practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of accounting
The judge should audit supervisors to identify the treacherous (khā'in) and replace them.
2
State the principle of accepting statements
The holder's (qābiḍ) word is accepted regarding the amount received and what was spent, just like in orphan property.
3
Understand the original distinction
Al-Khassaf said: The executor's word is accepted in plausible matters, but not the caretaker's, because the executor has disposal authority, while the caretaker only preserves.
4
Note the later view
Many shaykhs equated the executor and caretaker in indispensable expenses, and analogized to a mosque caretaker buying essentials. This is the fatwa in later times.
5
Apply the procedures
If the supervisor is trustworthy, the judge accepts a summary and does not compel itemization. If suspected, the judge can require details and threat, but not imprisonment. If the supervisor claims the removed judge settled, it is not accepted without evidence.

Source Text

كتاب الوقف
الضمان
مال تساوي ألفي درهم فإن المتولي يتبع الغاصب الثاني إن كان ملياً على قول من يرى جعل العقار مضموناً بالغصب لأن تضمين الثاني أنفع للوقف وإن كان الأول أملأ من الثاني يتبع الأول لأن تضمين الأول يكون أنفع للوقف، وإذا اتبع القيم أحدهما برئ الآخر خر عن كالمالك إذا اختار تضمين الغاصب الأول أو الثاني برئ الآخر اهـ. ومنها أكار تناول من الوقف فصالحه المتولي على شيء والأكار غني لا يجوز الحط من مال الوقف وإن كان الأكار فقيراً جاز ذلك اهـ. وهو محمول على ما إذا كان الوقف على الفقراء كما قيده به فيما إذا سكن الفقير دار الوقف وسامحه المتولي بالأجر، وأما إذا كان على أرباب معلومين ومستحقين مخصوصين لا تجوز المسامحة والحط بالصلح مطلقاً، وعلى هذا لا تجوز الإجارة بأقل من أجر المثل بغبن فاحش من فقير إذا كان الوقف على معينين وإن كان وقف الفقراء جاز. وفي الإسعاف : ولو اشترى بغلته ثوباً ودفعه إلى المساكين يضمن ما نقد من مال الوقف لوقوع الشراء له. حائط بين دارين إحداهما وقف والأخرى ملك فانهدم وبناه صاحب الملك في حد دار الوقف قال أبو القاسم : يرفع القيم الأمر إلى القاضي ليجبره على نقضه ثم يبنيه حيث كان في القديم، ولو قال القيم للباني أنا أعطيك قيمة البناء وأقره حيث بنيت وابن أنت لنفسك حائطاً آخر في حدك قال أبو القاسم : ليس للقيم ذلك بل يأمره بنقضه وبنائه حيث كان في القديم اهـ. ولو أخذ متولي الوقف من غلته شيئاً ثم مات بلا بيان لا يكون ضامناً هكذا قالوا، وقيده الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل بحثاً بما إذا لم يطالب المستحق، أما إذا طالبه المستحق ولم يدفع له ثم مات بلا بيان فإنه يكون ضامناً .اهـ. ومقتضاه أنه لو ادعى في حياته الهلاك لا يقبل قوله لأنه صار ضامناً بمنع المستحق بعد الطلب. وفي القنية : وينبغي للقاضي لنفسي ببذري ونفقتي وقال أهل الوقف بل زرعتها لنا فالقول قوله من قبل أن البذر له، فما حدث من الزرع من هذا البذر فهو لصاحب البذر ، وهو في ذلك بمنزلة الواقف فيما يزرع له . قلت : فترى إخراجه من يده بما فعل ؟ قال : نعم ويضمن نقصان الأرض .اهـ. قوله : (وقيده الطرسوسي الخ) نص عبارته ينبغي أن يكون التفصيل فيها أنه إن حصل طلب المستحقين منه المال وأخر ثم مات مجهلاً أنه يضمن، وإن لم يحصل طلب منهم ومات مجهلاً فينبغي أن يقال أيضاً إن كان محموداً بين الناس معروفاً بالديانة والأمانة أنه لا ضمان عليه، وإن لم يكن كذلك ومضى زمن والمال بيده ولم يفرقه ولم يمنعه من ذلك مانع شرعي أنه يضمن اهـ وكان قوله وينبغي أن يكون التفصيل الخ من نسخة الرملي فاعترض على المؤلف بأنه غير مطابق لما نقله عنه ثم قال : والعمل بإطلاقهم متعين ولا نظر لما قاله الطرسوسي ! بحثاً ويكفي المانع احتماله. وقد قيل في حق الطرسوسي إنه ليس من أهل الفقه والقائل فيه ذلك الكمال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى .اهـ. تأمل. ثم اعلم أن البيري في شرح الأشباه ذكر أن قوله غلات الوقف وقع هكذا مطلقاً في الولوالجية والبزازية، وقيده قاضيخان

كتاب الوقف
٤٠٧
الانفاق
أن يحاسب أمناءه فيما في أيديهم من أموال اليتامى ليعرف الخائن فيستبدله، وكذا القوام على الأوقاف ويقبل قولهم في مقدار ما حصل في أيديهم من مقدار الغلات الوصي والقيم فيه سواء. والأصل فيه أن القول قول القابض في مقدار المقبوض وفيما يخبر من الانفاق على اليتيم أو على الضيعة ومؤنات الأراضي. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف: ويقبل قول الوصي في المحتمل دون القيم لأن الوصي من فوض إليه الحفظ والتصرف والقيم من فوض إليه الحفظ دون التصرف، وكثير من مشايخنا سووا بين الوصي والقيم فيما لا بد فيه من وقالوا: ويقبل قولهما فيه وقاسوه على قيم المسجد أو واحد من أهل المحلة إذا اشترى للمسجد ما لا بد منه كالحصير والحشيش والدهن وأجر الخادم ونحوه لا يضمن للإذن دلالة ولا يتعطل المسجد كذا هذا وبه يفتي في زماننا قال رضي الله عنه : والصحيح والصواب في عرفنا بخوارزم هذا أنه لا فرق بينهما. (ط) وإن اتهمه القاضي يحلفه وإن كان أميناً كالمودع يدعي هلاك الوديعة أو ردها قيل إنما يستحلف إذا ادعى عليه شيئاً معلوماً، وقيل يحلف على كل حال وإن أخبروا أنهم أنفقوا على اليتيم والضيعة من إنزال الأرض كذا وبقي في أيدينا كذا، فإن عرف بالأمانة يقبل القاضي الإجمال ولا يجبره على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً، وإن كان متهماً يجبره القاضي على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً ولا يحبسه ولكن يحضره يومين أو ثلاثة أو يخوفه ويهدده إن لم يفسره، فإن فعل وإلا يكتفي منه باليمين ولو عزل القاضي ونصب غيره فقال الوصي للمنصوب حاسبني المعزول لا يقبل منه إلا ببينة وفي وقف الناصحي إذا أجر الواقف أو قيمه أو وصيه أو أمينه ثم قال قبضت الغلة فضاعت أو فرقته على الموقوف عليهم وأنكروا فالقول له مع يمينه . اهـ ما في القنية فقد علمت أن مشروعية المحاسبات للنظار إنما هي ليعرف القاضي الخائن من الأمين لا لأخذ شيء من النظار للقاضي واتباعه، والواقع بالقاهرة في زماننا الثاني وقد شاهدنا فيها من الفساد للأوقاف كثيراً بحيث يقدم كلفة المحاسبة على العمارة والمستحقين، وكل ذلك من علامات الساعة المصدقة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام كما رواه البخاري في أول كتاب العلم إذا وسد الأمر لغير أهله فانتظروا الساعة»(۱) بمتولي المسجد إذا أخذ غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان .اهـ. أقول : أما إذا كانت الغلة مستحقة لقوم بالشرط فيضمن مطلقاً ثم ذكر الاستدلال عليه فراجعه قلت ويؤيده قولهم إن غلة الوقف يملكها الموقوف عليه وإن لم يقبل وما سيأتي في باب دعوى الرجلين من أن دعوی من قبيل دعوى الملك المطلق، وحينئذ فتكون في حكم سائر الأمانات فتنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل كشريك ومفاوض والله أعلم. قوله : ( وفي وقف الناصحي الخ قال الرملي: سئل مولانا شيخ (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب العلم باب ٢.
الغلة
Book of Waqf. Liability: Property equal to two thousand dirhams, then the trustee follows the second usurper if he is solvent, according to the view that makes real estate liable through usurpation, because holding the second liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the first is more solvent than the second, he follows the first, because holding the first liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the trustee follows one of them, the other is discharged, just as if the owner chooses to hold the first or second usurper liable, the other is discharged. End. Among them: A tenant farmer (akar) took from the endowment and the trustee settled with him for something; if the farmer is rich, it is not permissible to reduce from the endowment property; if the farmer is poor, that is permissible. End. It is interpreted as referring to when the endowment is for the poor, as he restricted it, regarding when a poor person lives in the endowment house and the trustee waives the rent for him. But if it is for known beneficiaries and specific entitled persons, it is not permissible to waive or reduce through settlement absolutely. On this basis, it is not permissible to lease for less than the fair rent with a significant loss from a poor person if the endowment is for specific individuals, but if it is an endowment for the poor, it is permissible. In al-Is'af: And if he bought a garment with his mule and gave it to the poor, he is liable for what he paid from the endowment property because the purchase was for him. A wall between two houses, one being an endowment and the other private property, it collapsed and the owner of the property built it within the boundary of the endowment house. Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee raises the matter to the judge to compel him to demolish it, then build it where it was originally. And if the trustee says to the builder: I will give you the value of the construction and let it stay where you built, and you build another wall for yourself on your boundary, Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee does not have that; rather, he orders him to demolish it and build it where it was originally. End. And if the trustee of the endowment takes something from its produce and then dies without explanation, he is not liable; thus they said. Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il restricted it as a research: if the beneficiary did not demand, but if the beneficiary demanded and he did not pay and then died without explanation, then he is liable. End. Its implication is that if he claimed during his lifetime that it perished, his statement is not accepted, because he became liable by preventing the beneficiary after demand. In al-Qunyah: And it is appropriate for the judge... (a dispute about sowing). His statement: (And al-Tarsusi restricted it...) The text of his wording: The detail should be that if the beneficiaries demanded the money from him and he delayed and then died without specifying, then he is liable. And if there was no demand from them and he died without specification, then it should also be said that if he was praiseworthy among the people, known for religiosity and trustworthiness, then there is no liability. And if he was not like that and time passed with the money in his hand and he did not distribute it and there was no legal impediment, then he is liable. End. And his statement that the detail should be from the copy of al-Ramli, he objected to the author that it does not match what he transmitted from him. Then he said: Acting on their absolute statements is determined, and no regard is given to what al-Tarsusi said as a research; the impediment's possibility is sufficient. And it has been said about al-Tarsusi that he is not among the scholars of fiqh, and the one who said that is al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him. End. Reflect. Then know that al-Bayri in Sharh al-Ashbah mentioned that his statement 'produce of the endowment' occurred absolutely in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Bazzaziyyah, and Qadikhan restricted it. [Missing text] Book of Waqf. Spending: That he should audit his trustees regarding what is in their hands of orphans' property to know the treacherous one and replace him, and similarly the supervisors of endowments, and their statement is accepted regarding the amount that came into their hands from the amount of produce. The executor and the caretaker are the same in this. The principle is that the statement of the holder is accepted regarding the amount received and regarding what he reports of spending on the orphan or on the estate and expenses of lands. In Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: The statement of the executor is accepted in what is plausible, but not the caretaker, because the executor is delegated with preservation and disposal, while the caretaker is delegated with preservation without disposal. Many of our shaykhs equated the executor and the caretaker in what is indispensable and said: Their statement is accepted in it, and they analogized it to the caretaker of a mosque or one of the neighborhood residents if he buys for the mosque what is indispensable, like a mat, grass, oil, wages of a servant, etc.; he is not liable because of implicit permission and the mosque should not be left idle; similarly this, and according to this fatwa is given in our time. He said, may Allah be pleased with him: The correct and proper in our custom in Khwarazm is that there is no difference between them. (T) And if the judge suspects him, he swears him, even if he is trustworthy, like a depositary who claims loss of the deposit or return. It is said that he is only sworn if a known thing is claimed against him. And it is said he is sworn in any case. And if they report that they spent on the orphan and the estate from the produce of the land such and such and in our hands remains such, if he is known for trustworthiness, the judge accepts the summary and does not compel him to detail it item by item. And if he is suspected, the judge compels him to detail it item by item, and does not imprison him, but summons him for two or three days, or threatens and intimidates him if he does not detail it. If he does, otherwise he suffices with an oath. And if the judge is removed and another appointed, and the executor says to the appointed: The removed one settled accounts with me, it is not accepted from him except with evidence. And in Waqf al-Nasihi: If the founder or his caretaker or executor or trustee leases, then says I received the produce and it was lost or I distributed it to the beneficiaries and they deny, then his statement is accepted with his oath. End of what is in al-Qunyah. So you know that the legislation of audits for supervisors is only for the judge to know the treacherous from the trustworthy, not to take anything from the supervisors for the judge and his followers. The reality in Cairo in our time is the second; we have witnessed much corruption of endowments therein, such that the expense of accounting is given priority over building and beneficiaries. All of that is from the signs of the hour, confirming his saying, peace be upon him, as narrated by al-Bukhari in the beginning of Kitab al-Ilm: 'When a matter is entrusted to other than its people, then await the Hour' regarding the trustee of a mosque if he takes the mosque's produce and dies without explanation. End. I say: As for when the produce is due to a people by condition, he is liable absolutely. Then he mentioned the evidence for it, so refer to it. I said: And it is supported by their statement that the produce of an endowment is owned by the beneficiary even if not accepted, and what will come in the chapter on the claim of two men, that such a claim is like a claim of absolute ownership. Thus it is in the ruling of other trusts, so it becomes liable through death without specification, like a partner and a participant. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And in Waqf al-Nasihi…) al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh was asked…
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presenting multiple rulings related to waqf (endowment). The author, Ibn Nujaym, addresses the liability of the mutawalli (trustee) and procedures. The passage begins with a ruling on following a guarantor (ضمان) in case of usurpation, stating that the trustee should pursue the more beneficial option for the endowment. Then comes a ruling about a tenant farmer (أكار) who takes from the endowment: if the farmer is rich, a settlement reducing the endowment's property is not allowed; if poor, it is allowed, but this is restricted to endowments for the poor. For endowments with specified beneficiaries, no reduction is permitted. Next is a ruling about a collapsed wall between an endowment house and a private house: the private owner who rebuilds on endowment land must demolish and rebuild on his own land; the trustee cannot accept compensation. Then a ruling on a mutawalli who takes produce and dies without explanation: generally not liable unless the beneficiary demanded payment. Al-Tarsusi's detailed view is discussed, and al-Ramli criticizes it, upholding the absolute view. The passage then discusses accounting procedures: the judge should audit trustees to identify the treacherous, accepting their statements in plausible matters. A distinction between an executor (وصي) and a caretaker (قيم) is noted from al-Khassaf: the executor's word is accepted in plausible matters, but not the caretaker's, though many later scholars equated them, and fatwa is given accordingly. Finally, a ruling from Waqf al-Nasihi: if the founder or his agent claims to have received and distributed produce, his word is accepted with oath. The author comments on the corruption of audits in his time. Throughout, the Hanafi school's positions are presented with details and differences.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): Executor or guardian with full authority to dispose of property.
القيم (al-qayyim): Caretaker with only preservation authority.
المحاسبة (al-muḥāsabah): Auditing or accounting of funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Never

The later Hanafi view accepts the caretaker's word on essential waqf expenses, analogizing to a mosque caretaker.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
10 min
Acceptance of the Mutawalli's Claim and the Oath Requirement
Fatwa discussion on mutawalli's claim and oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mutawalli's claim of disbursement is accepted and explain the Hanafi disagreement on whether he must be sworn.

Core Idea
The mutawalli's word is trusted for expenses consistent with outward appearance, but later Hanafi practice requires him to swear an oath.

This lesson examines a key procedural question in waqf administration: When a mutawalli claims to have spent waqf revenues, is his word accepted, and must he confirm it with an oath? The Hanafi sources present a layered discussion—from the general principle that agents are trusted in their accounts, to a nuanced disagreement among later authorities about the oath requirement. Understanding this ruling clarifies the balance between trust and accountability in Islamic trusts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the precise legal question: Is the mutawalli's statement about expenses accepted, and is an oath necessary? The core ruling is that his word is accepted if it aligns with outward appearances (zahir). The ancillary issue is the oath, which is disputed.
The ruling applies to claims of disbursement to beneficiaries or for maintenance—not to claims of entitlement to wages.
2
Locate the dalil and its extension
The proof comes from general principles of agency and from specific fatwas. The passage cites al-Bazzaziyyah: a judge may take wages for non-obligatory acts (like writing) but not for obligatory ones (like marrying an orphan). By analogy, accounting for waqf is obligatory, so the mutawalli cannot take wages for it, but his accounting statement is accepted as an amanah (trust).
The analogy establishes that the mutawalli is a trustee (amin) whose word is normally accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy works through the common element of obligation: what is wajib (obligatory) cannot be compensated, but it also means the mutawalli is acting as an agent, and an agent's statement about his actions is generally credible. The text also uses the principle that the mutawalli's statement is accepted 'because this is his work in the waqf.'
The implicit illa (effective cause) is that the mutawalli is entrusted with the management, so his claim of fulfillment is presumed true unless contradicted by outward evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the tarjih
There is a clear intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the mutawalli must swear. Shaykhuna (in al-Fawa'id) held no oath is needed, while the later fatwa—followed by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq—holds that he must be sworn in this time due to prevalent dishonesty. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that an oath is required.
This shift illustrates the authority of fatwa according to zaman (time) and the use of the principle 'al-ḥukm yataghayyaru bi taghayyuri al-zamān' (rulings change with time).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : هل يباح للقاضي أخذ الأجر على المحاسبات من مال الأوقاف؟ قلت قال في البزازية من كتاب القضاء : وإن كتب القاضي سجلاً أو تولى قسمة وأخذ أجرة المثل له ذلك، ولو تولى نكاح صغيرة لا يحل له أخذ شيء لأنه واجب عليه وكلما وجب عليه لا يجوز أخذ الأجر عليه، وما لا يجب عليه يجوز أخذ الأجر. وذكر عن البقالي في القاضي يقول إذا عقدت عقد البكر فلي دينار وإن ثيباً فلي نصفه أنه لا يحل له إن لم يكن لها ولي، في فتح القدير. وأما بيان ما عليه من العمل فحاصل ما ذكره الخصاف أن ما يجعله الواقف للمتولي ليس له حد معين وإنما هو على ما تعارفه الناس من الجعل عند عقدة كذا من النفقة جملة الإسلام الشيخ محمد الغزي عن فليعمل به في غير محله إذ يلزم منه تضمين الناظر له إذا دفع لهم بلا بينة لتعديه .فافهم وقوله آنفاً «واعتمد شيخنا الخ» الفتوى على أنه يحلف في هذا الزمان والله تعالى أعلم اهـ.
If you say: Is it permissible for the judge to take wages for accounting from waqf funds? I say: It is stated in al-Bazzaziyyah from the Book of Judging: If the judge writes a record or undertakes a division and takes market-rate wages, he may do so. If he undertakes the marriage of a minor girl, it is not permissible for him to take anything because it is obligatory upon him; and whenever something is obligatory upon him, it is not permissible to take wages for it, and what is not obligatory upon him, it is permissible to take wages. And he mentioned from al-Baqqali regarding the judge who says, 'If I contract the marriage of a virgin, I get a dinar; if a non-virgin, I get half of that,' that it is not permissible for him if she has no guardian; but if there is another guardian, it is permissible based on what they mentioned. And if he sells the property of an orphan, he takes nothing; and if he takes and gives permission for the sale, his sale does not take effect. It is learned from this that it is permissible for him to take for the writing itself, but not for the accounting itself because the accounting is obligatory upon him, just as if he undertook the marriage of an orphan or the sale of an orphan's property. And we have previously stated from al-Bazzaziyyah that if the mutawalli hires a scribe for accounting, it is not permissible for him to pay his wage from waqf funds. In al-Qunyah: If the right-holder releases the qayyim from his share after he has consumed it, it is not valid. In al-Khaniyyah: A waqf has a mutawalli and a mushrif; the mushraf may not dispose of waqf property because that is entrusted to the mutawalli, and the mushraf is ordered only to preserve. This varies according to custom regarding the meaning of mushraf. In Fath al-Qadir: As for the explanation of what work is required of him, the conclusion of what al-Khassaf mentioned is that what the waqf founder makes for the mutawalli has no fixed limit, but rather it is according to what people customarily give as a fee at the contract of such-and-such from the expenses. [The text continues with the fatwa of Shaykh Muhammad al-Ghazzi and Shaykh al-Islam Abu al-Su'ud al-'Imadi.]
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the mutawalli's claim regarding expenses from waqf funds is accepted and whether he must be sworn. It begins by citing from al-Bazzaziyyah a general principle: a judge may take wages for permissible acts like writing records, but not for obligatory acts like marrying a minor orphan. This is analogized to the mutawalli: accounting is obligatory, so he cannot take wages for it, but writing may be permissible. The passage then moves to the specific fatwa: when the mutawalli claims he paid waqf revenues to beneficiaries, his word is accepted if it aligns with outward appearance, and similarly for expenses on the waqf itself. There is disagreement on whether he must be sworn; Shaykhuna held no oath, but the fatwa in this time is that he must be sworn. The fatwa of Shaykh al-Islam Abu al-Su'ud al-'Imadi distinguishes: if the mutawalli claims payment to those specifically named by the waqf founder (e.g., his children), his word is accepted; if to general recipients like the imam of a mosque, it is not accepted. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this, arguing that the correct fatwa is the earlier position of the Hanafi scholars, because the mutawalli is an agent and his word is accepted for his own innocence. The concluding fatwa is that the mutawalli should be sworn in this time, following the practice of later authorities.

Key Terms
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The trustee or administrator of a waqf, responsible for its management and disbursement.
القيم (al-qayyim): Similar to mutawalli, the person in charge of the waqf, often appointed by the qadi.
تحليفه (tahlifuhu): The act of making the mutawalli take an oath when claiming expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) position in this passage, which of the following is true regarding the mutawalli's claim of disbursement?
A) The claim is accepted only if the mutawalli provides written receipts.
B) The claim is accepted without any condition, but the mutawalli must swear an oath.
C) The claim is accepted if consistent with outward appearance, and the mutawalli must swear an oath.
D) The claim is accepted only if the beneficiaries confirm it.

Key Takeaway
The mutawalli's claim is accepted if it aligns with outward appearances, and the later Hanafi fatwa requires him to swear an oath to protect waqf from abuse.

Duties and Remuneration of Waqf Officials: Nazir, Jabi, and Sayrafi
Explanation of waqf officials' duties and wage entitlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the distinct duties of the nazir, jabi, and sayrafi, and apply the Hanafi rules on their remuneration, including the effect of custom.

Core Idea
The nazir manages, the jabi collects, the sayrafi weighs — and custom determines their wages when not stipulated.

Waqf administration requires clear roles. The Hanafi school defines the duties of the nazir (overall manager), jabi (collector), and sayrafi (treasurer), and sets rules for their wages based on appointment type and custom. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains these roles and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on wage entitlement when no wage is specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify each official and their duties
From the passage, list the specific tasks of the nazir, jabi, and sayrafi. Note that the nazir handles command, management, and contracts; the jabi collects rents; the sayrafi counts and weighs money.
These duties are defined by custom and may vary by context.
2
Understand the nazir's delegation
The nazir is not required to do everything personally; he may delegate to employees. His obligation is to perform what is customary for his peers.
This prevents overburdening the nazir and allows efficient administration.
3
Distinguish the jabi's authority to sue
The jabi cannot sue tenants or lease property without authorization from the nazir, unless the jabi is appointed directly by the waqf founder alongside the nazir, in which case his authority is limited.
Al-Ramli clarifies: the jabi appointed by the nazir is an agent for collection and can sue; the jabi appointed by the founder alongside the nazir cannot.
4
Analyze the remuneration rules
If the waqf founder appoints, the official gets the stipulated wage even if above market rate. If the qadi appoints, the official gets the market rate. There is a dispute over entitlement when no wage is specified.
The dispute is resolved by reference to custom: if it is customary to pay, the official is entitled.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute and reconciliation
Some narrations say the qayyim gets nothing without a specified wage; others say he gets market rate because he would not accept the position without a wage. Al-Ramli reconciles by applying the maxim 'al-ma'hud ka al-mashrut' (what is customary is like a stipulation).
Also, if the qayyim does no work, he deserves nothing.

Source Text

قوله : (هل للجابي الدعوى الخ) قال في الواقف ليقوم بمصالحه من عمارة واستغلال وبيع غلات وصرف ما اجتمع عنده فيما شرطه الواقف، ولا يكلف من العمل بنفسه إلا مثل ما يفعله أمثاله ولا ينبغي له أن يقصر عنه، وأما ما تفعله الأجراء والوكلاء فليس ذلك بواجب عليه حتى لو جعل الولاية إلى امرأة وجعل لها أجراً معلوماً لا تكلف إلا مثل ما يفعله النساء عرفاً ولو نازع أهل الوقف القيم وقالوا للحاكم إن الواقف إنما جعل له هذا في مقابلة العمل وهو لا يعمل شيئاً لا يكلفه الحاكم من العمل ما لا تفعله الولاة. فإن قلت : إذا شرط الواقف ناظراً وجابياً وصيرفياً فما عمل كل منهم؟ قلت : الأمر والنهي والتدبير والعقود وقبض المال وظيفة الناظر، وجمع المستأجرين هلالياً وخراجياً وظيفة الجابي، ونقد المال ووزنه وظيفة الصيرفي . فإن قلت : هل للجابي الدعوى على المستأجر وهل له إجارة المسقف؟ قلت : لا إلا بتوكيل الناظر، وهذه الوظائف إنما يبتنى حكمها على العرف فيها كما ذكره في فتح القدير في المشرف، وأما بيان ما له فإن كان من الواقف فله المشروط ولو كان أكثر من أجرة المثل، وإن كان منصوب القاضي فله أجر مثله، واختلفوا هل يستحقه بلا تعيين القاضي؟ فنقل في القنية أولاً أن القاضي لو نصب قيماً مطلقاً ولم يعين له أجراً فسعى فيه سنة فلا شيء له. وثانيا أن القيم يستحق أجر مثل سعيه سواء شرط له القاضي أو أهل المحلة أجراً أو لا، لأنه لا يقبل القوامة ظاهراً إلا بأجر والمعهود كالمشروط . قال : وقالوا : إذا عمل القيم في عمارة المسجد والوقف كعمل الأجير لا يستحق الأجر لأنه لا يستحق له أجر القوامة وأجر العمل فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق بالقوامة أجراً .اهـ. وإذا لم يعمل الناظر لا يستحق شيئاً لما في الخانية : ولو وقف أرضه على مواليه مثلاً ثم مات فجعل القاضي للوقف قيما وجعل له عشر الغلة في الوقف وللوقف طاحونة في يد رجل بالمقاطعة لا يحتاج فيها إلى القيم، وأصحاب الوقف يقبضون غلتها منه لا يستحق القيم عشر غلتها لأن ما يأخذه بطريق الأجرة ولا أجرة بدون العمل .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير بعد نقله : فهذا عندنا فيمن لم يشترط له الواقف، أما إذا شرط الرملي : صرح مولانا الشيخ محمد بن سراج الدين في فتاواه أن الجابي المنصوب من جانب الناظر وكيل عن الناظر في القبض فيؤخذ منه أنه يملك الخصومة مع المستأجر في دعوى الاستيفاء لما تقرر أن وكيل القبض خصم في ذلك فما هنا مقيد بالجابي المنصوب من جانب الواقف مع الناظر كما إذا شرط ناظراً وجابياً فليس للجابي الدعوى والحالة هذه وفي كلام هذا الشارح إشارة إليه فافهم. قوله : (وأما بيان ماله الخ) قال الرملي فلو لم يشترط له الواقف شيئاً لا يستحق شيئاً إلا إذا جعل له القاضي أجرة مثل عمله في الوقف فيأخذه على أنه أجرة كما يفهم مما كتبنا فيما يأتي قريباً. قوله : (والمعهود كالمشروط) قال الرملي : فيحمل ما نقله أولاً على ما إذا لم يكن معهوداً. قوله : (فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق بالقوامة أجراً قال الرملي يحمل على ما إذا شرط له شيء أن كان معهوداً توفيقاً.
His statement: '(Does the jabi have the right to sue, etc.)' He said: The waqf founder (appoints the mutawalli) to manage the interests of the waqf, such as maintenance, exploitation, sale of produce, and disbursement of what is collected according to what the waqf founder stipulated. The mutawalli is not required to do personally more than what his peers do, and he should not fall short of that. As for what employees and agents do, that is not obligatory upon him. Even if he appoints a woman as administrator with a known wage, she is only required to do what women customarily do. If the people of the waqf dispute with the qayyim and say to the judge that the waqf founder only gave him this wage in return for work and he does nothing, the judge does not require him to do what other administrators do. If you say: If the waqf founder stipulates a nazir, a jabi, and a sayrafi, what is the work of each? I say: Commanding, forbidding, managing, contracts, and receiving money are the duties of the nazir. Collecting from tenants on a monthly or annual basis is the duty of the jabi. Counting and weighing money are the duties of the sayrafi. If you say: Does the jabi have the right to sue the tenant? Can he lease the property? I say: No, except with the authorization of the nazir. The ruling on these functions is based on custom, as mentioned in Fath al-Qadir regarding the mushraf. As for the explanation of his remuneration, if he is appointed by the waqf founder, he gets what is stipulated even if it is more than the market rate. If he is appointed by the qadi, he gets the market rate. They differed over whether he is entitled to it without the qadi specifying it. It is transmitted in al-Qunyah first that if the qadi appoints a qayyim absolutely without specifying a wage and he works for a year, he gets nothing. Second, that the qayyim is entitled to the market rate for his work whether the qadi or the people of the neighborhood specifies a wage or not, because he would not accept the position apparently without a wage, and what is customary is like a stipulation. It is said: If the qayyim works on building the mosque and the waqf like a hired worker, he does not deserve a wage, because he does not deserve both the wage of qawwamah and the wage of work. This indicates that he deserves a wage for qawwamah. If the nazir does not work, he deserves nothing, as in al-Khaniyyah: If a person endows his land to his clients, etc., then dies, and the qadi appoints a qayyim for the waqf and gives him ten percent of the produce, but the waqf has a mill in the hands of a man on a lump-sum basis that does not need the qayyim, and the people of the waqf collect its produce from him, the qayyim does not deserve ten percent of the mill's produce because what he takes is by way of wage, and there is no wage without work. In Fath al-Qadir after quoting this: This is in our view for one for whom the waqf founder did not stipulate anything. As for when he stipulates, al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh Muhammad ibn Siraj al-Din stated in his fatwas that the jabi appointed by the nazir is an agent for the nazir in collection, so it is understood that he has the right to litigate with the tenant in a claim of recovery because the agent for collection is a litigant in that. So what is here is restricted to the jabi appointed by the waqf founder along with the nazir, as when a nazir and jabi are stipulated, then the jabi does not have the right to sue in this case, and in the speech of this commentator there is an indication to that, so understand. His statement: '(As for the explanation of his remuneration, etc.)' al-Ramli said: If the waqf founder did not stipulate anything for him, he deserves nothing unless the qadi gives him the market rate for his work on the waqf, and he takes it as a wage, as understood from what we wrote below. His statement: '(What is customary is like a stipulation)' al-Ramli said: So the first narration is interpreted as when it is not customary. His statement: '(This indicates that he deserves a wage for qawwamah)' al-Ramli said: It is interpreted as when something is stipulated or it is customary, as a reconciliation.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage explains the duties and wages of waqf officials: the nazir (manager), jabi (collector), and sayrafi (treasurer). It begins with the general principle that the nazir is not required to do more than what his peers customarily do; he may delegate work to employees. The duties are defined: the nazir handles overall management, the jabi collects rents, and the sayrafi handles money counting and weighing. The jabi cannot sue tenants or lease property without the nazir's authorization. Regarding wages, if appointed by the waqf founder, the official gets whatever was stipulated, even if above market rate. If appointed by the qadi, he gets market rate. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the qayyim is entitled to wages without explicit specification; the reconciled position is that if it is customary to pay, he is entitled. The passage also discusses the special case where the jabi is appointed by the nazir versus by the waqf founder, affecting his right to sue tenants. Finally, al-Ramli's commentary resolves apparent contradictions by tying entitlement to custom and stipulation.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nazir): The overall supervisor/manager of a waqf, responsible for command, prohibition, management, contracts, and receiving money.
الجابي (al-jabi): The collector of waqf revenues, responsible for collecting rents from tenants.
الصيرفي (al-sayrafi): The money changer/treasurer responsible for counting and weighing money.
المعهود كالمشروط (al-ma'hud ka al-mashrut): What is customary (in terms of wages) is considered as if it were explicitly stipulated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general rule for the wage of a waqf official appointed by the qadi?
A) He gets whatever the qadi stipulates, regardless of market rate.
B) He gets the market rate (ajr al-mithl) for his work.
C) He gets nothing unless the waqf founder also approved.
D) He gets a fixed percentage of the waqf's revenue.

Key Takeaway
The duties of waqf officials are defined by custom, and their wage entitlement depends on appointment type and custom, applying the maxim 'al-ma'hud ka al-mashrut'.

Duties of the Nazir: Personal Work vs. Delegation
Defines the nazir's required personal duties and permissible delegation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on the nazir's personal obligations, determine which tasks must be performed by him personally based on custom, and identify permissible delegation.

Core Idea
The nazir is only bound to do personally what his peers customarily do; the rest can be delegated.

This lesson clarifies the scope of a nazir's personal work obligation in a waqf. The Hanafi school uses custom (urf) to define what the nazir must do himself, avoiding disputes with beneficiaries. Understanding this prevents unrealistic expectations and ensures smooth waqf management.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nazir's core duties
From the passage, list the main responsibilities: construction, exploitation (leasing), sale of produce, and spending according to the waqif's stipulation. These are the typical tasks of a nazir.
2
Distinguish personal vs. delegable tasks
The passage states 'لا يكلف من العمل بنفسه إلا مثل ما يفعله أمثاله' – he is only required to do personally what his peers (similar appointees) do. Tasks that can be done by hired workers or agents are not obligatory on him.
The phrase 'وأما ما تفعله الأجراء والوكلاء فليس ذلك بواجب عليه' explicitly relieves him from delegable work.
3
Understand the role of custom (urf)
Custom determines the scope. For a woman nazir, she is only required to do what women customarily do. The judge cannot force the nazir to perform work that is not normally done by trustees.
Custom may vary by time, place, and type of waqf.
4
Apply to a dispute scenario
If beneficiaries complain that the nazir is not working, the judge must assess based on custom. The nazir cannot be forced to do work that trustees do not normally do, such as manual labor.
The passage says 'لا يكلفه الحاكم من العمل ما لا تفعله الولاة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواقف ليقوم بمصالحه من عمارة واستغلال وبيع غلات وصرف ما اجتمع عنده فيما شرطه الواقف، ولا يكلف من العمل بنفسه إلا مثل ما يفعله أمثاله ولا ينبغي له أن يقصر عنه، وأما ما تفعله الأجراء والوكلاء فليس ذلك بواجب عليه حتى لو جعل الولاية إلى امرأة وجعل لها أجراً معلوماً لا تكلف إلا مثل ما يفعله النساء عرفاً ولو نازع أهل الوقف القيم وقالوا للحاكم إن الواقف إنما جعل له هذا في مقابلة العمل وهو لا يعمل شيئاً لا يكلفه الحاكم من العمل ما لا تفعله الولاة.
The waqif (appoints) to manage the interests of the waqf such as construction, exploitation, sale of produce, and spending what has been collected according to the waqif's stipulation. He is not required to personally do work except what his peers do, and he should not fall short of that. As for what the hired workers and agents do, that is not obligatory upon him. Even if the trusteeship is given to a woman and a known wage is assigned to her, she is only required to do what women customarily do. If the people of the waqf dispute with the qayyim and say to the judge, 'The waqif only assigned this to him in exchange for work, and he does nothing,' the judge does not require him to do work that trustees do not do.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a ruling on the duties of the nazir (overseeer) of a waqf. It states that the nazir must personally perform the customary responsibilities of such a role, like maintenance and rent collection, but he is not obliged to personally perform tasks that can be delegated to employees or agents. The standard is based on what similar appointees typically do ('urf). If the nazir is a woman, her duties are limited to what women customarily do. The passage also clarifies that if the waqf beneficiaries complain that the nazir is not working, the judge cannot force him to do work that is not normally done by trustees; the nazir's role is supervisory, not menial.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nāẓir): The person appointed to manage the affairs of a waqf, including construction, leasing, and distribution of proceeds.
العرف (al-ʿurf): Customary practice; used here to determine the scope of work expected of the nazir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The beneficiaries' demands.

Key Takeaway
The nazir's personal duties are determined by custom; he is not obliged to do tasks that can be delegated.

Functions of Nazir, Jabi, and Sayrafi in Waqf
Defines the distinct functions of three waqf officials based on custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the functions of the nazir, jabi, and sayrafi in a waqf, and state the role of custom (urf) in determining their duties.

Core Idea
Custom defines the duties of waqf officials: nazir manages, jabi collects, sayrafi verifies currency, and jabi acts only with nazir's authorization.

In a waqf, the founder may stipulate multiple officials to manage, collect, and handle finances. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies their distinct roles using the principle of custom (urf), a key Hanafi concept. Understanding these functions is essential for proper waqf administration and preventing overreach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three officials
Find the three names mentioned in the passage: nazir, jabi, and sayrafi. Note that they are appointed by the waqif in the deed.
2
Extract each official's specific duty
From the text, list what each official does: nazir commands, forbids, administers, contracts, and receives money; jabi collects rents monthly and on land-tax basis; sayrafi examines and weighs money.
The duties are based on custom (urf), not fixed by explicit legal text.
3
Analyze the jabi's limitations
Note that the jabi cannot sue a tenant or lease a roofed building except with the nazir's authorization. This shows the jabi's role is purely collection, not management.
This restriction prevents conflict of authority.
4
Recognize the role of custom
The passage states that these functions are based on custom (urf), as mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. This means the specific duties may vary by time and place, but the general framework remains.
Custom fills in details where the founding deed is silent.
5
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Imagine a waqf where the deed only says 'appoint a nazir and a jabi.' What can each do? Use the passage to reason: nazir manages all, jabi collects but cannot lease or sue without permission.
This demonstrates the practical application of the definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا شرط الواقف ناظراً وجابياً وصيرفياً فما عمل كل منهم؟ قلت : الأمر والنهي والتدبير والعقود وقبض المال وظيفة الناظر، وجمع المستأجرين هلالياً وخراجياً وظيفة الجابي، ونقد المال ووزنه وظيفة الصيرفي . فإن قلت : هل للجابي الدعوى على المستأجر وهل له إجارة المسقف؟ قلت : لا إلا بتوكيل الناظر، وهذه الوظائف إنما يبتنى حكمها على العرف فيها كما ذكره في فتح القدير في المشرف.
If you ask: 'If the waqif specifies a nazir, a jābi, and a ṣayrafī, what is the work of each?' I answer: Commanding and forbidding, administration, contracts, and receipt of money are the duties of the nazir. Collecting from tenants on a monthly (hilālī) and land-tax (kharājī) basis is the duty of the jābi. Examining and weighing money is the duty of the ṣayrafī. If you ask: 'Does the jābi have the right to sue the tenant, and does he have the right to lease a roofed building?' I answer: No, except with the authorization of the nazir. These duties are based on custom (ʿurf) as mentioned in Fatḥ al-Qadīr under 'al-mushrif'.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed breakdown of the responsibilities of three key waqf officials when all are stipulated by the waqif. The nazir is the overall manager: he has authority to manage, contract, and receive funds. The jabi (collector) is responsible for collecting rents—whether periodic (hilali) or annual (kharaji). The sayrafi (money exchanger) handles the valuation and weighing of currency. Importantly, the jabi cannot independently sue tenants or lease properties unless explicitly authorized by the nazir. The passage emphasizes that these definitions are not fixed but rely on local custom (ʿurf), a fundamental principle in Hanafi waqf law.

Key Terms
الجابي (al-jābī): The collector of rents and revenues from waqf properties.
الصيرفي (al-ṣayrafī): The treasurer or money-changer responsible for examining and weighing currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the function of the jabi in a waqf as defined in this passage?
A) Administering contracts and receiving money.
B) Collecting rents from tenants on a regular basis.
C) Examining and weighing the currency.
D) Appointing and dismissing other officials.

Key Takeaway
The duties of waqf officials are determined by custom: nazir manages overall, jabi collects rents, sayrafi verifies currency, and the jabi cannot sue or lease without the nazir's authorization.
