Entitlement of Waqf Appointee: Waqif vs Qadi Appointment
Discusses remuneration of waqf appointee and intra-Hanafi dispute on customary wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the remuneration rules for waqif-appointed and qadi-appointed nazirs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a qadi's appointee deserves a wage without explicit specification.

Core Idea
A qadi-appointed qayyim's wage depends on custom: two Hanafi views, one requiring a stipulation, the other relying on custom as substitute.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a practical waqf question: when does a nazir get paid? It distinguishes between the waqif's appointee (gets stipulated amount, even above market) and the qadi's appointee (gets standard wage). A dispute arises when the qadi appoints without specifying a wage. Two views from al-Quniya set the terms, and the commentator invokes the maxim 'al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ' to favor the second view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of appointment
The passage distinguishes nazir appointed by the waqif vs. by the qadi. Note the different rules: waqif's appointee gets stipulated amount (even above market); qadi's appointee gets ujrat al-mithl.
2
State the core dispute
For a qadi-appointed qayyim, if the qadi sets no wage, does the qayyim get paid? Two narrations from al-Quniya: first says no wage; second says standard wage because custom implies it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the proofs for each view
First view: absolute appointment implies no wage unless stipulated. Second view: 'al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ' – custom fills the gap; people do not accept trusteeship without pay.
The second view rests on the Hanafi recognition of ʿurf as a legal source.
4
Analyze the tarjih
The commentator leans toward the second view, as indicated by citing the maxim. This is the mufta bihi position in later fatwa.
Tarjih is by Ibn Nujaym in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a qadi appoints a qayyim for a mosque, says nothing about pay. The qayyim works for a year. Under the first view, he gets nothing; under the second, he gets ujrat al-mithl.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a real-world difference in entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان ما له فإن كان من الواقف فله المشروط ولو كان أكثر من أجرة المثل، وإن كان منصوب القاضي فله أجر مثله، واختلفوا هل يستحقه بلا تعيين القاضي؟ فنقل في القنية أولاً أن القاضي لو نصب قيماً مطلقاً ولم يعين له أجراً فسعى فيه سنة فلا شيء له. وثانيا أن القيم يستحق أجر مثل سعيه سواء شرط له القاضي أو أهل المحلة أجراً أو لا، لأنه لا يقبل القوامة ظاهراً إلا بأجر والمعهود كالمشروط . قال : وقالوا : إذا عمل القيم في عمارة المسجد والوقف كعمل الأجير لا يستحق الأجر لأنه لا يستحق له أجر القوامة وأجر العمل فهذا يدل على أنه يستحق بالقوامة أجراً .اهـ. وإذا لم يعمل الناظر لا يستحق شيئاً لما في الخانية : ولو وقف أرضه على مواليه مثلاً ثم مات فجعل القاضي للوقف قيما وجعل له عشر الغلة في الوقف وللوقف طاحونة في يد رجل بالمقاطعة لا يحتاج فيها إلى القيم، وأصحاب الوقف يقبضون غلتها منه لا يستحق القيم عشر غلتها لأن ما يأخذه بطريق الأجرة ولا أجرة بدون العمل .اهـ.
As for the statement of what he receives: if he is appointed by the waqif, he receives the stipulated amount even if it is more than the standard wage. If he is appointed by the qadi, he receives his standard wage (ujrat al-mithl). They differed: does he receive it without the qadi's specification? It is reported in al-Quniya, first, that if the qadi appoints a qayyim absolutely without specifying a wage, and he works for a year, he gets nothing. Second, that the qayyim deserves the standard wage for his work, whether the qadi or the people of the locality stipulated a wage or not, because one does not normally accept trusteeship without a wage, and what is customary is like a stipulation. He said: They said: if the qayyim works on the construction of the mosque or the waqf like a hired worker, he does not deserve a wage because he does not deserve both the wage of trusteeship and the wage of work. This indicates that he deserves a wage for trusteeship. And if the nazir does not work, he deserves nothing, as in al-Khaniyya: if a person waqf his land to his relatives, then dies, and the qadi appoints a qayyim for the waqf and gives him a tenth of the produce, but the waqf has a mill in the hands of a man on a fixed rent (muqāṭaʿa) that needs no qayyim, and the waqf beneficiaries collect the rent from him, the qayyim does not deserve a tenth of the mill's produce because he receives (the tenth) by way of a wage, and there is no wage without work.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage addresses the remuneration of a waqf appointee (nazir or qayyim). It distinguishes between the waqif's appointee, who gets whatever is stipulated even if above market rate, and the qadi's appointee, who gets the standard wage (ujrat al-mithl). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the qadi's appointee receives any wage if the qadi did not specify an amount. Two views are cited from al-Quniya: first, if the qadi appointed absolutely and the qayyim worked a year, he gets nothing; second, he deserves the standard wage because custom fills in for stipulation (al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ). The passage then clarifies that if the appointee also does physical labor (like construction), he does not get double pay—trusteeship wage already covers that. Finally, a case from al-Khaniyya illustrates that if the appointee does no work for a particular property (like a mill on fixed rent), he gets no share of its income.

Key Terms
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The standard or customary wage for similar work in the market.
المعهود كالمشروط (al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ): A legal maxim meaning 'what is customary is like a stipulation'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second view in al-Quniya, why does a qayyim appointed by the qadi without specified wage still deserve payment?
A) Because the waqf must always pay a wage.
B) Because the qayyim explicitly demanded it.
C) Because custom dictates that trusteeship is not accepted without a wage, and custom functions like a stipulation.
D) Because the waqif required it.

Key Takeaway
The remuneration of a qadi-appointed waqf manager depends on custom; in the Hanafi school, custom (ʿurf) can substitute for an explicit wage agreement.

Waqf — Endowment

Final Resolution on Waqf Appointee's Wage and Custom
Summarizes the correct ruling, distinguishing waqif vs qadi appointment and work condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for waqf appointee wage entitlement and apply the Hanafi positions correctly.

Core Idea
Waqf appointee's wage depends on source: waqif's stipulation, qadi's set wage, or custom — work required unless stipulation is unconditional.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq presents the final authoritative resolution (taḥrīr) on when a waqf appointee (nazir) is entitled to a wage. The author synthesizes earlier views and corrects a common misinterpretation of Qāḍīkhān. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing who appointed the appointee and whether work was actually performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the appointment source
Determine whether the appointee was appointed by the waqif (with or without a stipulation) or by the qadi. This is the primary distinction in the text.
Waqif's stipulation is unconditional
2
Apply the work condition
If the waqif specified a wage without making it conditional on work, the appointee gets it even without working. If the qadi appointed, work is required for any wage entitlement.
Except when waqif stipulates otherwise
3
Check for custom (ʿurf)
If the qadi appointed without specifying a wage, custom (al-maʿhūd) acts as a stipulation: if it is customary that such work is only done for a wage, the appointee gets the standard wage (ujrat al-mithl).
Maxim: al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ
4
Limit the wage to standard rate
Even if the qadi sets a wage, it cannot exceed ujrat al-mithl. The second qadi deducts any excess, correcting a common error.
Refutes misinterpretation of Qāḍīkhān
5
Consider special cases (construction, hilālī)
During reconstruction, all beneficiaries' shares may be cut unless the nazir works personally. For a hilālī waqf (non-productive), no wage is due without work except for construction.
Protects waqf assets

تؤخر العمارة إذا احتيج إليها وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها لها إن لم يخف ضرر بين فإن خيف قدم، وأما الناظر فإن كان المشروط له من الواقف فهو كأحد المستحقين، فإذا قطعوا للعمارة قطع إلا أن يعمل فيأخذ قدر أجرته وإن لم يعمل لا يأخذ شيئاً اهـ. ثم نقل مسألة الطاحون بعده من غير فصل بين الكلامين ثم أعقبها بقوله : فهذا عندنا فيمن لم يشترط له الواقف الخ. وأنت خبير بأن المتولي يقطع في زمن التعمير مطلقاً اشترط له الواقف أو لم يشترط إلا أن يعمل فيأخذ قدر أجرته ولا تعرض في مسألة الطاحون للتعمير، فعوده لذلك غير متجه بل المتجه الفرق بين ناظر وناظر، فتحرر أن الواقف إن عين له شيئاً فهو له كثيراً كان أو قليلاً على عمل وإن لم يعمل لا يستحق أجرة، وبمثله صرح في الأشباه في كتاب الدعوى. وإن نصبه القاضي ولم يعين له شيئاً ينظر ؛ إن كان المعهود أن لا يعمل إلا بأجرة المثل فله أجرة المثل لأن المعهود كالمشروط وإلا فلا شيء له فاغتنم هذا التحرير فإنه يجب إليه المصير لأنه المفهوم من عباراتهم والمتبادر من كلماتهم، وقوله في الفتح فهذا إشارة إلى الحكم المذكور في مسألة الطاحون وقوله «كان من جملة الموقوف عليهم أي فيستحق الريع بالشرط لا بالعمل كاستحقاق الموقوف عليهم فإنه
In Fatḥ al-Qadīr after quoting it: 'This is with us for one for whom the waqif did not stipulate. But if he stipulates...' Al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh Muḥammad b. Sirāj al-Dīn stated in his fatāwā that the jābī appointed by the nazir is an agent of the nazir in collection, so it follows that he can litigate with the tenant regarding claims of receipt, because it is established that the agent for collection is a litigant in that. What is here is restricted to the jābī appointed by the waqif together with the nazir, as when a nazir and a jābī are stipulated; then the jābī does not have the right to sue in this case. And in the words of this commentator there is an indication, so understand. His statement: 'As for the statement of what he receives, etc.' Al-Ramli said: If the waqif did not stipulate anything for him, he deserves nothing unless the judge gives him the standard wage for his work in the waqf, which he takes as a wage, as understood from what we wrote later. His statement: 'What is customary is like a stipulation', al-Ramli said: He interpreted the first narration as applying when there is no custom. His statement: 'This indicates that he deserves a wage for trusteeship', al-Ramli said: It is interpreted as applying when something was stipulated for him, if it is customary, as a reconciliation. The book of waqf: 'absence' (?) he was among the beneficiaries. The apparent meaning is that it refers to cutting the known wage during the time of construction. As for entitlement when there is no work, there is no difference between one nazir and another. Some inexperienced people have clung to the saying of Qāḍīkhān and made for him a tenth of the produce on the waqf, claiming that the qadi may assign to the mutawallī a tenth of the produce regardless of the standard wage, and this is wrong. He said in al-Quniya: The qadi was removed, and the qayyim claimed that the qadi had given him such and such monthly or yearly, and the removed one confirmed it; it is not accepted without evidence. Then, if what he specified was the standard wage for his work or less, the second (qadi) gives it to him; otherwise, he deducts the excess and gives him the remainder. This shows that the second qadi deducts what exceeds the standard wage, indicating that it is not valid for the qadi to fix for the nazir a known wage more than the standard wage. If you ask: 'If the waqf is hilālī and the nazir has assigned the beneficiaries to the shops and houses (to collect rents directly), and they receive from the residents, does the nazir deserve a known wage?' I answer: He does not deserve a known wage for the hilālī because he does no work in it, except for construction, as we mentioned from Qāḍīkhān in the mill case. The qayyim can appoint an agent and dismiss him, and he may give the agent something from his own salary, and he can stop it. If the waqif stipulates for the qayyim to delegate his affairs after his death similar to what he stipulated during his life, and the qayyim gives some of his salary to a man he appoints as qayyim, and remains silent about the rest, then dies, it belongs to his executor only. His statement: 'and gave him a tenth of the produce' al-Ramli said: i.e., in exchange for his work in the waqf. His statement: 'and the apparent meaning is that it refers to cutting the known wage', al-Ramli said: the determined view is contrary to this apparent meaning, because if interpreted that way, the meaning would be corrupt, as it would then imply that it is cut when the waqif stipulates but not otherwise, and this is corrupt—ponder. I also say: How can this be said when he first stated: 'And construction should not be delayed if needed, and the endowments allocated to the beneficiaries are cut for it if no evident harm is feared; if harm is feared, it is prioritized.' As for the nazir, if the stipulation is from the waqif, he is like one of the beneficiaries; if they are cut for construction, he is also cut, unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage, and if he does not work, he takes nothing. Then he quoted the mill case after that without separating the two statements, then followed it with: 'This is with us for one for whom the waqif did not stipulate, etc.' You are aware that the mutawallī is cut in times of construction absolutely, whether the waqif stipulated for him or not, unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage. There is no reference to construction in the mill case, so his return to that is not appropriate; rather, the appropriate view is the distinction between one nazir and another. It is settled that if the waqif specifies something for him, it is his, whether much or little, according to what he stipulated, whether he works or not, as long as he did not stipulate it in exchange for work—as is understood from our saying 'according to what he stipulated'. If the waqif did not specify anything for him and the qadi specified his standard wage, it is valid. If he specifies more, the excess over the standard wage is prevented. This is if he works; if he does not work, he does not deserve a wage. This is stated similarly in al-Ashbāh in the book of claims. If the qadi appoints him without specifying anything, it is considered: if it is customary that he does not work except for the standard wage, then he gets the standard wage, because custom is like a stipulation; otherwise, nothing. So take this analysis, for it must be followed, because it is the understanding of their expressions and the apparent meaning of their words. And his statement in al-Fatḥ: 'This' refers to the ruling mentioned in the mill case, and his statement: 'he was among the beneficiaries' meaning he deserves the income by stipulation, not by work, like the entitlement of the beneficiaries.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This extensive passage is the final resolution (taḥrīr) by the author of al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq on the remuneration of waqf officials. It synthesizes earlier discussions and corrects common errors. The author begins by quoting al-Ramlī's comments on the jābī's authority to sue, then moves to the central question of remuneration. He distinguishes three scenarios: (1) If the waqif specifies a payment, the appointee gets it regardless of work, unless it was explicitly made conditional on work. (2) If the qadi specifies a wage, it must not exceed the standard wage (ujrat al-mithl), and the appointee only gets it if he actually works. (3) If the qadi appoints without specifying any wage, the appointee is entitled to the standard wage only if it is customary that such work is compensated (following the maxim al-maʿhūd ka al-mashrūṭ); otherwise, nothing. The passage also clarifies that during periods of reconstruction, all beneficiaries—including the nazir—may have their shares cut unless they personally work. A critical warning is given against misinterpreting Qāḍīkhān's statement about the tenth share; the qadi cannot arbitrarily assign a high wage ignoring market rates. Finally, the author emphasizes that this taḥrīr is the correct position based on the collective understanding of earlier scholars.

Key Terms
التحرير (al-taḥrīr): The final, authoritative determination of a legal issue after reconciling conflicting views.
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The standard market wage for similar work, used as a benchmark for qadi-appointed wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final taḥrīr, if the qadi appoints a nazir without specifying any wage, when is the nazir entitled to the standard wage?
A) Always, because the appointment implies a wage.
B) Only if it is customary that such work is not done without the standard wage.
C) Only if the waqif also stipulates a wage.
D) Never, because the qadi must specify a wage.

Key Takeaway
The waqf appointee's wage entitlement hinges on who appointed them, whether work was done, and the role of custom — with the qadi never permitted to exceed the standard wage.

Waqf — Endowment

Compensation of the Waqf Administrator: Waqif's Conditions and Judge's Role
Explaining the ruling on the administrator's compensation and the effect of conditions set by the waqif and qadhi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the compensation of the waqf administrator, distinguish between the waqif's stipulation and the judge's setting, and apply the rule that custom is like a condition.

Core Idea
The waqif's condition on compensation is binding; the judge cannot exceed the equivalent wage.

In Hanafi waqf law, the compensation (ma'lum) of the administrator (nazir) can be set by the waqif or the judge. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the waqif's stipulation is binding even if the administrator does not work, unless it was explicitly tied to work. However, if the judge sets the compensation, it must not exceed the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl). Understanding this distinction is crucial for valid waqf administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the roles: waqif (endower), nazir/qayyim (administrator), qadhi (judge). The compensation can originate from either the waqif or the judge.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Separate the case where the waqif sets a specific compensation from the case where the judge sets it. The ruling differs for each.
3
Apply the ruling for waqif-set compensation
If the waqif specifies an amount, it is binding whether the administrator works or not, as long as it was not explicitly tied to work. The administrator takes it as a condition of the waqf.
The text: 'if the waqif specified something for him, it is his, whether he works or not.'
4
Apply the ruling for judge-set compensation
If the judge sets compensation, it must be at the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl) and cannot exceed it. The administrator receives it only if he works, unless custom dictates otherwise.
Judge cannot assign more than the equivalent wage; excess is deducted.
5
Incorporate custom
Custom ('urf) is considered like a condition. If it is customary that the administrator is paid for work, he gets the equivalent wage even without explicit stipulation.
The text: 'the custom is like a condition.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يقبل إلا ببينة، ثم إن كان ما عينه أجر مثل عمله أو دونه يعطيه الثاني وإلا يحط الزيادة ويعطيه الباقي اهـ. فقد أفاد أن القاضي الثاني يحط ما زاد على أجر المثل فأفاد عدم صحة تقرير القاضي للناظر معلوماً لأجل التعمير كما قدمناه عن قاضیخان في مسألة الطاحونة ، وللقيم التوكيل وعزل وكيله وله أن يجعل للوكيل من معلومه شيئاً، وله قطعه عنه. ولو شرط الواقف للقيم تفويض أمره بعد مماته مثل ما شرطه له في حياته فجعل القيم بعض معلومه لرجل أقامه قيماً وسكت عن الباقي ثم مات، يكون لوصيه ما . له فقط : سمی ويرجع قوله : (وجعل له عشر (الغلة قال الرملي أي في مقابلة عمله في الوقف قوله : (والظاهر أنه عائد إلى قطع المعلوم الخ) قال الرملي : المتعين خلاف هذا الظاهر إذ لو حمل عليه لفسد المعنى إذ يرجع والحال هذه إلى أنه يقطع إذا شرط له الواقف لا في غيره وهذا فاسد تأمل. وأقول أيضاً: كيف يقال هذا وقد قدم أولاً قوله فيه ولا تؤخر العمارة إذا احتيج إليها وتقطع الجهات الموقوف عليها لها إن لم يخف ضرر بين فإن خيف قدم، وأما الناظر فإن كان المشروط له من الواقف فهو كأحد المستحقين، فإذا قطعوا للعمارة قطع إلا أن يعمل فيأخذ قدر أجرته وإن لم يعمل لا يأخذ شيئاً اهـ. ثم نقل مسألة الطاحون بعده من غير فصل بين الكلامين ثم أعقبها بقوله : فهذا عندنا فيمن لم يشترط له الواقف الخ. وأنت خبير بأن المتولي يقطع في زمن التعمير مطلقاً اشترط له الواقف أو لم يشترط إلا أن يعمل فيأخذ قدر أجرته ولا تعرض في مسألة الطاحون للتعمير، فعوده لذلك غير متجه بل المتجه الفرق بين ناظر وناظر، فتحرر أن الواقف إن عين له شيئاً فهو له كثيراً كان أو قليلاً على حسب ما شرطه عمل أو لم يعمل حيث لم يشرطه في مقابلة العمل كما هو مفهوم من قولنا على حسب ما شرطه . وإن لم يعين له الواقف وعين له القاضي أجرة مثله جاز، وإن عين أكثر يمنع عنه الزائد عن أجرة المثل. هذا إن عمل وإن لم يعمل لا يستحق أجرة، وبمثله صرح في الأشباه في كتاب الدعوى. وإن نصبه القاضي ولم يعين له شيئاً ينظر ؛ إن كان المعهود أن لا يعمل إلا بأجرة المثل فله أجرة المثل لأن المعهود كالمشروط وإلا فلا شيء له فاغتنم هذا التحرير فإنه يجب إليه المصير لأنه المفهوم من عباراتهم والمتبادر من كلماتهم، وقوله في الفتح فهذا إشارة إلى الحكم المذكور في مسألة الطاحون وقوله «كان من جملة الموقوف عليهم أي فيستحق الريع بالشرط لا بالعمل كاستحقاق الموقوف عليهم فإنه الباقي إلى أصل الغلة. ولو شرط المعلوم ولم يشرط له أن يجعل لغيره ليس له أن يوصي به ولا بشيء منه لأحد، ويجوز له أن يوصي بأمر الوقف وينقطع المعلوم عنه بموته، ولو وكل هذا القيم وكيلاً في الوقف أو أوصى به إلى رجل وجعل له كل المعلوم أو بعضه ثم جن جنوناً مطبقاً يبطل توكيله ووصايته وما جعل للوصي أو الوكيل من المال ويرجع الوقف إلا أن يكون الواقف عينه لجهة أخرى عند انقطاعه عن القيم فينفذ فيها حينئذ. وقدر الجنون المطبق بما يبقى حولاً لسقوط الفرائض كلها عنه، ولو عاد عقله عادت الولاية إليه لأنها زالت بعارض فإذا زال عاد إلى ما كان عليه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف
21. The Book of Waqf. [Text]... The apparent meaning is that it refers to stopping the known allowance during the time of reconstruction. As for entitlement when there is no work, there is no difference between one administrator and another. Some ignorant person has clung to the statement of Qadi Khan and assigned him a tenth of the produce on the basis that the judge may assign to the trustee a tenth of the yields without regard to the equivalent wage, and this is a mistake. He said in al-Qunyah: The judge removed him, and the trustee claimed that he had been given such-and-such monthly or yearly, and the removed one verified it; it is not accepted without evidence. Then, if what he specified is the equivalent of his work or less, the second gives it; otherwise, he deducts the excess and gives the remainder. End. So it is understood that the second judge deducts what exceeds the equivalent wage, indicating the invalidity of the judge's setting for the administrator more than the equivalent wage. If you say: if the waqf is hilali and the administrator has referred the beneficiaries to the shops and houses and they take from the residents, does the administrator deserve an allowance? I say: he does not deserve an allowance for the hilali because he does not work in it, except for reconstruction as we previously mentioned from Qadi Khan in the mill case. The trustee may appoint an agent, dismiss his agent, and give some of his allowance to the agent and take it away from him. If the waqif stipulated for the trustee the delegation of his affairs after his death like what he stipulated for him during his life, so the trustee gave some of his allowance to a man whom he appointed trustee, and remained silent about the remainder, then died, his executor has only what was named and it returns. His statement: (And he made for him a tenth of the produce) al-Ramli said: i.e., in return for his work in the waqf. His statement: (The apparent meaning is that it refers to stopping the allowance etc.) al-Ramli said: the definitive is contrary to this apparent meaning, because if it is interpreted that way, the meaning would be corrupted, as it would then imply that he stops when the waqif stipulates it, not otherwise, and this is corrupt, reflect. And I also say: how can this be said when he first stated: 'Do not delay reconstruction when needed, and stop the beneficiaries' shares for it if no obvious harm is feared; if harm is feared, give priority.' As for the administrator, if he has a stipulation from the waqif, he is like one of the beneficiaries; if they are stopped for reconstruction, he stops, unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage; if he does not work, he takes nothing. End. Then he transmitted the mill case afterwards without separation between the two statements, then followed it with his statement: 'This is our view for one for whom the waqif did not stipulate.' And you are aware that the trustee is stopped during reconstruction absolutely, whether the waqif stipulated for him or not, unless he works, then he takes the amount of his wage; and there is no mention of reconstruction in the mill case, so returning to it is not appropriate; rather, the appropriate view is the difference between one administrator and another. So it is settled that if the waqif specifies something for him, it is his, whether much or little, in accordance with what he stipulated, whether he works or not, as long as he did not stipulate it in return for work, as is understood from our statement 'in accordance with what he stipulated'. If the waqif did not specify for him and the judge specified his equivalent wage, it is permissible; if he specified more, the excess over the equivalent wage is prevented. This is if he works; if he does not work, he is not entitled to a wage. The same is stated in al-Ashbah in the Book of Claims. If the judge appointed him but did not specify anything for him, there is consideration: if the custom is that he does not work without his equivalent wage, then he gets his equivalent wage because custom is like a condition; otherwise, nothing. So take this insight, for it is necessary to adopt it, because it is the understanding from their expressions and the obvious meaning of their words. And his statement in al-Fath: 'This is an indication of the ruling mentioned in the mill case.' And his statement: 'He was among the beneficiaries' means he deserves the revenue by condition, not by work, like the entitlement of the beneficiaries, then the remainder goes back to the principal of the produce. If he stipulated the allowance and did not stipulate for him to give it to others, he may not bequeath it or any part of it to anyone. He may bequeath the management of the waqf, and the allowance is cut off by his death. If this trustee appointed an agent for the waqf or bequeathed it to a man and gave him all or part of the allowance, then became permanently insane, his agency and bequest are invalidated, and whatever money was given to the legatee or agent returns to the waqf, unless the waqif designated another purpose for it when it is cut off from the trustee, in which case it is executed then. The extent of permanent insanity is what lasts a year, due to all obligatory rights falling away. If his mind returns, his guardianship returns because it was removed by a temporary cause; when it is removed, it returns to what it was. So in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) expanding on the rulings of the trustee (nazir/qayyim) of a waqf regarding his compensation (ma'lum). The commentator first distinguishes between the trustee's allowance during reconstruction and his entitlement when not working. The key point is that if the waqif has stipulated a specific compensation, the trustee takes it regardless of whether he works, as long as the stipulation was not explicitly in return for work. If the judge sets the compensation, it must not exceed the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl). If the trustee does not work, he is not entitled to any compensation unless stipulated. The passage also covers the trustee's right to appoint an agent and allocate part of his compensation, the effect of insanity on his position, and the ruling when the waqif delegates authority. The commentator refutes a misunderstanding from some who relied on Qadi Khan's statement about a tenth of the produce, clarifying that it applies only when there is no stipulation by the waqif and the judge's setting must align with the equivalent wage.

Key Terms
معلوم (ma'lum): The fixed compensation or allowance assigned to the trustee (nazir/qayyim) of a waqf for his work.
ناظر (nazir): The administrator or supervisor of a waqf, also called qayyim or mutawalli.
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The customary or equivalent wage for similar work in the market, used as a benchmark when no specific compensation is stipulated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqif stipulates a specific monthly compensation for the administrator without linking it to work, and the administrator does not perform any work, what is the ruling?
A) The administrator takes nothing because he did not work.
B) The administrator takes the stipulated amount because the waqif's condition is binding.
C) The judge must deduct the amount because it exceeds the equivalent wage.
D) The administrator takes only half of the stipulation.

Key Takeaway
The waqif's condition regarding the administrator's compensation is binding; if the judge sets it, it must not exceed the equivalent wage, and work is required unless custom dictates otherwise.

Removal of a Treacherous Trustee and Invalidity of Contradictory Conditions
Explaining the ruling on removing a treacherous trustee and the invalidity of conditions that contradict Shariah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on removing a treacherous trustee from a waqf and identify which conditions of the waqif are invalid.

Core Idea
A waqif's condition preventing removal of a treacherous trustee is void; the judge must remove such a trustee.

In waqf administration, the judge's duty to protect the endowment sometimes overrides the founder's stipulations. This passage addresses a critical conflict: what happens when a waqif conditions that a trustee cannot be removed, even if the trustee proves treacherous? The commentator, drawing from earlier authorities, establishes that such a condition contradicts Shariah and is null. Understanding this ruling requires examining the proof, the scope of the waqif's authority, and the judge's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the ruling? The act is the removal of a treacherous trustee (kha'in) by the judge. The text states it is wajib (obligatory) upon the judge, based on al-Bazzaziyyah. Also note that a condition to prevent removal is void (batil).
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, due to it being established by a zanni dalil (qiyas and general principles).
2
Locate the Dalil
What proof supports this? The passage uses analogy (qiyas) to the executor (wasi): just as a treacherous executor is removed, so is a trustee. It also invokes the principle of protecting the waqf (nazaran lil-waqf).
The passage also implies that conditions contradicting Shariah are void by consensus.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The analogy is based on the common illa: both the waqf and the orphan's property are trusts that must be safeguarded from treachery. The condition collides with this objective, hence it is void.
The maxim 'shart al-waqif ka nass al-shari' is qualified: it applies only to valid conditions.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
What is the intra-Hanafi difference? Al-Khassaf holds that the judge may either remove the khain or add a co-trustee. The commentator reconciles by stating the goal is removing harm: if adding a co-trustee suffices, that is acceptable.
The mufta bihi position is removal, but the alternative is permitted if harm is eliminated.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The commentator favors the view that removal is wajib, citing al-Bazzaziyyah, but allows al-Khassaf's view as a practical alternative. The judge must act to protect the waqf.
This shows the practical flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وينزع لو كالوصي وإن شرط أن لا ينزع) أي ويعزل القاضي الواقف المتولي على وقفه لو كان خائناً كما يعزل الوصي الخائن نظراً للوقف واليتيم ولا اعتبار بشرط الواقف أن لا يعزله القاضي والسلطان لأنه شرط مخالف لحكم الشرع فبطل. واستفيد منه أن للقاضي عزل المتولي الخائن غير الواقف بالأولى. وصرح في البزازية أن عزل القاضي للخائن واجب عليه ومقتضاه الإثم بتركه والإثم بتولية الخائن ولا شك فيه. وفي المصباح وفرقوا بين الخائن والسارق والغاصب بأن الخائن هو الذي خان ما جعل عليه أميناً والسارق من أخذ خفية من موضع كان ممنوعاً من الوصول إليه، وربما قيل كل سارق خائن دون عكسه، والغاصب من جهاراً معتمداً على قوته .اهـ. وقدمنا أنه لا يعزله القاضي بمجرد الطعن في أمانته ولا يخرجه إلا بخيانة ظاهرة ببينة وأن له إدخال غيره معه إذا طعن في أمانته، وأنه إذا أخرجه ثم تاب وأناب أعاده، وأن امتناعه من التعمير خيانة. وكذا لو باع الوقف أو بعضه أو تصرف تصرفاً غير جائز عالماً به، وبيناه غاية البيان عند الكلام على نصب القاضي المتولي . وإنما الكلام الآن في شروط الواقفين فقد أفادوا هنا أنه ليس كل شرط يجب اتباعه فقالوا هنا : إن اشتراطه أن لا يعزله القاضي شرط باطل مخالف للشرع . وبهذا علم أن قولهم «شرط الواقف كنص الشارع» ليس على عمومه قال العلامة قاسم في فتاواه أجمعت الأمة أن من شروط الواقفين معتبر يعمل به ومنها ما ليس كذلك، ونص أبو عبد الله الدمشقي في كتاب هو صحيح الوقف عن شيخه شيخ الإسلام قول الفقهاء نصوصه كنص الشارع يعني في الفهم والدلالة في وجوب العمل مع أن التحقيق أن لفظه ولفظ الموصي والحالف والناذر وكل عاقد يحمل على عادته في خطابه ولغته التي يتكلم بها وافقت لغة العرب ولغة الشرع أم لا، ولا خلاف من وقف على صلاة أو صيام أو قراءة أو جهاد غير شرعي ونحوه لم يصح اهـ. قال ما لا أن أخذ بالشرط لا بالعمل وهذا هو المتعين في فهم عبارته والله تعالى أعلم . قوله : (ومقتضاه الإثم بتركه) مخالف لما قدمه في الموضع الثالث عن الخصاف أنه يخرجه أو يضم إليه آخر وقدمنا الجواب بأن المراد بعزله إزالة ضرره عن الوقف فإذا حصل ذلك بضم ثقة إليه حصل المقصود قوله : (وإن امتناعه من التعمير خيانة)
His statement (He is removed if treacherous like the executor, even if he stipulated that he not be removed) means: The judge removes the waqif who is trustee over his own waqf if he is treacherous, just as he removes a treacherous executor, out of consideration for the waqf and the orphan. The condition of the waqif that the judge and ruler not remove him is disregarded, because it is a condition contrary to the ruling of Shariah, so it is void. It is understood from this that the judge may remove a treacherous trustee who is not the waqif, a fortiori. It is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyyah that removal of a treacherous person by the judge is obligatory upon him; its consequence is sin if he leaves him, and sin in appointing a treacherous person, and there is no doubt about it. In al-Misbah, they distinguished between the treacherous person (kha'in), the thief (sariq), and the usurper (ghasib): the kha'in is one who betrays what was entrusted to him; the sariq is one who takes secretly from a place he was prevented from accessing; it is sometimes said that every thief is a traitor but not vice versa; the ghasib is one who takes openly relying on his power. End. And we previously stated that the judge does not remove him merely by accusation against his trustworthiness, nor does he remove him except for apparent treachery with evidence, and that he may bring in someone else with him if his trustworthiness is questioned, and that if he removes him and then he repents and reforms, he returns him, and that his refusal to reconstruct is treachery. Likewise if he sells the waqf or part of it or acts in an impermissible manner knowingly, and we explained it thoroughly when discussing the judge's appointment of a trustee. Now the discussion is about the conditions of waqifs: they have indicated here that not every condition must be followed. They said here: the stipulation that the judge not remove him is a void condition contrary to Shariah. By this it is known that their statement 'The condition of the waqif is like the text of the Lawgiver' is not general. 'Allamah Qasim said in his Fatawa: The ummah is agreed that some conditions of the waqif are considered and acted upon, and some are not. Abu Abdullah al-Dimashqi wrote in his book 'Sahih al-Waqf' from his teacher Shaykh al-Islam that the statement of the jurists 'His texts are like the text of the Lawgiver' means in terms of understanding and indication regarding the obligation of acting upon them, but the verification is that his wording and the wording of the testator, the one who swears, the one who vows, and every contractor is interpreted according to his custom and language, whether it agrees with the language of the Arabs and the language of the law or not. There is no disagreement that a waqf for un-Islamic prayer, fasting, recitation, or jihad, etc., is not valid. End. He said: 'Because taking by the condition, not by work' and this is the definitive in understanding his statement, and Allah knows best. His statement (And its consequence is sin if he leaves him) contradicts what he previously mentioned in the third place from al-Khassaf that he removes him or joins another to him. And we previously answered that the meaning of his removal is removing his harm from the waqf; if that is achieved by joining a trustworthy person with him, the purpose is achieved. His statement (And that his refusal to reconstruct is treachery.)
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the rules regarding the waqf trustee. The commentator explains the ruling that a trustee who is treacherous (kha'in) must be removed by the judge, even if the waqif stipulated that he should not be removed. Such a condition is void because it contradicts Shariah, which requires protecting the waqf from harm. The judge's duty to remove a treacherous trustee is obligatory (wajib), and failing to do so incurs sin. The passage then distinguishes between a treacherous person (kha'in), a thief (sariq), and a usurper (ghasib): the kha'in betrays a trust, the sariq takes secretly from a protected place, and the ghasib takes openly by force. The commentator also emphasizes that removal requires clear evidence of treachery, not mere suspicion. The second part addresses the general principle that not all conditions set by the waqif are binding; those that contradict Shariah are void. The famous maxim 'The condition of the waqif is like the text of the Lawgiver' is not absolute; it applies only to valid conditions. Examples include a condition that the judge cannot remove a treacherous trustee or a waqf for un-Islamic acts. The commentator reconciles differing views from al-Khassaf by explaining that the goal is to eliminate harm, which can also be achieved by adding a trustworthy co-trustee.

Key Terms
خائن (kha'in): A trustee who betrays the trust placed in him regarding the waqf, such as by mismanagement, theft, or refusal to reconstruct.
شرط الواقف (shart al-waqif): A condition stipulated by the founder of a waqf regarding its administration, beneficiaries, or other matters.
عزل (azl): Removal of a trustee or administrator by the judge, typically for treachery or incompetence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqif stipulates that the trustee cannot be removed even if he is treacherous, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The condition is valid and must be followed.
B) The condition is void, and the judge must remove the trustee if treachery is proven.
C) The condition is valid only if the trustee is a relative.
D) The judge can remove the trustee only if the waqif agrees.

Key Takeaway
A waqif's condition that contradicts Shariah, such as preventing removal of a treacherous trustee, is void; the judge must remove such a trustee to protect the waqf.

Removal of the Dishonest Waqf Trustee Despite the Waquif's Condition
Ruling on the qadi's authority to remove a dishonest trustee even if the waqif stipulated otherwise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on removing a treacherous waqf trustee and explain why the waqif's condition to the contrary is void.

Core Idea
Conditions contrary to shari'ah are void; the qadi must remove a treacherous trustee to protect the waqf.

Waqf trustees are entrusted with managing charitable endowments. What happens when a trustee proves treacherous? Does the waqif's stipulation that the trustee cannot be removed bind the qadi? The Hanafi school addresses this through a clear ruling grounded in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The matn states: 'He (the qadi) removes (the trustee) if he is treacherous, like the executor, even if he (the waqif) stipulated that he should not be removed.' Pin down the act (removal) and its ruling (obligatory).
2
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The qiyas compares the waqf trustee to an executor (wasi). Both are trustees. If a treacherous executor is removed to protect the orphan, the same applies to a waqf trustee to protect the endowment.
Common illa: protection of the beneficiary from harm.
3
Analyze the waqif's condition
The condition 'not to remove' contradicts the shari'ah goal of preventing harm. Hence it is void. The qadi's obligation overrides the condition.
Hanafi principle: conditions opposing shari'ah are invalid.
4
Note the legal definitions
The passage distinguishes kha'in (treacherous) from sariq (thief) and ghasib (usurper). This is important for proving treachery.
Treachery requires a breach of trust; mere accusation is insufficient.

Source Text

وينزع لو خائناً كالوصي وإن شرط أن لا ينزع .
إلى غلة
خائناً
الباقي إلى أصل الغلة. ولو شرط المعلوم ولم يشرط له أن يجعل لغيره ليس له أن يوصي به ولا بشيء منه لأحد، ويجوز له أن يوصي بأمر الوقف وينقطع المعلوم عنه بموته، ولو وكل هذا القيم وكيلاً في الوقف أو أوصى به إلى رجل وجعل له كل المعلوم أو بعضه ثم جن جنوناً مطبقاً يبطل توكيله ووصايته وما جعل للوصي أو الوكيل من المال ويرجع الوقف إلا أن يكون الواقف عينه لجهة أخرى عند انقطاعه عن القيم فينفذ فيها حينئذ. وقدر الجنون المطبق بما يبقى حولاً لسقوط الفرائض كلها عنه، ولو عاد عقله عادت الولاية إليه لأنها زالت بعارض فإذا زال عاد إلى ما كان عليه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف قوله : (وينزع لو كالوصي وإن شرط أن لا ينزع أي ويعزل القاضي الواقف المتولي على وقفه لو كان خائناً كما يعزل الوصي الخائن نظراً للوقف واليتيم ولا اعتبار بشرط الواقف أن لا يعزله القاضي والسلطان لأنه شرط مخالف لحكم الشرع فبطل. واستفيد منه أن للقاضي عزل المتولي الخائن غير الواقف بالأولى. وصرح في البزازية أن عزل القاضي للخائن واجب عليه ومقتضاه الإثم بتركه والإثم بتولية الخائن ولا شك فيه. وفي المصباح وفرقوا بين الخائن والسارق والغاصب بأن الخائن هو الذي خان ما جعل عليه أميناً والسارق من أخذ خفية من موضع كان ممنوعاً من الوصول إليه، وربما قيل كل سارق خائن دون عكسه، والغاصب من جهاراً معتمداً على قوته .اهـ. وقدمنا أنه لا يعزله القاضي بمجرد الطعن في أمانته ولا يخرجه إلا بخيانة ظاهرة ببينة وأن له إدخال غيره معه إذا طعن في أمانته، وأنه إذا أخرجه ثم تاب وأناب أعاده، وأن امتناعه من التعمير خيانة. وكذا لو باع الوقف أو بعضه أو تصرف تصرفاً غير جائز عالماً به، وبيناه غاية البيان عند الكلام على نصب القاضي المتولي .
The Book of Waqf. He (the qadi) removes if (the trustee) is treacherous like the executor, even if he (the waqif) stipulated that he should not be removed. ... (the commentary explains: that the qadi removes the waqif-trustee if he is treacherous, as he removes the treacherous executor, considering the waqf and the orphan, and no attention is paid to the waqif's condition that the qadi and the sultan should not remove him, because it is a condition contrary to the ruling of shari'ah, so it is void. From this it is understood that the qadi has the right to remove a treacherous trustee who is not the waqif a fortiori. It is stated in al-Bazzaziyyah that the qadi's removal of the treacherous person is obligatory upon him, and its consequence is sin if he leaves it, and sin in appointing a treacherous person, and there is no doubt in it. In al-Misbah, they distinguished between the treacherous (kha'in), the thief (sariq), and the usurper (ghasib): the treacherous is one who betrayed what he was made an trustee over; the thief is one who takes secretly from a place he was prevented from reaching; and sometimes it is said every thief is treacherous but not vice versa; the usurper is one who takes openly relying on his strength. ...)
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the ruling that the qadi has the authority to remove a trustee of a waqf who proves to be dishonest, even if the founder of the waqf stipulated that the trustee should never be removed. The author begins by stating the ruling from the matn: 'He (the qadi) removes (the trustee) if he is treacherous, like the executor, even if he (the waqif) stipulated that he should not be removed.' The commentary expands on this: the qadi removes the waqif-trustee if he is treacherous, just as he removes a treacherous executor, because the condition violates the shari'ah principle that harm must be removed. The commentator notes that this ruling applies a fortiori to a trustee who is not the waqif. He cites al-Bazzaziyyah that it is obligatory for the qadi to remove a treacherous trustee, and he sins if he fails to do so or if he appoints someone treacherous. The passage also provides a legal distinction between a treacherous person (kha'in), a thief (sariq), and a usurper (ghasib): the kha'in betrays a trust, the sariq takes secretly from a protected place, and the ghasib takes openly by force. The commentator clarifies that the qadi does not remove a trustee based on mere accusation; there must be clear proof of treachery. If a trusted person is suspected, the qadi may appoint another alongside him. If the trustee repents and reforms, he may be reinstated. Refusal to maintain the property is considered treachery. Also, selling the waqf property knowingly or any invalid disposition is treachery. The author references earlier discussion on the appointment of the qadi as trustee.

Key Terms
خائن (khā'in): One who betrays the trust placed in him as a trustee of the waqf.
متولي (mutawallī): The trustee or administrator of a waqf appointed by the waqif or qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a qadi who fails to remove a treacherous trustee of a waqf?
A) He is not sinful because he follows the waqif's condition.
B) He is sinful because it is wajib upon him to remove the treacherous trustee.
C) He is sinful only if the waqif did not stipulate otherwise.
D) He is not sinful if he appoints someone else alongside the trustee.

Key Takeaway
The qadi must remove a treacherous waqf trustee even if the waqif stipulated otherwise, because protecting the waqf from harm overrides void conditions.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
The Principle 'Shart al-Waqif Ka-Nass al-Shari'' and Its Core Limitation
Ruling statement on the invalidity of conditions conflicting with shari'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the waqif's condition is like a legislative text and identify its core limitation: conditions violating shari'ah are invalid.

Core Idea
The waqif's condition is binding like a text, but only if it does not contradict shari'ah.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the widely-quoted maxim 'shart al-waqif ka-nass al-shari'' is not absolute. While conditions are generally to be followed, the text gives a clear example: a condition that the qadi cannot remove the trustee is invalid because it contradicts the qadi's authority. We will explore the basis of this limitation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its apparent meaning
The phrase 'شرط الواقف كنص الشارع' suggests full obligation to follow the condition.
This maxim is often invoked to justify enforcing all conditions.
2
Find the counter-example in the text
The condition that the qadi not remove the trustee is ruled invalid, showing the maxim is not absolute.
The qadi's authority to oversee the waqf is a shar'i right.
3
Understand the reason for the invalidity
The condition contradicts a shar'i principle: the qadi must be able to remove an unfit trustee.
This is based on the necessity of protecting the waqf.
4
State the conclusion
The maxim is qualified: conditions are valid only if they comply with shari'ah.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما الكلام الآن في شروط الواقفين فقد أفادوا هنا أنه ليس كل شرط يجب اتباعه فقالوا هنا : إن اشتراطه أن لا يعزله القاضي شرط باطل مخالف للشرع . وبهذا علم أن قولهم «شرط الواقف كنص الشارع» ليس على عمومه قال العلامة قاسم في فتاواه أجمعت الأمة أن من شروط الواقفين معتبر يعمل به ومنها ما ليس كذلك، ونص أبو عبد الله الدمشقي في كتاب هو صحيح الوقف عن شيخه شيخ الإسلام قول الفقهاء نصوصه كنص الشارع يعني في الفهم والدلالة في وجوب العمل مع أن التحقيق أن لفظه ولفظ الموصي والحالف والناذر وكل عاقد يحمل على عادته في خطابه ولغته التي يتكلم بها وافقت لغة العرب ولغة الشرع أم لا، ولا خلاف من وقف على صلاة أو صيام أو قراءة أو جهاد غير شرعي ونحوه لم يصح اهـ. قال

العلامة
قاسم : قلت : وإذا كان المعنى ما ذكر فما كان من عبارة الواقف من قبيل المفسر لا يحتمل تخصيصاً ولا تأويلاً يعمل به وما كان من قبيل الظاهر كذلك، وما احتمل وفيه قرينة حمل عليها، وما كان مشتركاً لا يعمل به لأنه لا عموم له عندنا ولم يقع فيه نظر المجتهد لترجح أحد مدلوليه، وكذلك ما كان من قبيل المجمل إذا مات الواقف، وإن كان حياً يرجع إلى بيانه. هذا معنى ما أفاده .اهـ. قلت فعلى هذا إذا ترك صاحب الوظيفة مباشرتها في بعض الأوقات المشروط عليه فيها العمل لا يأثم عند الله تعالى غايته أنه لا يستحق المعلوم. ومن الشروط المعتبرة ما صرح به الخصاف لو شرط أن لا يؤجر المتولي الأرض فإن إجارتها باطلة، وكذا اشتراط أن لا يعامل على ما فيها من نخل وأشجار، وكذا إذا شرط أن المتولي إذا أجرها فهو خارج عن التولية، فإذا خالف المتولي صار خارجاً ويوليها القاضي من يثق بأمانته، وكذا إذا شرط أنه إن أحدث أحد من أهل هذا الوقف حدثاً في الوقف يريد إبطاله كان خارجاً اعتبر، فإن نازع البعض وقال أردت تصحيح الوقف وقال سائر أهل الوقف إنما أردت إبطاله نظر القاضي في القوم الذين تنازعوا فإن كانوا يريدون تصحيحه فلهم ذلك، وإن كانوا
قال الرملي : إذا كان هناك ما يعمر به من مال الوقف وخيف ضرر بين بتأخير العمارة كما تقدم بيانه . قوله : (قلت فعلى هذا الخ) قال في النهر بعد نقله كلام العلامة قاسم : وأراد بشيخ الإسلام تقي الدين بن تيمية الحنبلي فإنه في موضع آخر عزا هذا إلى أبي عبد الله الدمشقي عن شيخه شيخ الإسلام وأبو عبد الله بن مفلح وشيخه هو ابن تيمية. وهذا كما ترى لا يلزم أن يكون رأياً للحنفية وأي مانع من أنه كنص الشارع في وجوب العمل به، فإذا شرط عليه أداء خدمة كقراءة أو تدريس وجب عليه إما العمل أو الترك لمن يعمل حتى لو لم يعمل أو لم يترك ينبغي أن لا يتردد في إثمه ولا سيما إن كانت الخدمة مما يلزم بتعطيلها ترك شعيرة من شعائر الإسلام كالأذان ونحوه فتدبره .اهـ. وقال الرملي قال هذا الشارح في فتاواه : ويصح أن يكون التشبيه في وجوب العمل أيضاً من جهة أن الصرف في الوقف على اتباع شرطه لأنه إنما أوصى بملكه فهذه الشروط لا بد من مراعاتها . وذكر الشارح في كتاب القضاء عند الكلام على قوله «وإذا رفع إليه حكم قاض أمضاه الخ نقلاً عن الأشباه والنظائر للأسيوطي معزياً إلى فتاوى السبكي أن قضاء القاضي ينقض عند الحنفية إذا كان حكماً لا دليل عليه . قال : وما خالف شرط الواقف فهو مخالف للنص وهو حكم لا دليل عليه، سواء كان نصه في الوقف نصاً أو ظاهراً .اهـ. قال هذا الشارح : وهذا موافق لقول مشايخنا كغيرهم شرط الواقف كنص الشارع فيحب اتباعه كما في شرح المجمع للمصنف اهـ. فهذا يؤيد قوله ويصح أن يكون التشبيه في وجوب العمل أيضاً تأمل والله تعالى أعلم اهـ . قلت : استثنى المؤلف في أشباهه من هذا الأصل مسائل : الأولى شرط أن القاضي لا يعزل الناظر فله عزل غير الأهل . الثانية شرط أن لا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة والناس لا يرغبون في استئجاره سنة أو كان في الزيادة نفع للفقراء فللقاضي المخالفة دون الناظر الثالثة لو شرط أن يقرأ على قبره فالتعيين باطل . الرابعة شرط أن يتصدق بفاضل الغلة على من يسأل في مسجد كذا كل يوم لم يراع شرطه وللقيم التصدق على
Now the discussion is about the conditions of the waqifs. They have indicated here that not every condition must be followed. They said: his stipulation that the qadi should not remove him is an invalid condition contrary to shari'ah. By this it is known that their saying 'the condition of the waqif is like the text of the Lawgiver' is not absolute. Al-Allama Qasim said in his Fatawa: The ummah is agreed that among the conditions of the waqifs some are considered and acted upon, and some are not. Abu Abdullah al-Dimashqi stated in his book Sahih al-Waqf from his teacher Shaykh al-Islam: The saying of the jurists 'his texts are like the text of the Lawgiver' means in understanding and indication regarding the obligation of acting upon it, while the verification is that his wording and the wording of the testator, the oath-taker, the vow-maker, and every contractor is interpreted according to his custom in speech and his language, whether it agrees with the language of the Arabs and the language of the shari'ah or not. There is no disagreement that if someone endows upon an un-Islamic prayer, fasting, recitation, or jihad and the like, it is not valid. ... He said: The author in his Ashbah excepted from this principle several issues: first, the condition that the qadi should not remove the overseer, so he (the qadi) may remove an unqualified person; second, the condition that the waqf should not be leased for more than a year, but if people are unwilling to lease it for a year or there is benefit for the poor in a longer term, the qadi may violate this condition, not the overseer; third, if he stipulated that one should recite over his grave, the specification is void; fourth, the condition that the surplus of the revenue should be given to whoever asks in a certain masjid every day, his condition is not observed, and the trustee may give to...
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the scope and limitations of the principle that 'the condition of the waqif is like a legislative text.' The author begins by stating that the previous ruling (that the qadi can remove a trustee despite a condition to the contrary) shows that not every condition must be followed. The condition that the qadi should not remove the trustee is invalid because it contradicts shari'ah. Al-Allama Qasim in his Fatawa explains that while conditions are generally to be observed, some are not. He quotes Abu Abdullah al-Dimashqi that the phrase 'like the text of the Lawgiver' is about understanding and obligation, but in reality, the waqif's words are interpreted according to his custom, not necessarily according to Arabic or shari'ah. Un-Islamic conditions are automatically void. The commentator then discusses the interpretation of ambiguous terms: clear (mufassar) terms are acted upon, apparent (zahir) terms are similar, terms with a contextual clue (qarinah) are interpreted accordingly, ambiguous (mushtarak) terms are not acted upon due to lack of generality, and ambivalent (mujmal) terms require the waqif's explanation while he lives, but after death they cannot be acted upon. The passage then gives examples of valid conditions from al-Khassaf: the condition that the trustee should not lease the land (such a lease is void), or that if he does, he is removed. The qadi enforces these conditions. The passage also discusses the situation where the waqif conditions a service like teaching or recitation; the beneficiary must perform it or delegate it. If he fails, he sins, especially if the service is a public rite like the adhan. The author concludes by citing exceptions from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair where the principle is overridden, such as conditions that harm the beneficiaries or violate shari'ah.

Key Terms
شرط الواقف كنص الشارع (shart al-wāqif ka-naṣṣ al-shāri‘): A maxim meaning the waqif's condition is treated like a legislative text in terms of obligation to follow, but with limitations.
مفسر (mufassar): Clear and unambiguous text that requires no interpretation.
ظاهر (zāhir): Apparent meaning, but subject to possible specification (takhsis) if there is evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a condition that the qadi should not remove the trustee?
A) It is valid and must be followed.
B) It is invalid because it contradicts shari'ah.
C) It is valid only if the trustee is qualified.
D) It is invalid only if the trustee is dishonest.

Key Takeaway
The waqif's condition is binding only when it complies with shari'ah; conditions that conflict with shari'ah are void.

Waqf — Endowment

Interpreting the Waif's Words: Textual Categories
Expansion on the interpretation of waqif's wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify waqif's statements as mufassar, zahir, mushtarak, or mujmal and determine whether they are enforceable.

Core Idea
The waqif's words are interpreted by his custom, not by absolute linguistic rules.

In the previous lesson we learned that conditions are subject to shari'ah compatibility. Now we delve into how to interpret the waqif's actual phrasing. The text from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that the waqif's intention is key, and his words are categorized by clarity: mufassar (clear) is binding, zahir (apparent) is similar, mushtarak (ambiguous) is not acted upon, and mujmal (ambivalent) requires explanation from the waqif if he is alive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif's statement type
Determine if the wording is mufassar (unambiguous), zahir (clear but open to specification), mushtarak (homonym), or mujmal (ambivalent).
This classification comes from Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
2
Apply the rule for each type
Mufassar and zahir are acted upon. Mushtarak is not acted upon because it has no general applicability (la ‘umūm lahu). Mujmal requires the waqif's clarification while alive; after death it is ignored.
The text emphasizes that the waqif's custom (urf) governs interpretation.
3
Consider the context (qarina)
If the wording has a possible meaning and there is a contextual clue (qarina), the interpretation follows the clue.
Example: 'my family' might mean his immediate kin if that is his custom.
4
State the enforceability
Only mufassar and zahir statements are enforceable. Ambiguous statements are void.
This protects the waqf from uncertain conditions.

Source Text

كتاب الوقف
العلامة
قاسم : قلت : وإذا كان المعنى ما ذكر فما كان من عبارة الواقف من قبيل المفسر لا يحتمل تخصيصاً ولا تأويلاً يعمل به وما كان من قبيل الظاهر كذلك، وما احتمل وفيه قرينة حمل عليها، وما كان مشتركاً لا يعمل به لأنه لا عموم له عندنا ولم يقع فيه نظر المجتهد لترجح أحد مدلوليه، وكذلك ما كان من قبيل المجمل إذا مات الواقف، وإن كان حياً يرجع إلى بيانه. هذا معنى ما أفاده .اهـ. قلت فعلى هذا إذا ترك صاحب الوظيفة مباشرتها في بعض الأوقات المشروط عليه فيها العمل لا يأثم عند الله تعالى غايته أنه لا يستحق المعلوم. ومن الشروط المعتبرة ما صرح به الخصاف لو شرط أن لا يؤجر المتولي الأرض فإن إجارتها باطلة، وكذا اشتراط أن لا يعامل على ما فيها من نخل وأشجار، وكذا إذا شرط أن المتولي إذا أجرها فهو خارج عن التولية، فإذا خالف المتولي صار خارجاً ويوليها القاضي من يثق بأمانته، وكذا إذا شرط أنه إن أحدث أحد من أهل هذا الوقف حدثاً في الوقف يريد إبطاله كان خارجاً اعتبر، فإن نازع البعض وقال أردت تصحيح الوقف وقال سائر أهل الوقف إنما أردت إبطاله نظر القاضي في القوم الذين تنازعوا فإن كانوا يريدون تصحيحه فلهم ذلك، وإن كانوا
قال الرملي : إذا كان هناك ما يعمر به من مال الوقف وخيف ضرر بين بتأخير العمارة كما تقدم بيانه . قوله : (قلت فعلى هذا الخ) قال في النهر بعد نقله كلام العلامة قاسم : وأراد بشيخ الإسلام تقي الدين بن تيمية الحنبلي فإنه في موضع آخر عزا هذا إلى أبي عبد الله الدمشقي عن شيخه شيخ الإسلام وأبو عبد الله بن مفلح وشيخه هو ابن تيمية. وهذا كما ترى لا يلزم أن يكون رأياً للحنفية وأي مانع من أنه كنص الشارع في وجوب العمل به، فإذا شرط عليه أداء خدمة كقراءة أو تدريس وجب عليه إما العمل أو الترك لمن يعمل حتى لو لم يعمل أو لم يترك ينبغي أن لا يتردد في إثمه ولا سيما إن كانت الخدمة مما يلزم بتعطيلها ترك شعيرة من شعائر الإسلام كالأذان ونحوه فتدبره .اهـ. وقال الرملي قال هذا الشارح في فتاواه : ويصح أن يكون التشبيه في وجوب العمل أيضاً من جهة أن الصرف في الوقف على اتباع شرطه لأنه إنما أوصى بملكه فهذه الشروط لا بد من مراعاتها . وذكر الشارح في كتاب القضاء عند الكلام على قوله «وإذا رفع إليه حكم قاض أمضاه الخ نقلاً عن الأشباه والنظائر للأسيوطي معزياً إلى فتاوى السبكي أن قضاء القاضي ينقض عند الحنفية إذا كان حكماً لا دليل عليه . قال : وما خالف شرط الواقف فهو مخالف للنص وهو حكم لا دليل عليه، سواء كان نصه في الوقف نصاً أو ظاهراً .اهـ. قال هذا الشارح : وهذا موافق لقول مشايخنا كغيرهم شرط الواقف كنص الشارع فيحب اتباعه كما في شرح المجمع للمصنف اهـ. فهذا يؤيد قوله ويصح أن يكون التشبيه في وجوب العمل أيضاً تأمل والله تعالى أعلم اهـ . قلت : استثنى المؤلف في أشباهه من هذا الأصل مسائل : الأولى شرط أن القاضي لا يعزل الناظر فله عزل غير الأهل . الثانية شرط أن لا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة والناس لا يرغبون في استئجاره سنة أو كان في الزيادة نفع للفقراء فللقاضي المخالفة دون الناظر الثالثة لو شرط أن يقرأ على قبره فالتعيين باطل . الرابعة شرط أن يتصدق بفاضل الغلة على من يسأل في مسجد كذا كل يوم لم يراع شرطه وللقيم التصدق على
Now the discussion is about the conditions of the waqifs. They have indicated here that not every condition must be followed. They said: his stipulation that the qadi should not remove him is an invalid condition contrary to shari'ah. By this it is known that their saying 'the condition of the waqif is like the text of the Lawgiver' is not absolute. Al-Allama Qasim said in his Fatawa: The ummah is agreed that among the conditions of the waqifs some are considered and acted upon, and some are not. Abu Abdullah al-Dimashqi stated in his book Sahih al-Waqf from his teacher Shaykh al-Islam: The saying of the jurists 'his texts are like the text of the Lawgiver' means in understanding and indication regarding the obligation of acting upon it, while the verification is that his wording and the wording of the testator, the oath-taker, the vow-maker, and every contractor is interpreted according to his custom in speech and his language, whether it agrees with the language of the Arabs and the language of the shari'ah or not. There is no disagreement that if someone endows upon an un-Islamic prayer, fasting, recitation, or jihad and the like, it is not valid. ... He said: The author in his Ashbah excepted from this principle several issues: first, the condition that the qadi should not remove the overseer, so he (the qadi) may remove an unqualified person; second, the condition that the waqf should not be leased for more than a year, but if people are unwilling to lease it for a year or there is benefit for the poor in a longer term, the qadi may violate this condition, not the overseer; third, if he stipulated that one should recite over his grave, the specification is void; fourth, the condition that the surplus of the revenue should be given to whoever asks in a certain masjid every day, his condition is not observed, and the trustee may give to...
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the scope and limitations of the principle that 'the condition of the waqif is like a legislative text.' The author begins by stating that the previous ruling (that the qadi can remove a trustee despite a condition to the contrary) shows that not every condition must be followed. The condition that the qadi should not remove the trustee is invalid because it contradicts shari'ah. Al-Allama Qasim in his Fatawa explains that while conditions are generally to be observed, some are not. He quotes Abu Abdullah al-Dimashqi that the phrase 'like the text of the Lawgiver' is about understanding and obligation, but in reality, the waqif's words are interpreted according to his custom, not necessarily according to Arabic or shari'ah. Un-Islamic conditions are automatically void. The commentator then discusses the interpretation of ambiguous terms: clear (mufassar) terms are acted upon, apparent (zahir) terms are similar, terms with a contextual clue (qarinah) are interpreted accordingly, ambiguous (mushtarak) terms are not acted upon due to lack of generality, and ambivalent (mujmal) terms require the waqif's explanation while he lives, but after death they cannot be acted upon. The passage then gives examples of valid conditions from al-Khassaf: the condition that the trustee should not lease the land (such a lease is void), or that if he does, he is removed. The qadi enforces these conditions. The passage also discusses the situation where the waqif conditions a service like teaching or recitation; the beneficiary must perform it or delegate it. If he fails, he sins, especially if the service is a public rite like the adhan. The author concludes by citing exceptions from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair where the principle is overridden, such as conditions that harm the beneficiaries or violate shari'ah.

Key Terms
مفسر (mufassar): Clear and unambiguous text that requires no interpretation.
ظاهر (zāhir): Apparent meaning, but subject to possible specification (takhsis) if there is evidence.
مشترك (mushtarak): A word with multiple possible meanings with no preference.
مُجْمَل (mujmal): An ambivalent word that requires clarification from the speaker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a condition that is mushtarak (ambiguous) after the waqif's death?
A) The qadi selects the most likely meaning.
B) The condition is void and not acted upon.
C) The condition is valid but interpreted literally.
D) The condition is referred to the beneficiaries.

Key Takeaway
Only clear (mufassar) and apparent (zahir) conditions are enforceable; ambiguous ones are void.

Exceptions to the Maxim: Cases Where the Qadi Overrides Conditions
Listing of exceptions to the principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four specific exceptions where the qadi may override the waqif's condition and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The waqif's condition is not absolute: the qadi may violate it when it harms the waqf or its beneficiaries.

The passage concludes with a list of exceptions from the work 'Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair' where the principle 'shart al-waqif ka-nass al-shari'' is set aside. These cases involve conditions that would cause harm to the waqf or its beneficiaries, allowing the qadi to intervene. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for anyone managing or judging waqf cases.

Guided Path
1
List the four exceptions
Identify each of the four scenarios: 1) condition that qadi not remove trustee; 2) condition limiting lease to one year; 3) condition to recite over grave; 4) condition to give surplus to daily askers.
These are from the text's final paragraph.
2
Understand the harm each exception prevents
In each case, enforcing the condition would harm the waqf's sustainability or violate shari'ah.
The common thread is public interest (maslahah).
3
Identify who may override
In some cases the qadi overrides; in others the trustee or qadi may act.
E.g., the qadi may violate the lease condition, but the trustee cannot.
4
Apply the ratio to new cases
The underlying reason (illah) is preventing harm; apply to similar situations.
If a condition would greatly harm beneficiaries, it is likely void.

وإنما الكلام الآن في شروط الواقفين فقد أفادوا هنا أنه ليس كل شرط يجب اتباعه فقالوا هنا : إن اشتراطه أن لا يعزله القاضي شرط باطل مخالف للشرع . وبهذا علم أن قولهم «شرط الواقف كنص الشارع» ليس على عمومه قال العلامة قاسم في فتاواه أجمعت الأمة أن من شروط الواقفين معتبر يعمل به ومنها ما ليس كذلك، ونص أبو عبد الله الدمشقي في كتاب هو صحيح الوقف عن شيخه شيخ الإسلام قول الفقهاء نصوصه كنص الشارع يعني في الفهم والدلالة في وجوب العمل مع أن التحقيق أن لفظه ولفظ الموصي والحالف والناذر وكل عاقد يحمل على عادته في خطابه ولغته التي يتكلم بها وافقت لغة العرب ولغة الشرع أم لا، ولا خلاف من وقف على صلاة أو صيام أو قراءة أو جهاد غير شرعي ونحوه لم يصح اهـ. قال

Interpreting Waqf Conditions: Mufassar, Zahir, and Mujmal
Interpreting waqf conditions linguistically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a waqf condition into mufassar, zahir, mushtarak, or mujmal and apply the corresponding Hanafi ruling on enforceability and compensation.

Core Idea
A waqf condition's enforceability depends on its linguistic clarity: clear terms bind, ambiguous ones do not, and missing work forfeits payment but not sin.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how to interpret conditions set by a waqf founder. It categorises the waqif's wording by linguistic clarity and shows that the legal effect varies: explicit or apparent conditions are binding, while ambiguous ones are not. Importantly, the passage clarifies that failing to perform stipulated work is not sinful, only affecting entitlement to compensation. This distinction prevents conflating contractual conditions with religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif's condition and its wording
Read the stipulation carefully. Note the specific phrase used by the endower regarding the duties of the position.
For example, 'the teacher must teach every day' or 'the imam should lead prayers when possible'.
2
Classify the wording using Hanafi linguistic categories
Determine if the wording is mufassar (explicit, unambiguous), zahir (apparent but may admit interpretation), mushtarak (ambiguous with multiple meanings), or mujmal (summary, needing clarification). Use Hanafi usul criteria.
Mushtarak has no 'umum in Hanafi usul; mujmal cannot be specified after the waqif's death.
3
Apply the ruling: binding for compensation, not for sin
If the wording is mufassar or zahir, the condition is enforceable in the sense that the holder must perform to receive the stipend, but failure is not a sin. If mushtarak or mujmal (with waqif dead), the condition is not acted upon.
The ruling hinges on the condition being mu'awwad (compensatory) rather than ta'abbudi (worship-related).
4
Determine the consequence for the appointed person
When the holder fails to perform at the stipulated time, does he sin? No. Does he lose the stipend for that time? Yes, if the condition was enforceable.
This follows from the principle that the condition is a condition for entitlement, not a religious duty.

Source Text

قاسم : قلت : وإذا كان المعنى ما ذكر فما كان من عبارة الواقف من قبيل المفسر لا يحتمل تخصيصاً ولا تأويلاً يعمل به وما كان من قبيل الظاهر كذلك، وما احتمل وفيه قرينة حمل عليها، وما كان مشتركاً لا يعمل به لأنه لا عموم له عندنا ولم يقع فيه نظر المجتهد لترجح أحد مدلوليه، وكذلك ما كان من قبيل المجمل إذا مات الواقف، وإن كان حياً يرجع إلى بيانه. هذا معنى ما أفاده .اهـ. قلت فعلى هذا إذا ترك صاحب الوظيفة مباشرتها في بعض الأوقات المشروط عليه فيها العمل لا يأثم عند الله تعالى غايته أنه لا يستحق المعلوم.
Qasim said: I say: If the meaning is as mentioned, then whatever of the waqif's expression is of the type of mufassar (explicit), it does not admit of specification or interpretation, and it is acted upon. Whatever is of the type of zahir (apparent) is likewise. Whatever is probable and has a contextual indication, it is interpreted accordingly. Whatever is mushtarak (ambiguous) is not acted upon because it has no generality in our view, and the ijtihad of the mujtahid did not occur to give preponderance to one of its meanings. Likewise, whatever is of the type of mujmal (summary), if the waqif has died, [it is not acted upon]; if he is alive, reference is made to his explanation. This is the meaning of what he conveyed—end. I say: On this basis, if the holder of a position fails to perform it at some times when work is stipulated for him, he does not sin before Allah Almighty; at most, he does not deserve the stipend.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how to interpret conditions set by the waqif (endower) in a waqf deed. The author, quoting 'Allamah Qasim, categorizes the waqif's wording into linguistic types: mufassar (explicit, unambiguous), zahir (apparent, but may admit interpretation), mushtarak (ambiguous, having multiple meanings), and mujmal (summary, needing clarification). Hanafi usul holds that mufassar and zahir wordings are binding and must be followed; mushtarak is not enforced because it lacks 'umum (generality) and no preponderance can be given without further evidence. Mujmal is not enforceable after the waqif's death, but if he is alive, he may clarify. The author then applies this: if a person is appointed to a position (e.g., teacher, reader) and is required to work at specific times, but fails to show up sometimes, he does not commit a sin because the condition is not absolutely binding (it is only a condition for entitlement to payment), but he does forfeit his stipend for that time. This shows that waqf conditions are often interpreted as conditions for compensation rather than obligations enforceable in the hereafter.

Key Terms
المفسر (al-mufassar): A clear, unambiguous expression that cannot be specified or interpreted differently
المشترك (al-mushtarak): An ambiguous word with multiple possible meanings, lacking umum (generality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqif stipulates that the teacher must teach every day, but the teacher misses a day, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The teacher sins but still deserves the stipend.
B) The teacher does not sin but forfeits the stipend for that day.
C) The teacher must make up the day to receive the stipend.
D) The condition is invalid and the teacher receives full stipend.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, clear waqf conditions are binding for compensation but not for sin; ambiguous ones are not enforceable without clarification by the living waqif.

Valid Conditions in Waqf: Binding Stipulations and Judicial Override
A compilation of valid waqf conditions and their consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize waqf conditions into those that bind the trustee absolutely and those that the judge may override, and apply the rule to new cases.

Core Idea
Waqf conditions are binding, but the judge may override those related to yield for public benefit.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the types of conditions a waqif (endower) may validly impose. While Hanafi law holds the waqif's conditions as binding like the Lawgiver's text, it distinguishes conditions that affect the yield (ghalla) of the waqf property — those the judge may override for the beneficiaries' welfare. This lesson walks through the major categories of such conditions and their consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
The passage opens with conditions from al-Khassaf. Recognize that the default rule is that the waqif's conditions are binding and must be followed. Note the exceptions: conditions related to yield (ghalla) may be overridden by the judge, but not by the trustee.
This principle is stated at the end: 'الشرائط الراجعة إلى الغلة وتحصيلها لا يقدر المتولي على مخالفتها ولو كان أصلح للوقف، وإنما يخالفها القاضي'.
2
Categorize the conditions on the trustee
List the conditions that restrict the trustee's actions: (a) not leasing the land, (b) not dealing with trees, (c) automatic removal upon leasing, (d) limiting lease duration to one year. For each, note the consequence of violation.
The judge may override lease duration when it benefits the poor, but only if the condition itself does not allow the trustee to act.
3
Categorize the conditions on the beneficiaries
List conditions that affect beneficiaries: (a) intention to invalidate the waqf leads to expulsion, (b) disputing the trustee even for a rightful claim may lead to expulsion, (c) changing madhhab (e.g., to Mu'tazili, Khariji, Rafidi) leads to expulsion, (d) moving from Baghdad forfeits right, (e) marriage restrictions on ummahat awlad or Sufis. Note the burden of proof on the claimant.
Return to the original state (e.g., return to Baghdad or to original madhhab) may restore rights only if the condition so provides.
4
Distinguish conditions related to yield vs. others
The passage concludes with the key distinction: conditions that affect the collection and distribution of yield (ghalla) can be overridden by the judge for public benefit, but conditions that do not relate to yield cannot be violated even by the judge. Identify which conditions from the list fall into each category.
Examples of ghalla-related: lease duration. Examples of non-ghalla: madhhab conditions, marriage, location.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical waqf condition, determine whether it binds the trustee absolutely or could be overridden by the judge. Consider whether the condition relates to the yield of the property or to the personal conduct of beneficiaries.
This step practices the analytical skill of applying the ghalla vs. non-ghalla distinction.
