ومن الشروط المعتبرة ما صرح به الخصاف لو شرط أن لا يؤجر المتولي الأرض فإن إجارتها باطلة، وكذا اشتراط أن لا يعامل على ما فيها من نخل وأشجار، وكذا إذا شرط أن المتولي إذا أجرها فهو خارج عن التولية، فإذا خالف المتولي صار خارجاً ويوليها القاضي من يثق بأمانته، وكذا إذا شرط أنه إن أحدث أحد من أهل هذا الوقف حدثاً في الوقف يريد إبطاله كان خارجاً اعتبر، فإن نازع البعض وقال أردت تصحيح الوقف وقال سائر أهل الوقف إنما أردت إبطاله نظر القاضي في القوم الذين تنازعوا فإن كانوا يريدون تصحيحه فلهم ذلك، وإن كانوا يريدون إبطاله أخرجهم وأشهدهم على إخراجهم. ولو شرط أن من نازع القيم وتعرض له ولم يقل لإبطاله فنازعه البعض وقال منعني حقي صار خارجاً ولو كان طالباً حقه اتباعاً للشرط كما لو شرط أن من طالبه بحقه فللمتولي إخراجه فلو أخرجه ليس له إعادته بدون الشرط، ومنها ما لو وقف على أولاده وشرط أن من انتقل إلى مذهب المعتزلة صار خارجاً فانتقل منهم واحد صار خارجاً، فإن ادعى على واحد منهم بأنه صار معتزلياً فالبينة على المدعي والقول للمنكر. وكذا لو كان الواقف من المعتزلة وشرط أن من انتقل إلى مذهب أهل السنة صار خارجاً اعتبر شرطه ولو شرط أن من انتقل من مذهب أهل السنة إلى غيره فصار خارجياً أو رافضياً خرج، فلو ارتد والعياذ بالله تعالى عن الإسلام خرج المرأة والرجل سواء، فلو شرط أن من خرج من مذهب الإثبات إلى غيره خرج فخرج واحد ثم عاد إلى مذهب الإثبات لا يعود إلى الوقف إلا بالشرط وكذلك لو عين الواقف مذهباً من المذاهب وشرط أنه إن انتقل عنه خرج اعتبر شرطه وكذا لو شرط أن من انتقل من قرابته من بغداد فلا حق له اعتبر لكن هنا إذا عاد إلى بغداد رد إلى الوقف ولو شرط وقفه على العميان فالشرط باطل وتكون الغلة للمساكين لأن فيهم الغني والفقير وهم لا يحصون وكذا على العوران والعرجان والزمني اهـ. مختصراً. ومنها ما في قاضيخان لو وقف على أمهات أولاده وشرط عدم تزوجهن كان الشرط صحيحاً. فعلى هذا لو شرط في حق الصوفية بالمدرسة عدم التزوج كما بالمدرسة الشيخونية بالقاهرة اعتبر شرطه ومنها ما في الفتاوى أيضاً : لو شرط الواقف أن لا تؤجر أكثر من سنة والناس لا يرغبون في استئجارها وكانت إجارتها أكثر من سنة أنفع للفقراء، فليس للقيم أن يؤاجرها أكثر من سنة ولكنه يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي حتى يؤاجرها القاضي أكثر من سنة لأن للقاضي ولاية النظر على الفقراء وعلى الميت أيضاً، ولو شرط أن لا تؤجر أكثر من سنة إلا إذا كان أنفع للفقراء كان للقيم أن يؤاجرها بنفسه أكثر من سنة إذا كان رأى ذلك خيراً ولا يحتاج إلى القاضي .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أن الشرائط الراجعة إلى الغلة وتحصيلها لا يقدر المتولي على مخالفتها ولو كان أصلح للوقف، وإنما يخالفها القاضي وهذا بخلاف ما لم ترجع إلى الغلة فإنه لا يجوز مخالفة القاضي كما قدمناه في تقرير القاضي فراشاً للمسجد بغير
Among the valid conditions is what al-Khassaf stated: If he stipulates that the trustee may not lease the land, then its lease is void. Likewise, stipulating that he may not transact regarding the palm trees and trees therein. Likewise, if he stipulates that if the trustee leases it, he is removed from trusteeship; then if the trustee violates, he is removed, and the judge appoints someone he trusts. Likewise, if he stipulates that if anyone among the people of this waqf causes an incident in the waqf intending to invalidate it, he is expelled—this is considered. If some dispute and say, 'I intended to correct the waqf,' and the rest of the waqf people say, 'you intended to invalidate it,' the judge looks at those who disputed: if they intended to correct it, they have that; if they intended to invalidate it, he expels them and witnesses their expulsion. And if he stipulates that whoever disputes the trustee and interferes without saying [he intends] to invalidate, and some dispute him saying 'he prevented me from my right,' he is expelled, even if he is demanding his right, following the condition—just as if he stipulates that whoever demands his right, the trustee may expel him; if he expels him, he may not return him without the condition. Among them: if he makes a waqf for his children and stipulates that whoever converts to the Mu'tazili school is expelled, and one of them converts, he is expelled. If he claims that one of them became Mu'tazili, the burden of proof is on the claimant, and the denial of the defendant is accepted. Likewise, if the waqif was Mu'tazili and stipulated that whoever converts to the Sunni school is expelled, his condition is respected. If he stipulates that whoever converts from the Sunni school to another becomes a Khariji or Rafidi, he leaves. If he apostatizes from Islam, he leaves—man and woman are equal. If he stipulates that whoever leaves the school of affirmation (Ithbat) for another leaves, then one leaves and later returns to the school of affirmation, he does not return to the waqf except by condition. Similarly, if the waqif specifies a particular school and stipulates that whoever converts from it leaves, his condition is respected. Likewise, if he stipulates that whoever among his relatives moves from Baghdad has no right, it is respected; but here, if he returns to Baghdad, he is restored to the waqf. If he makes waqf for the blind, the condition is void and the produce goes to the poor because among them are rich and poor, and they are countless—similarly for the one-eyed, the lame, and the chronically ill—end. Summarized. Among them is what is in Qadi Khan: if he makes waqf for his ummahat awlad and stipulates that they not marry, the condition is valid. Thus, if he stipulates regarding the Sufis in a school that they not marry, as in the Shaykhuniyya school in Cairo, his condition is respected. Among them is what is in the Fatawa as well: if the waqif stipulates that it not be leased for more than a year, but people are not inclined to lease it for a year, and leasing for more than a year is more beneficial for the poor, the trustee may not lease it for more than a year, but he refers the matter to the judge so that the judge leases it for more than a year because the judge has authority to look after the poor and also over the deceased. If he stipulates that it not be leased for more than a year unless it is more beneficial for the poor, the trustee may himself lease it for more than a year if he sees that as better, and he does not need the judge—end. From this, it becomes clear that conditions related to the yield and its collection cannot be violated by the trustee even if it would be better for the waqf; only the judge may violate them. This is contrary to what does not relate to the yield, where the judge may not violate, as we previously stated regarding the judge's appointment of a doorman for the mosque without...
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on various conditions that are valid and binding in a waqf. It begins by citing al-Khassaf: if the waqif stipulates that the trustee may not lease the land, any lease by the trustee is void. The same applies to stipulations against dealing with the trees. If the waqif stipulates that leasing by the trustee results in automatic removal from trusteeship, that condition is effective: upon violation, the trustee is removed and the judge appoints a replacement. Similarly, if a beneficiary commits an act intending to invalidate the waqf, he is expelled. If there is a dispute over intent, the judge investigates: if the majority intended correction, they are allowed; if invalidation, they are expelled with witnesses. The condition is also binding if it bars beneficiaries from disputing the trustee, even if they are seeking a rightful claim. This extends to stipulations about changing madhhab: if the waqif stipulates that conversion to the Mu'tazili school results in loss of entitlement, that is effective. If the waqif himself is Mu'tazili and stipulates conversion to Sunni, it is similarly respected. Stipulations about leaving a madhhab, apostasy, or moving from a specific location (e.g., Baghdad) are binding, though return may restore rights if the condition implies so. Conditions for waqf on a specific group (e.g., the blind) are invalid if the group is uncountable and includes rich and poor; the produce goes to the poor instead. The passage also addresses marriage restrictions, citing Qadi Khan: a stipulation that ummahat awlad not marry is valid, and similarly for Sufis in a school. Finally, it discusses lease duration: a condition limiting lease to one year is binding on the trustee, but if it harms beneficiaries, the judge may override it because of his general authority. If the condition itself allows longer lease when beneficial, the trustee may decide without the judge. The key distinction is that conditions affecting the collection and distribution of yield (ghalla) can be overridden by the judge for public benefit, but conditions unrelated to yield cannot be violated even by the judge.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The yield or produce of the waqf property, including rent

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The trustee may decide on his own.
B) Any beneficiary may approve.
C) Only the judge may authorize a longer lease.
D) The condition is void and the trustee may lease for any term.

Key Takeaway
Waqf conditions are binding; only the judge may override those related to yield for the benefit of the poor.

Seven Exceptions to Following Waqf Conditions
Lists seven exceptions to the rule that waqif's condition must be followed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the seven exceptions to the rule that a waqif's condition must be followed in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A waqif's condition is not absolute—seven exceptions allow overriding for public interest or validity.

The Hanafi school establishes that a waqif's condition is like the text of the Lawgiver and must generally be observed. However, Ibn Nujaym in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir enumerates seven cases where the condition may be overridden, either by the judge or the trustee, to protect the waqf's purpose or public benefit. This lesson breaks down each exception and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recall the rule: 'The condition of the waqif is like the text of the Lawgiver'—it is normally binding. The passage lists exceptions.
This is the baseline from which the exceptions depart.
2
Analyze exceptions 1–3: Judge's authority over supervisor, lease duration, and grave recitation
For each: identify the condition stipulated, why it is overridden, and who may override (judge or trustee). First: condition barring removal of unfit supervisor. Second: condition limiting lease to one year when a longer lease benefits the poor. Third: condition specifying a reciter at the grave—void because it serves a private benefit.
Note the distinction: judge can override in first two; the third is void entirely.
3
Analyze exceptions 4–5: Surplus distribution and specific food items
Fourth: condition to give surplus to beggars in a specific mosque—trustee may give elsewhere. Fifth: condition for specific bread and meat—trustee may give cash equivalent; beneficiaries may also demand the specific items or take cash.
The fourth shows flexibility for charity; the fifth shows a choice between in-kind and cash.
4
Analyze exceptions 6–7: Imam's salary and substitution (istibdal)
Sixth: judge may increase imam's salary from waqf if insufficient and imam is qualified. Seventh: condition prohibiting substitution (istibdal) can be overridden by judge if substitution is more beneficial.
Both involve judge's discretion for public interest.
5
Evaluate the closing remark on changing beneficiaries
The passage adds a note on determining poor relatives: the criterion is their state at distribution time, not a fixed status. This highlights that conditions may adapt to changing circumstances.
This is a corollary to the principle of considering current need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت : استثنى المؤلف في أشباهه من هذا الأصل مسائل : الأولى شرط أن القاضي لا يعزل الناظر فله عزل غير الأهل . الثانية شرط أن لا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة والناس لا يرغبون في استئجاره سنة أو كان في الزيادة نفع للفقراء فللقاضي المخالفة دون الناظر الثالثة لو شرط أن يقرأ على قبره فالتعيين باطل . الرابعة شرط أن يتصدق بفاضل الغلة على من يسأل في مسجد كذا كل يوم لم يراع شرطه وللقيم التصدق على سائل غير ذلك المسجد أو خارج المسجد أو على من لا يسأله الخامسة لو شرط للمستحقين خبزاً ولحماً معيناً كل يوم فللقيم أن يدفع القيمة من النقد، وفي موضع آخر لهم طلب العين وأخذ القيمة السادسة تجوز الزيادة من القاضي على معلوم الإمام إذا كان لا يكفيه وكان عالماً تقياً. السابعة شرط الواقف عدم الاستبدال فللقاضي الاستبدال إذا كان أصلح اهـ كلامه قوله : (لكن هنا إذا عاد الخ) لأن النظر ههنا إلى حالهم يوم القسمة ألا ترى أنه لو وقف على فقراء قرابته وكان فيهم فقراء وأغنياء تكون الغلة للفقراء، ثم لو افتقر الأغنياء واستغنى الفقراء تكون الغلة لمن افتقر
I say: The author in his 'Ashbah' excepted from this principle the following issues: First: A stipulation that the judge may not remove the supervisor — but the judge may remove an unfit one. Second: A stipulation that his waqf not be leased for more than a year, but people are not inclined to lease it for a year, or there is benefit for the poor in increasing — the judge may violate it, not the supervisor. Third: If he stipulates that [a reader] read at his grave — the specification is void. Fourth: A stipulation that the surplus yield be given as charity to whoever asks in a certain mosque every day — his condition is not observed, and the trustee may give charity to a beggar in another mosque, outside the mosque, or to one who does not ask. Fifth: If he stipulates for the beneficiaries specific bread and meat every day — the trustee may give the value in cash; and in another place, they may demand the specific item and also take the value. Sixth: The judge may increase the salary of the imam if it does not suffice him and he is a knowledgeable, pious person. Seventh: The waqif's stipulation that there be no substitution (istibdal) — the judge may authorize substitution if it is more beneficial. End of his words. His statement: (But here, if he returns...) because consideration here is to their state on the day of distribution; do you not see that if he makes a waqf for the poor of his relatives and among them are poor and rich, the produce goes to the poor; then if the rich become poor and the poor become rich, the produce goes to those who become poor.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a list of seven exceptions to the general rule that the waqif's condition is like the text of the Lawgiver and must be followed. The author (Ibn Nujaym) enumerates them from his own work 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir'. The first exception: a condition that the judge cannot remove the appointed supervisor (nazir) is overridden if the supervisor is unfit; the judge may remove him. Second: a condition barring lease for more than a year can be violated by the judge if the public interest requires it, such as when a one-year lease is unattractive or a longer lease benefits the poor. The trustee may not violate it himself. Third: a condition specifying that a particular person read at the waqif's grave is void; the appointment is invalid because it is a private benefit unrelated to the waqf's purpose. Fourth: a condition that surplus yield be given daily to beggars in a specific mosque is not binding; the trustee may give to other beggars. Fifth: if the waqif specifies exact food items (bread and meat) for beneficiaries, the trustee may give the cash equivalent; in another opinion, beneficiaries may demand the actual items or take cash. Sixth: the judge may increase the imam's salary from waqf funds if the imam is pious and learned and the salary is insufficient. Seventh: a condition prohibiting substitution (istibdal, selling waqf property to buy better) can be overridden by the judge if substitution is more beneficial. The passage ends with a comment on the seventh exception: when determining who is poor among relatives, the criterion is their state at the time of distribution, not a fixed status. If the rich become poor later, they become entitled.

Key Terms
شرط الواقف (shart al-waqif): The condition set by the founder of a waqf regarding its administration or beneficiaries.
الناظر (al-nazir): The supervisor or manager of a waqf, appointed by the waqif or judge.
الاستبدال (al-istibdal): Exchange of waqf property for another property or its sale to buy a better replacement.
القيم (al-qayyim): The trustee or caretaker of a waqf, often synonymous with nazir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqif stipulates that the surplus yield be given to beggars in a specific mosque daily, what is the ruling?
A) The condition is binding and must be followed exactly.
B) The condition is void and the yield goes to the poor generally.
C) The trustee may give to beggars in other mosques or outside.
D) The condition is valid only if the mosque is specified in the deed.

Key Takeaway
The waqif's condition is generally binding, but Hanafi jurisprudence recognizes seven specific exceptions where overriding is permitted to protect the waqf's purpose or public interest.

Waqf — Endowment

Valid and Void Conditions in Waqf for Exclusion of Beneficiaries
Enumeration of valid and invalid conditions in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which conditions in waqf are valid for excluding beneficiaries and apply that rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A waqif may impose conditions that exclude beneficiaries, but only if the condition is possible to enforce and not contrary to the nature of waqf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates various conditions a waqif can stipulate to exclude certain beneficiaries. Hanafi law gives the waqif wide latitude to condition the distribution of waqf benefits, as long as the condition is not impossible or indefinite. We will examine the valid conditions and the one void condition mentioned, understanding the underlying principle that conditions must be definite and enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on conditions in waqf
The passage states that a waqif may set conditions that exclude beneficiaries. The default ruling is that such conditions are valid and binding, as long as they are not inherently impossible or contrary to the nature of waqf. Identify the general principle: conditions that are possible and definite are upheld.
This is a key feature of Hanafi waqf law: the waqif's stipulations are given effect, even if they restrict who may benefit.
2
Analyze the valid conditions regarding behavior and madhhab
List the valid conditions mentioned: disputing the trustee (even if demanding a right), adopting a different madhhab (e.g., Mu'tazilism, or leaving Sunnism), apostasy, and moving from a specified location. For each, note the specific wording and any procedural rules (e.g., burden of proof on claimant for madhhab change).
Conditions about madhhab are upheld regardless of whether the waqif is Sunni or Mu'tazilite.
3
Understand the effect of return after exclusion
For geographic relocation, if the condition only says moving from a place forfeits the right, then returning restores the right. But if the condition is about madhhab change, returning to the original madhhab does not automatically restore the right unless the condition explicitly states so.
This distinction shows that the waqif's precise wording matters.
4
Identify the void condition and its reason
The passage states that a waqf for 'the blind' is void as a condition, and the produce goes to the poor. The reason given is that the class is indefinite (they are not countable and include both rich and poor). Similarly for the one-eyed, lame, and chronically ill. Recognize that conditions leading to uncertainty (gharar) are void.
This is consistent with the Hanafi prohibition of gharar in waqf conditions.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a new condition (e.g., 'whoever studies in Kufa'), evaluate its validity using the criteria: is it possible? Is it definite? Does it contradict the nature of waqf? Practice by applying to conditions like 'whoever becomes a Hanbali' or 'whoever moves from Kufa to Basra'.
Conditions that are indefinite or impossible are void; the waqf then proceeds as if no condition was made.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شرط أن من نازع القيم وتعرض له ولم يقل لإبطاله فنازعه البعض وقال منعني حقي صار خارجاً ولو كان طالباً حقه اتباعاً للشرط كما لو شرط أن من طالبه بحقه فللمتولي إخراجه فلو أخرجه ليس له إعادته بدون الشرط، ومنها ما لو وقف على أولاده وشرط أن من انتقل إلى مذهب المعتزلة صار خارجاً فانتقل منهم واحد صار خارجاً، فإن ادعى على واحد منهم بأنه صار معتزلياً فالبينة على المدعي والقول للمنكر. وكذا لو كان الواقف من المعتزلة وشرط أن من انتقل إلى مذهب أهل السنة صار خارجاً اعتبر شرطه ولو شرط أن من انتقل من مذهب أهل السنة إلى غيره فصار خارجياً أو رافضياً خرج، فلو ارتد والعياذ بالله تعالى عن الإسلام خرج المرأة والرجل سواء، فلو شرط أن من خرج من مذهب الإثبات إلى غيره خرج فخرج واحد ثم عاد إلى مذهب الإثبات لا يعود إلى الوقف إلا بالشرط وكذلك لو عين الواقف مذهباً من المذاهب وشرط أنه إن انتقل عنه خرج اعتبر شرطه وكذا لو شرط أن من انتقل من قرابته من بغداد فلا حق له اعتبر لكن هنا إذا عاد إلى بغداد رد إلى الوقف ولو شرط وقفه على العميان فالشرط باطل وتكون الغلة للمساكين لأن فيهم الغني والفقير وهم لا يحصون وكذا على العوران والعرجان والزمني اهـ. مختصراً.
And if he stipulates that whoever disputes the trustee and opposes him without saying to invalidate (the waqf), then someone disputes him and says 'he prevented me from my right', he becomes excluded, even if he was demanding his right, following the condition. Just as if he stipulates that whoever demands his right, the trustee may expel him; if he expels him, he cannot return him without the condition. Among these is: if he makes a waqf for his children and stipulates that whoever adopts the Mu'tazilite madhhab becomes excluded, then one of them adopts it, he becomes excluded. If he claims against one of them that he became Mu'tazilite, the burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier. Likewise, if the waqif is Mu'tazilite and stipulates that whoever adopts the Sunni madhhab becomes excluded, his condition is upheld. And if he stipulates that whoever changes from the Sunni madhhab to another becomes an outsider or a Rafidite, he is excluded. If he apostatizes (may Allah protect us) from Islam, he is excluded, whether male or female. If he stipulates that whoever leaves the madhhab of affirmation (al-ithbat) to another leaves, then one leaves and returns to the madhhab of affirmation, he does not return to the waqf except by the condition. Likewise, if the waqif specifies a particular madhhab and stipulates that if one departs from it he leaves, his condition is upheld. Similarly, if he stipulates that whoever moves from his relatives in Baghdad has no right, it is upheld, but here if he returns to Baghdad, he is restored to the waqf. And if he makes a waqf for the blind, the condition is void and the produce goes to the poor, because among them are rich and poor and they are not countable. Similarly for the one-eyed, the lame, and the chronically ill. End. Abridged.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presents a series of rulings regarding the validity of conditions set by the waqif (endower) that exclude certain beneficiaries. The author, Ibn Nujaym, expands on the matn by enumerating various scenarios. The core principle is that conditions that are not contrary to the nature of waqf and are possible to enforce are upheld. The first scenario involves a condition that anyone who disputes the trustee (qayyim) without alleging an attempt to invalidate the waqf will be excluded; even if the beneficiary is merely demanding his right, the condition applies. If the condition explicitly says 'whoever demands his right', the trustee may expel him, but once expelled, he cannot be reinstated without a new condition. The second set of conditions relates to madhhab (school of thought) affiliation. If the waqif stipulates that adopting a different madhhab (e.g., Mu'tazilism) leads to exclusion, it is valid. If the waqif himself is Mu'tazilite and stipulates exclusion for adopting the Sunni madhhab, it is also valid. The same applies to leaving the Sunni madhhab for another, including becoming an outsider (khariji) or Rafidite. Apostasy from Islam also leads to exclusion for both men and women. If the condition specifies a particular madhhab (e.g., 'madhhab al-ithbat' - the affirming school, likely referring to orthodox Sunnism), and one leaves and returns, he does not automatically regain his right; he only returns if the condition so provides. For geographic relocation, if the waqif stipulates that moving from Baghdad forfeits the right, it is valid, but if the beneficiary returns to Baghdad, his right is restored. Finally, conditions that are impossible to implement or contrary to the nature of waqf are void. For example, a waqf for 'the blind' is void because the class is indefinite (some blind are rich, some poor, and they are not countable). Similarly, conditions for the one-eyed, lame, and chronically ill are void because they are not manageable as a defined class. In such cases, the produce goes to the poor generally. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi approach to evaluating stipulations in waqf: they are binding so long as they are possible and not contrary to the permanence of waqf.

Key Terms
النزاع مع القيم (al-niza' ma'a al-qayyim): Disputing or opposing the trustee (mutawalli) of the waqf, which the waqif may condition as grounds for exclusion.
مذهب الإثبات (madhhab al-ithbat): The 'school of affirmation', likely referring to Sunni orthodoxy (Ash'ari or Maturidi) that affirms divine attributes, as opposed to Mu'tazilites who negate them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a waqif stipulates that whoever moves from Baghdad forfeits his right, and a beneficiary moves to Kufa and later returns to Baghdad, what is the ruling?
A) He remains excluded permanently.
B) He is restored to the waqf upon return.
C) He is only restored if the condition explicitly says so upon return.
D) He can be restored only with a new waqf deed.

Key Takeaway
A waqif may impose conditions to exclude beneficiaries, but the condition must be definite and possible; indefinite conditions like waqf for 'the blind' are void.

The Validity of Marriage Prohibition Conditions in Waqf
Ruling on validity of a marriage prohibition condition in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a condition prohibiting marriage in waqf and apply it to analogous female beneficiaries.

Core Idea
A condition in waqf that prohibits female beneficiaries from remarrying is valid and enforceable.

Waqf endowments often include conditions set by the donor (waqif). One such condition is prohibiting female beneficiaries from remarrying, as seen in endowments for ummahat awlad or Sufi women. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such conditions, which are upheld as valid under certain circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Beneficiaries
Determine who the waqf is for: in the source, it is ummahat awlad (slave mothers of the waqif's children) who become free upon his death. The ruling also applies to other female beneficiaries like Sufi women.
2
Understand the Condition
The waqif stipulates that these women must not remarry. The key question is whether such a condition is valid in Hanafi law.
The condition is a shart (stipulation) attached to the waqf.
3
Refer to the Source
The passage cites Qadikhan, a Hanafi jurist, who explicitly rules that the condition is valid (sahih). This is the relied-upon position.
Qadikhan is a recognized authority in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Extend to Analogous Cases
The ruling is not limited to ummahat awlad; it applies to any female beneficiaries in a waqf, such as Sufi women in a madrasa (e.g., Shaykhuniyya Madrasa in Cairo). The condition is upheld in these cases as well.
The expansion shows the principle is general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما في قاضيخان لو وقف على أمهات أولاده وشرط عدم تزوجهن كان الشرط صحيحاً. فعلى هذا لو شرط في حق الصوفية بالمدرسة عدم التزوج كما بالمدرسة الشيخونية بالقاهرة اعتبر شرطه
And among them is what is in Qadikhan: If he makes a waqf for his ummahat awlad (slave mothers of his children) and stipulates that they not remarry, the condition is valid. According to this, if he stipulates for the Sufis at the madrasa that they not marry, as at the Shaykhuniyya madrasa in Cairo, his condition is upheld.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage cites the ruling from Qadikhan, a Hanafi jurist, regarding a condition in waqf that prohibits the female beneficiaries from marrying. The waqif may be an owner of ummahat awlad (slave women who have borne their master's children), and upon his death they become free and inherit? Actually, ummahat awlad are freed upon the master's death, but the waqf here is upon them as free women. The ruling states that the condition prohibiting marriage is valid. This extends to any female beneficiaries, such as Sufi women housed in a madrasa. The example of the Shaykhuniyya madrasa in Cairo is given where such a condition was upheld. The Hanafi position is that such conditions are permissible as long as they are not contrary to the inviolable aspects of the waqf.

Key Terms
أمهات الأولاد (ummahat al-awlad): Female slaves who have given birth to a child by their master; upon the master's death, they become free.
شرط (shart): A condition or stipulation attached to a legal act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A condition in waqf prohibiting female beneficiaries from marrying is valid and extends to all analogous beneficiaries.

Waqif's Condition on Lease Period and Qadi's Authority
Ruling on waqif's condition restricting lease period and qadi's authority to override

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on waqif's lease condition by distinguishing when the trustee may act alone versus when the qadi's intervention is required.

Core Idea
The trustee must obey the waqif's condition; only the qadi can override an absolute condition for maslaha.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq illustrates a tension between the waqif's stipulation and the beneficiaries' interest. The Hanafi school holds that the trustee (qayyim) is bound by the waqif's condition, but the qadi possesses a superior authority to override the condition for the sake of the poor. Understanding the distinction between an absolute condition and one with an exception clause is crucial for proper waqf administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif's condition
Read the stipulation carefully. In this case, the condition restricts the lease period to a maximum of one year.
2
Determine if the condition includes an exception for maslaha
Check whether the condition has a clause allowing longer leases if beneficial for the poor. The passage gives two versions: an absolute condition and one with an 'unless' clause.
The exception empowers the trustee to act independently.
3
Apply the absolute condition scenario
If the condition is absolute, the trustee must not lease longer than one year, even if a longer lease is more beneficial. The trustee must refer the matter to the qadi, who can override the condition due to his general authority over waqf interests.
The qadi's authority stems from his role as guardian of the poor and the deceased.
4
Apply the conditional exception scenario
If the condition includes an exception for the poor's benefit, the trustee may himself lease for more than one year if he deems it beneficial, without needing the qadi.
The trustee's discretion is limited to what is genuinely beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما في الفتاوى أيضاً : لو شرط الواقف أن لا تؤجر أكثر من سنة والناس لا يرغبون في استئجارها وكانت إجارتها أكثر من سنة أنفع للفقراء، فليس للقيم أن يؤاجرها أكثر من سنة ولكنه يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي حتى يؤاجرها القاضي أكثر من سنة لأن للقاضي ولاية النظر على الفقراء وعلى الميت أيضاً، ولو شرط أن لا تؤجر أكثر من سنة إلا إذا كان أنفع للفقراء كان للقيم أن يؤاجرها بنفسه أكثر من سنة إذا كان رأى ذلك خيراً ولا يحتاج إلى القاضي .اهـ.
And among them is what is in al-Fatawa also: If the waqif stipulates that it not be leased for more than a year, and people are not willing to rent it, and leasing it for more than a year would be more beneficial for the poor, then the trustee may not lease it for more than a year, but he refers the matter to the qadi so that the qadi may lease it for more than a year, because the qadi has authority to look after the poor and also over the deceased. And if he stipulates that it not be leased for more than a year unless it is more beneficial for the poor, then the trustee may himself lease it for more than a year if he considers that good, and he does not need the qadi. End.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This ruling from al-Fatawa (likely Fatawa Qadikhan or similar) addresses a common conflict: the waqif's condition restricts the lease period to one year, but market conditions make a longer lease more profitable for the beneficiaries (the poor). The Hanafi position distinguishes two scenarios. In the first, the condition is absolute: no lease over one year. The trustee (qayyim) must obey and cannot lease longer even if it would be more beneficial. However, he may refer the matter to the qadi, who has general authority over waqf interests and can override the condition because the qadi has guardianship over the poor and the deceased waqif. In the second scenario, the waqif includes an exception: 'unless it is more beneficial for the poor.' In that case, the trustee himself may decide to lease for more than a year without qadi involvement, because the condition gives him discretion. This showcases the Hanafi principle that conditions related to the administration of the waqf (such as lease terms) are binding on the trustee, but the qadi can override them for the sake of maslaha (benefit) when the condition is absolute.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The trustee or administrator of the waqf, synonymous with mutawalli.
شرط (shart): Condition; a stipulation made by the waqif that must be followed in the administration of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the waqif stipulates that the waqf property cannot be leased for more than one year, and a longer lease would be more profitable for the beneficiaries, what should the trustee do?
A) Lease for the longer term anyway.
B) Follow the condition strictly and not lease longer.
C) Refer the matter to the qadi to authorize a longer lease.
D) Ask the beneficiaries for permission.

Key Takeaway
The trustee must obey the waqif's absolute condition; only the qadi can override for maslaha; if the condition itself has an exception for maslaha, the trustee has discretion.

Waqf Conditions: The Trustee's Authority vs. the Qadi's Override
Distinguishing conditions related to waqf yield from other conditions for qadi's override

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between yield-related and non-yield-related conditions in waqf and state the limits of the trustee's and qadi's authority to override them.

Core Idea
Only the qadi can override yield conditions in waqf; the trustee is bound by them even for greater benefit.

In waqf administration, the founder's conditions often specify how the yield is collected and distributed. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line: conditions pertaining to the yield itself are binding on the trustee, even if he sees a more beneficial alternative. Only the qadi, representing public interest, can modify them. But for non-yield conditions, even the qadi is bound. This principle ensures both respect for the founder's will and flexibility for the common good.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of conditions
From the text, note that conditions are divided into those related to the yield (ghalla) and those not related to the yield. Recognize that this classification determines which authority can override them.
Yield conditions include rent distribution, investment strategies, etc. Non-yield conditions include placement of objects, ritual directions, etc.
2
State the authority for each category
For yield conditions, the trustee cannot violate them even if it seems better; only the qadi may override. For non-yield conditions, even the qadi cannot violate them.
This is a strict rule with no discretion for the trustee regarding yield conditions.
3
Understand the rationale behind the distinction
Yield conditions involve financial administration and public interest, hence the qadi's overriding authority. Non-yield conditions often pertain to ritual or fixed matters where change would undermine the founder's intent without countervailing benefit.
The qadi's power is not absolute; it is limited to yield-related matters.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Consider a waqf where the founder stipulated that the rental income be given to a specific charity. The trustee believes giving to another charity would be more beneficial. According to this lesson, the trustee cannot change this on his own; he must seek the qadi's permission.
This illustrates the practical impact of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا ظهر أن الشرائط الراجعة إلى الغلة وتحصيلها لا يقدر المتولي على مخالفتها ولو كان أصلح للوقف، وإنما يخالفها القاضي وهذا بخلاف ما لم ترجع إلى الغلة فإنه لا يجوز مخالفة القاضي كما قدمناه في تقرير القاضي فراشاً للمسجد بغير سائل غير ذلك المسجد أو خارج المسجد أو على من لا يسأله
And by this, it becomes clear that conditions related to the yield (ghalla) and its collection, the trustee cannot violate them even if it were better for the waqf; only the qadi can violate them. This is in contrast to matters not related to the yield, for which it is not permissible for the qadi to violate, as we have previously stated in the determination of the qadi placing a mat in the mosque without an inquirer other than that mosque or outside the mosque or upon one who does not ask him.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This short passage extracts a general principle from the preceding rulings about lease conditions. The principle is: Conditions that pertain to the yield (ghalla) of the waqf—such as how it is collected, distributed, or invested—are binding on the trustee (mutawalli). He cannot deviate from them even if he believes a different course would be more beneficial for the waqf. Only the qadi, who has overarching authority over waqf administration, may override such conditions for the public good. In contrast, conditions that do not relate to the yield—such as the direction of the prayer rug in a mosque (the example given is about the qadi placing a mat in the mosque in a certain way) cannot be violated even by the qadi. These are matters of ritual or specific use that are not subject to financial optimization. The example is somewhat cryptic but illustrates the point: the qadi cannot change a condition about where a mat should be placed in the mosque (e.g., facing a certain direction) because that is not a yield-related matter. Thus, the Hanafi school distinguishes between administrative and ritual conditions in waqf.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The yield or income generated from the waqf property, such as rent or produce.
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The trustee or administrator of a waqf.
القاضي (al-qadi): The judge with supervisory authority over waqf administration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who has the authority to override conditions related to the yield (ghalla) of a waqf?
A) The trustee (mutawalli) alone.
B) The qadi (judge) alone.
C) Both the trustee and the qadi.
D) Neither, the conditions are absolute.

Key Takeaway
Yield-related waqf conditions are binding on the trustee and can only be overridden by the qadi, preserving both the founder's intent and public interest.

Fifth Ruling: Trustee’s Option to Pay Cash Value
First ruling: substitution of in-kind with cash.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the trustee may pay cash value when the waqif specified in-kind, and identify the alternative view that beneficiaries may demand the specific items.

Core Idea
The trustee may replace in-kind with cash, but the beneficiaries can demand the original items.

Waqif sometimes specifies exact items for beneficiaries, like bread and meat. The trustee has flexibility to pay cash equivalent, but beneficiaries may also insist on the original. This ruling balances administrative convenience with beneficiary rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulation
The waqif conditions specific bread and meat for beneficiaries each day.
2
Recognize the trustee’s option
The trustee may pay the cash value instead of the in-kind items.
This is a managerial discretion.
3
Note the alternative view
Another source states beneficiaries may demand the actual items or accept cash.
Indicates potential difference in practice.
4
Understand the practical outcome
The preferred view allows trustee flexibility, but beneficiaries have a choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة لو شرط للمستحقين خبزاً ولحماً معيناً كل يوم فللقيم أن يدفع القيمة من النقد، وفي موضع آخر لهم طلب العين وأخذ القيمة السادسة تجوز الزيادة من القاضي على معلوم الإمام إذا كان لا يكفيه وكان عالماً تقياً. السابعة شرط الواقف عدم الاستبدال فللقاضي الاستبدال إذا كان أصلح اهـ كلامه
The fifth: If he stipulates for the beneficiaries bread and specific meat each day, the trustee may pay the value in cash. In another place, they may demand the specific item and take the value. The sixth: The qadi may increase the known stipend of the imam if it is insufficient for him and he is a knowledgeable and pious person. The seventh: The waqif stipulates no substitution, but the qadi may substitute if it is more beneficial. End of his speech.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents three numbered rulings from the same source (likely al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on earlier matn). The fifth ruling deals with a waqf where the waqif specified that beneficiaries receive bread and meat daily. The trustee has the option to pay the cash equivalent instead. However, another source (موضع آخر) states that the beneficiaries may demand the actual items or accept the cash value. This indicates a difference of opinion, but the preferred view may be that the trustee can pay cash equivalent. The sixth ruling: The qadi may increase the imam's fixed salary from the waqf if the current salary is insufficient, provided the imam is knowledgeable (alim) and pious (taqi). The seventh ruling: Even if the waqif explicitly prohibits substitution (istibdal) of the waqf property, the qadi may authorize substitution if it is more beneficial for the waqf. This highlights the qadi's overriding authority to protect the waqf's interests.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The trustee or manager of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The waqif
B) The qadi
C) The trustee
D) The beneficiaries

Key Takeaway
The trustee may pay cash value even if in-kind is stipulated, but beneficiaries may demand the original items.

Sixth Ruling: Qadi’s Authority to Increase Imam’s Salary
Second ruling: qadi’s ability to increase imam’s salary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a qadi may increase the imam’s fixed salary from waqf funds.

Core Idea
The qadi may raise the imam’s salary if it is insufficient and the imam is knowledgeable and pious.

An imam serves the community and may receive a fixed salary from a waqf. If the salary does not meet his needs, the qadi can increase it, provided the imam is qualified and righteous. This ensures the imam’s livelihood and continued service.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The imam has a known stipend (ma'lum) from the waqf.
2
Check the condition of insufficiency
The stipend is not enough for the imam’s basic needs.
Not specified what constitutes insufficiency, left to qadi’s judgment.
3
Check the imam’s qualities
The imam must be knowledgeable (alim) and pious (taqi).
These ensure the increase serves the waqf’s purpose.
4
Qadi’s authority
The qadi may increase the salary from the waqf funds.
The qadi has oversight to adjust for public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة لو شرط للمستحقين خبزاً ولحماً معيناً كل يوم فللقيم أن يدفع القيمة من النقد، وفي موضع آخر لهم طلب العين وأخذ القيمة السادسة تجوز الزيادة من القاضي على معلوم الإمام إذا كان لا يكفيه وكان عالماً تقياً. السابعة شرط الواقف عدم الاستبدال فللقاضي الاستبدال إذا كان أصلح اهـ كلامه
The fifth: If he stipulates for the beneficiaries bread and specific meat each day, the trustee may pay the value in cash. In another place, they may demand the specific item and take the value. The sixth: The qadi may increase the known stipend of the imam if it is insufficient for him and he is a knowledgeable and pious person. The seventh: The waqif stipulates no substitution, but the qadi may substitute if it is more beneficial. End of his speech.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents three numbered rulings from the same source (likely al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on earlier matn). The fifth ruling deals with a waqf where the waqif specified that beneficiaries receive bread and meat daily. The trustee has the option to pay the cash equivalent instead. However, another source (موضع آخر) states that the beneficiaries may demand the actual items or accept the cash value. This indicates a difference of opinion, but the preferred view may be that the trustee can pay cash equivalent. The sixth ruling: The qadi may increase the imam's fixed salary from the waqf if the current salary is insufficient, provided the imam is knowledgeable (alim) and pious (taqi). The seventh ruling: Even if the waqif explicitly prohibits substitution (istibdal) of the waqf property, the qadi may authorize substitution if it is more beneficial for the waqf. This highlights the qadi's overriding authority to protect the waqf's interests.

Key Terms
المعلوم (al-ma'lum): The fixed salary or stipend assigned from the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When may the qadi increase the imam's salary?
A) Whenever the qadi deems it necessary
B) Only if the salary is insufficient and the imam is knowledgeable and pious
C) Only with the consent of the waqif’s heirs
D) Only if the imam requests an increase

Key Takeaway
The qadi may increase the imam’s salary from waqf funds if it is insufficient and the imam is learned and pious.

Seventh Ruling: Qadi’s Substitution Despite Waqif’s Prohibition
Third ruling: qadi's substitution overriding condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that the qadi may authorize substitution of waqf property even if the waqif prohibited it, provided it is more beneficial.

Core Idea
The qadi may override the waqif’s prohibition of substitution for the sake of greater benefit.

A waqif often includes conditions to preserve his endowment. One common condition is a ban on substitution. However, circumstances may change, making substitution beneficial. The qadi, as guardian of the waqf, can authorize a swap if it serves the waqf’s long-term interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif’s condition
The waqif stipulates that the waqf property cannot be substituted.
This is a binding condition in normal circumstances.
2
Recognize the qadi’s power
The qadi may authorize substitution despite this condition.
This is an exception to the rule.
3
Understand the justification
The qadi can do so if it is more beneficial (aslah) for the waqf.
Benefit is measured in terms of increased revenue or better utility.
4
Apply the principle
This ruling balances the waqif’s intent with the dynamic needs of the waqf.
The qadi must exercise ijtihad to determine what is more beneficial.

Source Text

Waqf Yield Distribution to Current Poor Among Relatives
Ruling that waqf for poor relatives goes to current poor, not based on past status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for distributing waqf yield to poor relatives and apply it to changing financial circumstances.

Core Idea
Waqf for poor relatives goes to whoever is poor at distribution time, not the originally poor.

A waqf designated for 'poor relatives' must be distributed according to the current state of poverty, not the state at the time of the waqf's creation. This ensures the beneficiary class remains truly deserving. Let's explore a concise ruling from the Hanafi school that clarifies this dynamic nature of beneficiary eligibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqf designation
The waqf is made for 'poor relatives' (fuqara' al-qaraba). This is the beneficiary class: a subset of relatives defined by poverty.
2
Apply the initial distribution
At the time of first distribution, some relatives are poor and some are rich. The ruling states the yield is only for the poor ones.
The rich are excluded because they do not meet the condition of being poor.
3
Consider a change in financial status
Later, the previously rich become poor, and the previously poor become rich. The ruling states that the yield now belongs to those who have become poor.
Eligibility is based on present poverty, not past status.
4
Extract the general principle
The description 'poor' is a temporal condition. It is reassessed at each distribution period. The waqf must be given to whoever is poor at that time.
This ensures the waqf always reaches the deserving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ألا ترى أنه لو وقف على فقراء قرابته وكان فيهم فقراء وأغنياء تكون الغلة للفقراء، ثم لو افتقر الأغنياء واستغنى الفقراء تكون الغلة لمن افتقر
Do you not see that if he makes a waqf for the poor of his relatives, and among them are poor and rich, the yield is for the poor. Then, if the rich become poor and the poor become rich, the yield belongs to those who become poor.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This brief ruling clarifies the distribution rule for a waqf designated for 'poor relatives.' The key point is that eligibility is determined at the time of each distribution, not at the moment of the waqf's creation. If initially there are both poor and rich relatives, the yield goes exclusively to the poor. Later, if the rich become poor and the previously poor become rich, the yield now goes to the newly poor relatives. This is because the description 'poor' is a temporal condition; it applies to whoever is poor when the distribution occurs. This ensures the waqf always benefits the deserving at the present time.

Key Terms
فقراء القرابة (fuqara' al-qaraba): Poor relatives of the waqif, a common category for waqf beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf is made for 'the poor of my relatives', and initially some relatives are poor and some rich, then later the rich become poor and the poor become rich, who receives the waqf income?
A) The original poor remain entitled.
B) The newly poor receive it.
C) The income is split equally among all.
D) The waqf reverts to the waqif's heirs.

Key Takeaway
The eligibility for a waqf designated for 'poor relatives' is reassessed each distribution period based on current poverty status, not the status at the time of the waqf's creation.

Beneficiaries' Right to Choose Yield in Waqf
Ruling on beneficiary option in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that beneficiaries may choose between the original waqf yield and its cash equivalent, and identify that the administrator has no discretion.

Core Idea
Beneficiaries choose; the administrator must comply.

In waqf, the founder may specify a particular yield. What if the administrator wishes to substitute cash? This lesson clarifies that the beneficiaries, not the trustee, have the right to decide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqf setup
Note that the waqf is on wheat for students of fiqh; the administrator pays dinars.
2
Recognize the beneficiaries' choice
The text states they may request the wheat or take the dinars if they wish.
3
Confirm the trustee's lack of choice
The apparent meaning is that the trustee has no choice and must pay what the beneficiaries choose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف غلتها من شرط الواقف فإنه غير جائز . وفي القنية: وقف على المتفقهة حنطة فيدفعها القيم دنانير فلهم طلب الحنطة ولهم أخذ الدنانير إن شاؤوا .اهـ. وبهذا يعلم أن الخيار للمستحقين في أخذ الخبز المشروط لهم أو قيمته وظاهره أنه لا خيار للمتولي وأنه يجبر على دفع ما شاؤوا. وفي القنية : يجوز صرف شيء من وجوه مصالح المسجد إلى الإمام إذا كان يتعطل لو لم يصرف إليه يجوز صرف الفاضل عن المصالح إلى الإمام الفقير بإذن القاضي لا بأس بأن يعين شيئاً من مسبلات المصالح للإمام زيد في وجه الإمام من مصالح المسجد ثم نصب إمام آخر فله أخذه إن كانت الزيادة لقلة وجود الإمام، وإن كان لمعنى في الإمام الأول نحو فضيلة أو زيادة حاجة فلا تحل للثاني . قال الإمام للقاضي : إن مرسومي المعين لا يفي بنفقتي ونفقة عيالي فزاد القاضي في مرسومه من أوقاف المسجد بغير رضا أهل المحلة والإمام مستغن وغيره يؤم بالمرسوم المعهود تطيب له الزيادة إذا كان عالماً تقياً .اهـ. ثم قال : إذا شرط الواقف أن يعطي شاء أو قال على أن يضعها حيث شاء فله أن يعطي الأغنياء.
The book of waqf. Its yield from the condition of the founder is not permissible. In al-Qunyah: He endowed wheat for the students of fiqh, so the administrator pays dinars. They may request the wheat and they may take the dinars if they wish. End quote. By this it is known that the choice is for the beneficiaries to take the bread conditioned for them or its value, and apparently there is no choice for the trustee and he is compelled to pay what they wish. In al-Qunyah: It is permissible to spend something from the categories of the mosque's benefits to the imam if he would be idle without it. It is permissible to spend the surplus beyond the benefits to the poor imam with the permission of the judge. There is no harm in assigning something from the mosque's endowments to imam Zayd as a salary from the mosque's benefits, then another imam is appointed; he may take it if the increase was due to scarcity of imams. But if it was for a reason in the first imam, such as virtue or increased need, it is not permissible for the second. The imam said to the judge: My fixed stipend does not cover my expenses and my family's expenses, so the judge increased his stipend from the mosque's endowments without the consent of the neighborhood residents, while the imam is self-sufficient and another leads with the usual stipend; the increase is permissible for him if he is knowledgeable and pious. End quote. Then he said: If the founder stipulates that he may give to whomever he wishes, or says: 'He may place it wherever he wishes,' then he may give to the rich.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with conditions in waqf. The opening statement indicates that a condition imposed by the founder that contradicts the nature of waqf is invalid. The reference to al-Qunyah provides an example: a waqf of wheat for students of fiqh; the administrator pays dinars instead. The beneficiaries have the choice to take the wheat or its value. The ruling clarifies that the choice belongs to the beneficiaries, not the administrator. The administrator must comply with their decision. The passage then discusses surplus from mosque endowments: it may be directed to the imam in need, with the judge's permission. If another imam is appointed later, he may receive the stipend only if the increase was due to scarcity of imams, not due to the first imam's personal qualities. The final ruling addresses a founder's condition allowing the administrator to give to whomever he wishes; this allows giving to the rich as well.

Key Terms
الواقف (al-wāqif): The person who establishes the waqf (endowment).
القيم (al-qayyim): The administrator or trustee of the waqf.
المستحقون (al-mustaḥiqqūn): The beneficiaries entitled to the waqf's yield.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf is established on wheat for students, and the administrator offers dinars instead, what is the students' right?
A) They must accept dinars.
B) They may choose between wheat and dinars.
C) They cannot take dinars.
D) The administrator decides.

Key Takeaway
Beneficiaries have the right to choose between the waqf yield and its cash equivalent; the administrator must follow their decision.

Using Surplus Mosque Endowments for the Imam's Stipend
Ruling on surplus mosque endowments and imam stipends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when surplus from mosque endowments may be given to the imam, and identify the conditions regarding a subsequent imam's entitlement.

Core Idea
Surplus mosque funds can support the imam in need, but a later imam's entitlement depends on the reason for the stipend.

Mosque endowments are designated for specific expenses. Surplus may be redirected to the imam if he is needy, with the judge's permission. But if a new imam is appointed, his right to the stipend depends on whether the increase was due to scarcity of imams or the first imam's personal merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Surplus from mosque endowments exists after covering basic needs.
2
Apply the rule for giving to the imam
It is permissible to give surplus to a poor imam with the judge's permission.
3
Consider the case of a new imam
If a new imam is appointed, he may take the stipend only if the increase was due to scarcity of imams, not due to the first imam's virtue or greater need.

Source Text

Founder's Condition Giving Trustee Discretion to Give to Rich Beneficiaries
Ruling on founder's condition of discretion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that if a founder stipulates that the trustee may give the yield to whomever he wishes, this includes the wealthy.

Core Idea
A condition allowing the trustee discretion permits giving to the rich unless prohibited.

A waqf founder may impose conditions on distribution. If he says 'give to whomever you wish,' the trustee has broad discretion, even to give to the wealthy. This lesson explains the scope of such a condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The founder says: 'He may give to whomever he wishes' or 'He may place it wherever he wishes.'
2
Interpret the condition
Such a condition gives the trustee wide latitude; it is not restricted to the poor.
3
Apply the ruling
The trustee may give to the rich because there is no restriction in the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف غلتها من شرط الواقف فإنه غير جائز . وفي القنية: وقف على المتفقهة حنطة فيدفعها القيم دنانير فلهم طلب الحنطة ولهم أخذ الدنانير إن شاؤوا .اهـ. وبهذا يعلم أن الخيار للمستحقين في أخذ الخبز المشروط لهم أو قيمته وظاهره أنه لا خيار للمتولي وأنه يجبر على دفع ما شاؤوا. وفي القنية : يجوز صرف شيء من وجوه مصالح المسجد إلى الإمام إذا كان يتعطل لو لم يصرف إليه يجوز صرف الفاضل عن المصالح إلى الإمام الفقير بإذن القاضي لا بأس بأن يعين شيئاً من مسبلات المصالح للإمام زيد في وجه الإمام من مصالح المسجد ثم نصب إمام آخر فله أخذه إن كانت الزيادة لقلة وجود الإمام، وإن كان لمعنى في الإمام الأول نحو فضيلة أو زيادة حاجة فلا تحل للثاني . قال الإمام للقاضي : إن مرسومي المعين لا يفي بنفقتي ونفقة عيالي فزاد القاضي في مرسومه من أوقاف المسجد بغير رضا أهل المحلة والإمام مستغن وغيره يؤم بالمرسوم المعهود تطيب له الزيادة إذا كان عالماً تقياً .اهـ. ثم قال : إذا شرط الواقف أن يعطي شاء أو قال على أن يضعها حيث شاء فله أن يعطي الأغنياء.

Key Terms
الأغنياء (al-aghnīyā’): The wealthy, as opposed to the poor.

Waqf with Lapsed Time and Administrator's Substitution
Rulings on waqf when distribution time lapses and administrator's substitution of assets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between waqf for tamlīk and waqf for ibāḥa, and apply the ruling on administrator's substitution of the waqf yield.

Core Idea
The permissibility of substituting waqf yield depends on whether the waqf is for ownership (tamlīk) or permissive use (ibāḥa).

This lesson examines two interconnected waqf issues: what to do when the time for distribution has passed, and the administrator's authority to substitute the specified assets. The key to understanding both lies in the purpose of the waqf—whether it aims to give ownership of the yield to beneficiaries or merely to provide use. We will explore the Hanafi rulings as articulated by Abu Nasr al-Dabbusi and later commentators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario: missed distribution
Read the opening ruling: if a waqf stipulates a yearly sacrifice but the administrator fails to perform it in time, the yield is given in charity. This shows that the charity purpose overrides the specific mode when the time lapses.
2
Classify the waqf purposes in the examples
Examine the examples from Abu Nasr al-Dabbusi: waqf for buying bread and clothes for charity (tamlīk) vs. waqf for buying horses and weapons for jihad (ibāḥa). Note the different rulings on substitution.
tamlīk = giving ownership of the yield; ibāḥa = allowing use without ownership.
3
Apply the distinction to determine substitution validity
For tamlīk waqf (e.g., charity), the administrator can give the yield directly because the purpose is to benefit the poor. For ibāḥa waqf (e.g., jihad equipment), the administrator must purchase and provide the specific items; giving cash is not allowed.
The text explicitly says: 'لا يجوز التصدق بعين الغلة' for ibāḥa waqf.
4
Analyze the commentary's critique on exchanging wheat for dinars
The commentary refutes a previous claim, emphasizing that the beneficiaries' right to take dinars was due to the administrator's consent, not a general right to substitute. This cements the principle that substitution is tied to the waqf's purpose.
This clarifies that the administrator's substitution is not unilateral; it requires that the waqf be for tamlīk and the beneficiaries agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيها من باب الوقف الذي مضى زمن صرفه ولم يصرفه إلى المصرف ماذا يصنع به وقف مستغلاً على أن يضحي عنه بعد موته من غلته كذا شاة كل سنة وقفاً صحيحاً ولم يضح القيم عنه حتى مضت أيام النحر يتصدق به وفيها باب تصرفات القيم من التبديل وتغيير الشروط ونحوها. قال أبو نصر الدبوسي رحمه الله : إذا جعل الوقف على شراء الخبز والثياب والتصدق بها على الفقراء يجوز عندي بأن يتصدق بعين الغلة من غير شراء خبز ولا ثوب لأن التصدق هو المقصود حتى جاز التقرب بالتصدق دون الشراء، ولو وقف على أن يشتري بها الخيل والسلاح على محتاجي المجاهدين جاز التصدق بعين الغلة كالخبز والثياب وإن شرط أن يسلمه الخيل والسلاح فيجاهد من غير تمليك ويسترد ممن أحب ثم يدفع إلى من أحب جاز الوقف، ويستوي فيه الغني والفقير ولا يجوز التصدق بعين الغلة ولا بالسلاح بل يشتري الخيل والسلاح ويبذلها لأهلها على وجهها لأن الوقف وقع للإباحة لا للتمليك. وكذا لو وقف على شراء النسم وعتقها جاز، ولم يجز إعطاء الغلة، وكذا لو وقف ليضحي أو ليهدي إلى مكة دون من استغنى، ولو لم ينظر إلى حالهم يوم القسمة لربما لزمه دفع الغلة إلى الأغنياء دون الفقراء إسعاف. قوله: (وبهذا يعلم الخ أقول : فيه نظر لأن ثبوت طلب الحنطة لهم لكونها أصل المشروط لهم، وأما إن لهم أخذ الدنانير فهو لكون القيم رضي بذلك فإذا رضوا أيضاً بأخذها بدلاً . عن أصل المشروط لهم جاز ذلك، ولا يدل ذلك على أن لهم استبدال المشروط لهم بالدنانير سواء رضي القيم أو لا تأمل قوله : (وفي القنية يجوز صرف شيء الخ) أي إذا اتحد الواقف والجهة كما مر في آخر قوله : ويبدأ من غلة الوقف بعمارته في قوله السادس عشر. قوله : (قال الإمام للقاضي أن مرسومي الخ قال الرملي : (عت) في وجوه الإمامة قلة فزاد أهل المحلة داراً له من مسبلات المسجد وحكم الحاكم به لا ينفذ؛ نقله الزاهدي في قنيته وكذا في حاويه. قال
And in it, from the chapter of waqf whose time of distribution has passed and it was not distributed to the beneficiary: what should be done with it? He endowed a property with the condition that a sacrifice be made from its yield after his death, such and such a sheep every year, as a valid waqf, but the administrator did not sacrifice until the days of Nahr passed: he should give it in charity. And in it, the chapter on the actions of the administrator regarding substitution and changing conditions and the like. Abu Nasr al-Dabbusi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: If the waqf is made for the purchase of bread and clothes and giving them in charity to the poor, it is permissible in my view to give charity from the yield itself without purchasing bread or clothes, because giving charity is the purpose, such that it is permissible to seek closeness through charity without purchase. And if he endows so that horses and weapons are purchased for the needy mujahideen, it is permissible to give charity from the yield itself, like bread and clothes. But if he stipulates that the horses and weapons be given for jihad without ownership, and that they be taken back from whomever he wishes, then given to whomever he wishes, the waqf is valid, and rich and poor are equal, and it is not permissible to give the yield itself or the weapons; rather, horses and weapons must be purchased and given to their people in the proper manner, because the waqf occurred for permissive use, not ownership. Similarly, if he endows for the purchase of slaves and their emancipation, it is permissible, and it is not permissible to give the yield. Similarly, if he endows to sacrifice or to send a gift to Mecca, excluding those who have become self-sufficient. And if he does not consider their condition on the day of distribution, perhaps it would be necessary to give the yield to the rich instead of the poor out of kindness. His statement: (By this it is known... I say: There is consideration, because the establishment of their right to request the wheat is because it is the original of what was stipulated for them. As for their taking the dinars, it is because the administrator consented to that. So if they also consent to take it as a substitute for the original stipulated, it is permissible. But this does not indicate that they have the right to substitute the stipulated for dinars, whether the administrator consents or not. Reflect on his statement: (In al-Qunyah, it is permissible to spend something... i.e., if the founder and the direction are the same, as mentioned at the end of his statement: And one begins from the yield of the waqf with its maintenance in his statement the sixteenth. His statement: (The imam said to the judge: My stipend... al-Ramli said: (?) There is scarcity in the ranks of the imamate, so the neighborhood residents increased a house for him from the mosque's endowments, and the judge's ruling on it is not enforceable, as al-Zahidi transmitted in his Qunyah and also in his Hawi. He said.

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues: waqf where the time for distribution has passed, and the administrator's authority to substitute. The first ruling: if a waqf stipulates a yearly sacrifice but the administrator fails to perform it in time, the yield is given in charity. The second part quotes Abu Nasr al-Dabbusi, who distinguishes between different types of waqf purposes. For waqf intended to purchase bread and clothes for charity, the administrator may give the yield directly because charity is the goal. For waqf intended to provide horses and weapons for jihad (without ownership), the administrator must purchase the horses and weapons and lend them; giving the yield directly is not allowed because the waqf is for permissive use (ibāḥa) not ownership (tamlīk). Similarly for waqf to purchase slaves and free them, or to sacrifice, the specific purpose must be fulfilled. The commentary then critiques a previous statement (from lesson 1), clarifying that the beneficiaries' right to take dinars was because the administrator agreed, not that they have an unqualified right to substitute.

Key Terms
التصدق (al-taṣadduq): Giving charity; in this context the direct giving of the yield.
الإباحة (al-ibāḥa): Permissive use, where the beneficiary is allowed to use the object without ownership.
التمليك (al-tamlīk): Ownership; when the beneficiary becomes owner of the yield or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must purchase bread and clothes.
B) He can give the yield directly in charity.
C) He can only give cash.
D) He must wait for the beneficiaries to request.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of substituting waqf yield hinges on whether the waqf is for tamlīk (ownership) or ibāḥa (permissive use).

When Does Mosque Ownership Cease? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mosque ownership cessation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on when a builder's ownership of a mosque ceases and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A mosque builder's ownership ends only upon physical separation and prayer permission—except Abu Yusuf says the mere declaration suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when does the builder of a mosque lose ownership? The majority holds that ownership continues until the mosque is physically separated and prayer is permitted, while Abu Yusuf holds that the mere declaration 'I have made it a mosque' transfers ownership. This difference has practical implications for the validity of subsequent transactions and the mosque's waqf status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the dispute
Locate the sentence: 'ومن بنى مسجداً لم يزل ملكه عنه حتى يفرزه عن ملكه بطريقه ويأذن بالصلاة' and note the phrase 'وقال أبو يوسف يزول ملكه بقوله جعلته مسجداً'. Recognize that two views exist within the Hanafi school.
The majority view is stated first; Abu Yusuf's view is introduced later as a contrasting opinion.
2
State the majority Hanafi view
The majority (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that ownership does not cease until the builder physically separates the mosque from his property (e.g., by a pathway) and permits prayer in it. Until then, the building remains his property.
The condition of 'permitting prayer' implies that a mere declaration is insufficient.
3
State Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that ownership ceases immediately upon the builder saying 'I have made it a mosque', even without physical separation or prayer being held. His view is based on the idea that the declaration alone dedicates the space to Allah.
The text adds 'وبالصلاة فيه' which may indicate that Abu Yusuf also requires prayer, or it may be a copyist gloss. The main dispute is about the declaration itself.
4
Explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a builder says 'this is a mosque' but does not separate it or permit prayer, under the majority view he can still sell it or revoke; under Abu Yusuf's view, it becomes a perpetual waqf and cannot be sold. This affects inheritance, transactions, and the mosque's legal status.
The practical consequence determines when the mosque is considered established for rulings like prohibition of sale, entry of non-Muslims, etc.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text references al-Dhakhira, indicating that Abu Yusuf's view is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Later Hanafi works often adopt Abu Yusuf's view as the operative ruling.
Tarjih is based on the authority of later sources like al-Dhakhira, which considers Abu Yusuf's view more practical.

Source Text

Section. 415. The book of waqf. Whoever builds a mosque, his ownership does not cease until he separates it from his ownership by his path (meaning?) and permits prayer. So if he sacrifices from it every year, it is permissible, and it is perpetual forever. Likewise, everything of this kind, the condition of the founder is observed. Just as if he vows to free his slave or to sacrifice his sheep as an udhiyah, he does not give its value in charity; rather, he must fulfill what he specified. And if he vows to give his slave in charity to the poor, or his sheep or his garment, it is permissible to give the exact item or its value. And if he endows for the needy of the people of knowledge, to buy for them clothes, ink, paper, and the like of their needs, the waqf is valid and perpetual, because knowledge has seekers until the Day of Judgment. It is permissible to observe the condition and it is permissible to give them charity from the yield itself. And if he endows to buy books and give them to the people of knowledge, then if it is ownership (tamlīk), it is permissible to give charity from the yield itself; if it is permissive use and loan, then no. A waqf on someone who recites the Quran every day: a mann of bread and a quarter of meat; the administrator may give them the value of that in paper money. He said: No. End. It agrees with what is in al-Hawi. He said in the aforementioned treatise: This indicates a prohibition of increase in stipends occurring in our time if they exceed the condition of the founders, and the judge's ruling is not effective therein. Whoever leaves the matter to the judge absolutely has introduced an innovation in the Shariah by his opinion and corrupted the religion by his poor understanding. So it is obligatory upon every judge to fear Allah, and upon every Muslim to prevent it. End. I say: It must be restricted to when the mosque is not idle due to scarcity of the stipend for the imamate. And it should be said that the disagreement is when the one who accepts the little is knowledgeable and pious. But if he is not like that, being ignorant and sinful, he is as if non-existent. And it is explicitly stated in al-Ashbah that increase is permissible, with his statement: It is permissible for the judge to increase the imam's stipend if it does not suffice him and he is knowledgeable and pious. Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling on mosque building: the builder retains ownership until he physically separates the mosque from his property and permits prayer. This is the Hanafi position. Then it discusses various waqf rulings: if a waqf stipulates a sacrifice, the actual sacrifice must be performed, not its value. For vows of charity, giving the value is allowed. For waqf for scholars, buying supplies or giving the yield is permissible depending on intent. The author then quotes a dispute about increasing the imam's stipend from mosque endowments: a judge's ruling to increase it is ineffective if it violates the founder's conditions. However, the author qualifies this: if the mosque would be idle without an imam, increase is allowed if the imam is qualified. The section concludes with Abu Yusuf's opinion that ownership of the mosque ends by merely declaring it a mosque, unlike the earlier view requiring separation and prayer permission. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; Abu Yusuf's view is the one relied upon in later practice (al-mufta bihi) as per the Dhakhira reference.

التمليك (al-tamlīk): Ownership; in waqf for books, if the beneficiary becomes owner.
الإباحة (al-ibāḥa): Permissive use; in waqf for books, if the books are only lent.
