Conditions in Waqf and Rulings on Mosque Endowments
Waqf rulings on conditions and stipend increase exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of the founder (shart al-waqif) to various waqf scenarios and identify when the administrator may deviate, including the exception for imam's stipend increase.

Core Idea
The founder's condition is binding like a text, but necessity can override when the waqf's purpose would otherwise be defeated.

This passage covers several nuanced waqf rulings: how to handle a vow for sacrifice or charity, waqf for scholars' supplies, the crucial distinction between tamlik (ownership) and ibahah (permissive use) in book endowments, and the permissibility of increasing an imam's stipend when the mosque would become idle without a qualified imam. Understanding these rulings is essential for administrators to properly fulfill the founder's intent while avoiding invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples of vows and waqfs
Examine the rulings for: (a) vow to sacrifice an animal – must sacrifice the exact animal, not its value; (b) vow to give a slave in charity – both the slave or its value are permissible; (c) waqf for scholars – purchase supplies or give yield; (d) waqf for books – depends on tamlik vs ibahah.
The general principle is that the founder's condition is followed, but for charity vows, giving value is allowed.
2
Note the principle of 'shart al-waqif' as like a text
The text states: 'هل الوصف في الموقوف عليهم كصريح الشرط' – descriptions of beneficiaries are like explicit conditions. For example, a waqf for 'Hanafi imam' cannot be given to a non-Hanafi.
This emphasizes that the founder's specification is binding and cannot be ignored arbitrarily.
3
Distinguish between tamlik and ibahah in book waqfs
If the waqf is set up as ownership (tamlik), beneficiaries own the books and can dispose of them. If it is permissive use (ibahah/loan), the books are only lent and must be returned.
This distinction is crucial for determining whether the books can be sold or passed on.
4
Analyze the stipend increase case and its exception
The text initially says a judge's ruling to increase an imam's stipend against the founder's condition is invalid. However, the author qualifies: if the mosque would be idle and the imam is knowledgeable and pious, increase is permissible (as per al-Ashbah).
This shows that necessity can override the condition when the waqf's purpose (providing imamate) would otherwise be defeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ٤١٥ كتاب الوقف ومن بنى مسجداً لم يزل ملكه عنه حتى يفرزه عن ملكه بطريقه ويأذن بالصلاة فيذبح عنه في كل سنة جاز وهو دائم أبداً، وكذا كل ما كان من هذا الجنس يراعى فيه شرط الواقف كما لو نذر بعتق عبده أو بذبح شاته أضحية لم يتصدق بقيمته وعليه الوفاء بما سمى. ولو نذر أن يتصدق بعبده على الفقراء أو شاته أو ثوبه جاز التصدق بعينه أو بقيمته، ولو وقف على محتاجي أهل العلم أن يشتري لهم الثياب والمداد والكاغد ونحوها من مصالحهم جاز الوقف وهو دائم لأن للعلوم طلاباً إلى يوم القيامة، ويجوز مراعاة الشرط ويجوز التصدق عليهم بعين الغلة ولو وقف ليشتري به الكتب ويدفع إلى أهل العلم، فإن كان تمليكاً جاز التصدق بعين الغلة وإن كان إباحة وإعارة فلا وقف على من يقرأ القرآن كل يوم. مناً من الخبز وربعاً من اللحم فللقيم أن يدفع إليهم قيمة ذلك ورقاً ولو وقف على أن يتصدق بفاضل غلة الوقف على من يسأل في مسجد كذا كل يوم فالمقيم أن يتصدق به على السؤال في غير ذلك المسجد أو خارج المسجد أو على فقير لا يسأل. قال رضي الله عنه : الأولى عندي أن يراعى في هذا الأخير شرط الواقف .اهـ. فإن قلت هل الوصف في الموقوف عليهم كصريح الشرط كما لو وقف على إمام حنفي ؟ قلت : نعم فلا يجوز تقرير غير الحنفي. قال في القنية : وقف ضيعته على أولاده الفقهاء وأولاد أولاده إن كانوا فقهاء ثم مات أحدهم عن ابن صغير تفقه بعد سنين لا يوقف نصيبه ولا يستحق قبل حصول تلك الصفة وإنما يستحق الفقيه وإن كان واحداً اهـ. والله أعلم. فصل لما اختص المسجد بأحكام تخالف أحكام مطلق الوقف أفرده بفصل على حدة وأخره المؤلف في رسالته القول النقي ناقلاً عن التتارخانية : ولو كان للإمام معلوم فزادوه وحكم بذلك حاكم هل ينفذ حكمه؟ قال : لا .اهـ. وهو موافق لما في الحاوي: قال في الرسالة المذكورة: فهذا يفيد منع الزيادة في المعاليم الواقعة في زماننا إذا كانت خارجة عن شرط الواقفين وأن حكم القاضي ليس بنافذ فيها. فمن جعل الأمر للقاضي مطلقاً فقد زاد في الشريعة برأيه وأفسد الدين بسوء فهمه فالواجب على كل حاكم روعه وعلى كل مسلم منعه .اهـ. أقول : يجب تقييده بما إذا لم يتعطل المسجد بقل المرسوم عن الإمامة وينبغي أن يكون الخلاف فيما إذا كان الذي يقبل القليل عالماً تقياً، أما من لم يكن كذلك بأن كان جاهلاً فاسقاً فهو كالعدم وقد صرح في الأشباه بجواز الزيادة بقوله تجوز الزيادة من القاضي على معلوم الإمام إذا كان لا يكفيه وكان عالماً تقياً. فصل في أحكام المساجد قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف يزول ملكه بقوله جعلته مسجداً) يعني وبالصلاة فيه ففي الذخيرة ما
Section. 415. The book of waqf. Whoever builds a mosque, his ownership does not cease until he separates it from his ownership by his path (meaning?) and permits prayer. So if he sacrifices from it every year, it is permissible, and it is perpetual forever. Likewise, everything of this kind, the condition of the founder is observed. Just as if he vows to free his slave or to sacrifice his sheep as an udhiyah, he does not give its value in charity; rather, he must fulfill what he specified. And if he vows to give his slave in charity to the poor, or his sheep or his garment, it is permissible to give the exact item or its value. And if he endows for the needy of the people of knowledge, to buy for them clothes, ink, paper, and the like of their needs, the waqf is valid and perpetual, because knowledge has seekers until the Day of Judgment. It is permissible to observe the condition and it is permissible to give them charity from the yield itself. And if he endows to buy books and give them to the people of knowledge, then if it is ownership (tamlīk), it is permissible to give charity from the yield itself; if it is permissive use and loan, then no. A waqf on someone who recites the Quran every day: a mann of bread and a quarter of meat; the administrator may give them the value of that in paper money. And if he endows to give charity from the surplus of the waqf's yield to those who ask in a certain mosque every day, the administrator may give charity to the beggars in another mosque or outside the mosque or to a poor person who does not ask. Radiyya Allahu anhu said: In my view, in this last case, the condition of the founder should be observed. End. If you ask: Is the description of the beneficiaries like an explicit condition, as if he endows for a Hanafi imam? I say: Yes, so it is not permissible to appoint a non-Hanafi. In al-Qunyah: He endowed his estate to his sons who are jurists and their sons if they are jurists; then one of them died leaving a young son who later acquired fiqh after years: his share is not suspended, nor does he become entitled before acquiring that attribute; only the jurist is entitled, even if only one. End. And Allah knows best. Section: Because the mosque has rulings that differ from the rulings of absolute waqf, the author separated it in a separate section and placed it at the end of his treatise al-Qawl al-Naqi, quoting from al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the imam has a stipend and they increased it, and a judge ruled on that, does his ruling take effect? He said: No. End. It agrees with what is in al-Hawi. He said in the aforementioned treatise: This indicates a prohibition of increase in stipends occurring in our time if they exceed the condition of the founders, and the judge's ruling is not effective therein. Whoever leaves the matter to the judge absolutely has introduced an innovation in the Shariah by his opinion and corrupted the religion by his poor understanding. So it is obligatory upon every judge to fear Allah, and upon every Muslim to prevent it. End. I say: It must be restricted to when the mosque is not idle due to scarcity of the stipend for the imamate. And it should be said that the disagreement is when the one who accepts the little is knowledgeable and pious. But if he is not like that, being ignorant and sinful, he is as if non-existent. And it is explicitly stated in al-Ashbah that increase is permissible, with his statement: It is permissible for the judge to increase the imam's stipend if it does not suffice him and he is knowledgeable and pious. Section on rulings of mosques. His statement (And Abu Yusuf said: His ownership ceases by his saying 'I have made it a mosque') means by prayer in it, so in al-Dhakhira...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling on mosque building: the builder retains ownership until he physically separates the mosque from his property and permits prayer. This is the Hanafi position. Then it discusses various waqf rulings: if a waqf stipulates a sacrifice, the actual sacrifice must be performed, not its value. For vows of charity, giving the value is allowed. For waqf for scholars, buying supplies or giving the yield is permissible depending on intent. The author then quotes a dispute about increasing the imam's stipend from mosque endowments: a judge's ruling to increase it is ineffective if it violates the founder's conditions. However, the author qualifies this: if the mosque would be idle without an imam, increase is allowed if the imam is qualified. The section concludes with Abu Yusuf's opinion that ownership of the mosque ends by merely declaring it a mosque, unlike the earlier view requiring separation and prayer permission. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; Abu Yusuf's view is the one relied upon in later practice (al-mufta bihi) as per the Dhakhira reference.

Key Terms
التمليك (al-tamlīk): Ownership; in waqf for books, if the beneficiary becomes owner.
الإباحة (al-ibāḥa): Permissive use; in waqf for books, if the books are only lent.
شرط الواقف (shart al-wāqif): Condition of the founder; binding stipulation in a waqf.
المسجد (al-masjid): Mosque; a place dedicated for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when can a judge increase an imam's stipend despite the founder's condition?
A) Never, because the founder's condition is absolute.
B) Only if the imam asks for a raise.
C) If the mosque would become idle and the imam is knowledgeable and pious.
D) Only if the founder himself agrees posthumously.

Key Takeaway
The founder's condition is binding, but necessity can override when the waqf's purpose would otherwise be defeated, as seen in the imam's stipend exception.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Building a Mosque and Conditions for Its Perpetuity
Rulings on building a mosque and various endowment conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a mosque to become a perpetual waqf according to the Hanafi school and apply the rule that the endower's conditions are binding.

Core Idea
A mosque becomes waqf only when the owner separates it and permits prayer; the endower's conditions are binding.

In the Hanafi school, building a mosque does not automatically remove the property from the owner's ownership. Two conditions must be fulfilled for it to become a perpetual waqf. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies these conditions and then explores how the endower's conditions (shart al-wāqif) govern the administration of the endowment. Understanding these nuances is crucial for the proper establishment and management of mosques and other endowments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The text begins with the rule that building a mosque does not automatically transfer ownership. The owner retains ownership until specific conditions are met.
This is the starting point: construction alone is insufficient.
2
List the two conditions for consecration
The owner must (1) separate the property from his estate by designating a boundary or path (tfrīz), and (2) permit at least one person to pray in it (idhn). Only then does the mosque become a perpetual waqf.
Both conditions must be fulfilled; one without the other is insufficient.
3
Understand the effect of fulfillment
Once a person prays with the owner's permission, the property is dedicated to Allah eternally. Ownership ceases and the mosque cannot be reverted or sold.
The consequence is irrevocable perpetuity.
4
Apply the principle of shart al-wāqif
The passage expands to general waqf rules: the endower's conditions must be observed. Examples include endowments for specific categories (scholars, Hanafi imams) and details like providing food or cash.
Conditions that do not contradict a legal maxim are binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ومن بنى مسجداً لم يزل ملكه عنه حتى يفرزه عن ملكه بطريقه ويأذن بالصلاة فيذبح عنه في كل سنة جاز وهو دائم أبداً، وكذا كل ما كان من هذا الجنس يراعى فيه شرط الواقف كما لو نذر بعتق عبده أو بذبح شاته أضحية لم يتصدق بقيمته وعليه الوفاء بما سمى. ولو نذر أن يتصدق بعبده على الفقراء أو شاته أو ثوبه جاز التصدق بعينه أو بقيمته، ولو وقف على محتاجي أهل العلم أن يشتري لهم الثياب والمداد والكاغد ونحوها من مصالحهم جاز الوقف وهو دائم لأن للعلوم طلاباً إلى يوم القيامة، ويجوز مراعاة الشرط ويجوز التصدق عليهم بعين الغلة ولو وقف ليشتري به الكتب ويدفع إلى أهل العلم، فإن كان تمليكاً جاز التصدق بعين الغلة وإن كان إباحة وإعارة فلا وقف على من يقرأ القرآن كل يوم مناً من الخبز وربعاً من اللحم فللقيم أن يدفع إليهم قيمة ذلك ورقاً ولو وقف على أن يتصدق بفاضل غلة الوقف على من يسأل في مسجد كذا كل يوم فالمقيم أن يتصدق به على السؤال في غير ذلك المسجد أو خارج المسجد أو على فقير لا يسأل. قال رضي الله عنه : الأولى عندي أن يراعى في هذا الأخير شرط الواقف .اهـ. فإن قلت هل الوصف في الموقوف عليهم كصريح الشرط كما لو وقف على إمام حنفي ؟ قلت : نعم فلا يجوز تقرير غير الحنفي. قال في القنية : وقف ضيعته على أولاده الفقهاء وأولاد أولاده إن كانوا فقهاء ثم مات أحدهم عن ابن صغير تفقه بعد سنين لا يوقف نصيبه ولا يستحق قبل حصول تلك الصفة وإنما يستحق الفقيه وإن كان واحداً اهـ. والله أعلم.
Section: And whoever builds a mosque, his ownership does not cease from it until he separates it from his ownership in his way and permits prayer in it. If he slaughters [an animal] for it every year, it is permissible, and it is perpetual forever. Similarly, everything of this kind is observed according to the condition of the endower, just as if he vowed to free his slave or to slaughter his sheep as a sacrifice, he does not give charity of its value, and he must fulfill what he named. And if he vows to give charity of his slave to the poor, or his sheep, or his garment, it is permissible to give charity of the specific item or its value. And if he endows upon the needy of the people of knowledge to buy them clothes, ink, paper, and the like of their needs, the endowment is permissible and it is perpetual because the sciences have students until the Day of Resurrection. It is permissible to observe the condition, and it is permissible to give charity to them from the specific yield. And if he endows to buy books with it and give them to the people of knowledge, then if it is ownership, it is permissible to give charity from the specific yield, but if it is permission and lending, then no. An endowment upon one who recites the Qur'an every day of a maund of bread and a quarter of meat: the administrator may give them its value in cash. And if he endows that he give charity from the surplus yield of the endowment upon those who ask in a certain mosque every day, the administrator may give charity from it to the askers in a different mosque, or outside the mosque, or to a poor person who does not ask. He (may Allah be pleased with him) said: In my view, the preferred approach in this last case is to observe the condition of the endower. Then if you ask: Is the description of the beneficiaries like an explicit condition, such as endowing upon a Hanafi imam? I say: Yes, so it is not permissible to appoint a non-Hanafi. He said in al-Qunyah: He endowed his estate upon his sons who are jurists and his grandsons if they are jurists, then one of them died leaving a young son who studied jurisprudence after years: his share is not suspended and he does not deserve before acquiring that description; rather, the jurist deserves even if he is one. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It opens with the rule that building a mosque does not remove the owner's ownership until he separates the plot from his other property by a designated boundary and permits people to pray in it. Once one person prays, the mosque becomes a perpetual waqf. This is a key condition: without separation and permission, the building remains the owner's property. The text then addresses related issues: if someone makes a vow to sacrifice an animal from the mosque's income, he must fulfill it by actual slaughter, not pay its value. Similarly, for vows of charity, the donor may give either the specific item or its value. Endowments for the benefit of scholars (e.g., buying supplies) are valid and perpetual because knowledge will always be sought. The administrator may give the actual produce or its value depending on the type of endowment. If the endowment is to provide food to Qur'an reciters, the administrator may pay cash. A nuanced ruling: if the endowment specifies giving surplus to askers of a particular mosque, the administrator may give to askers elsewhere or to needy non-askers, but the commentator (possibly al-Haskafi) prefers adhering to the endower's condition. The text further clarifies that descriptive conditions (like 'Hanafi imam') are binding; a non-Hanafi cannot be appointed. Finally, an example from al-Qunyah: if an estate is endowed on jurist sons and grandchildren who are jurists, a young son who later becomes a jurist does not inherit the share retroactively; only those who are jurists at the time of distribution benefit.

Key Terms
مسجد (masjid): A place dedicated for prayer that becomes a perpetual waqf upon fulfillment of conditions.
وقف (waqf): An endowment where the corpus is preserved and the benefit is given perpetually.
شرط الواقف (shart al-wāqif): The condition set by the endower that must be observed in the administration of the waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two essential conditions for a mosque to become a perpetual waqf according to the Hanafi school?
A) Building the mosque and hiring an imam
B) Separating the property from ownership and permitting prayer
C) Registration with the judge and public announcement
D) Donating a copy of the Qur'an and installing a minbar

Key Takeaway
A mosque becomes a perpetual waqf only after the owner separates the property and permits prayer; all conditions set by the endower are binding.

Waqf — Endowment

When a Mosque Becomes Waqf: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Taslim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of prayer (taslim) for mosque waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on when a mosque becomes a valid waqf, and explain the mufta-bihi view requiring congregational prayer.

Core Idea
A mosque becomes waqf only through prayer (taslim), not mere declaration, but the required number of worshippers differs among the imams.

This lesson explores a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the consecration of a mosque. While all Hanafi authorities agree that a mosque waqf is distinct from general waqf, they differ on whether mere declaration suffices or whether prayer (and how many participants) is necessary. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi method of legal reasoning (talil) and the concept of taslim for non-transferable properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The central question is: When does a mosque become a valid waqf, i.e., ownership transferred to Allah? The dispute revolves around the requirement of taslim (delivery).
2
State Abu Hanifah's Position
Abu Hanifah requires separation (ifraz) of the property from one's ownership and permission to pray, followed by at least one person praying. He suffices with a single worshipper.
Rationale: delivery of a mosque is achieved by prayer, its intended purpose.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's Position
Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifah on the need for prayer but insists on congregational prayer (jamāʿah) because the mosque is built for that purpose.
Al-Zayla'i affirmed this as the sounder view.
4
State Abu Yusuf's Position
Abu Yusuf holds that mere declaration 'I have made it a mosque' suffices; no prayer is needed. He analogizes waqf to emancipation (ʿitq), which requires no delivery.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, with congregational prayer being the operative condition, as adopted by later Hanafi authorities like al-Zayla'i.
This resolves the dispute in favor of a stronger requirement for consecration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل لما اختص المسجد بأحكام تخالف أحكام مطلق الوقف أفرده بفصل على حدة وأخره المؤلف في رسالته القول النقي ناقلاً عن التتارخانية : ولو كان للإمام معلوم فزادوه وحكم بذلك حاكم هل ينفذ حكمه؟ قال : لا .اهـ. وهو موافق لما في الحاوي: قال في الرسالة المذكورة: فهذا يفيد منع الزيادة في المعاليم الواقعة في زماننا إذا كانت خارجة عن شرط الواقفين وأن حكم القاضي ليس بنافذ فيها. فمن جعل الأمر للقاضي مطلقاً فقد زاد في الشريعة برأيه وأفسد الدين بسوء فهمه فالواجب على كل حاكم روعه وعلى كل مسلم منعه .اهـ. أقول : يجب تقييده بما إذا لم يتعطل المسجد بقل المرسوم عن الإمامة وينبغي أن يكون الخلاف فيما إذا كان الذي يقبل القليل عالماً تقياً، أما من لم يكن كذلك بأن كان جاهلاً فاسقاً فهو كالعدم وقد صرح في الأشباه بجواز الزيادة بقوله تجوز الزيادة من القاضي على معلوم الإمام إذا كان لا يكفيه وكان عالماً تقياً. فصل في أحكام المساجد قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف يزول ملكه بقوله جعلته مسجداً) يعني وبالصلاة فيه ففي الذخيرة ما فيه فإذا صلى فيه واحد زال ملكه ومن جعل مسجداً تحته سرداب أو فوقه بيت وجعل بحسب في ما قوله : (ومن بنى مسجداً لم يزل ملكه عنه حتى يفرزه عن ملكه بطريقه ويأذن بالصلاة فيه وإذا صلى فيه واحد زال ملكه أما الإفراز فإنه لا يخلص الله تعالى إلا به، وأما الصلاة فيه فلأنه لا بد من التسليم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فيشترط تسليم نوعه وذلك في المسجد بالصلاة فيه أو لأنه لما تعذر القبض يقام تحقق المقصود مقامه، ثم يكتفي بصلاة الواحد لأن فعل الجنس يتعذر فيشترط أدناه. وعن محمد تشترط الصلاة بالجماعة لأن المسجد لذلك مبني الغالب. وصححها الزيلعي تبعاً لما في الخانية لأن قبض كل شيء وتسليمه يكون يليق به وذلك في المسجد بأداء الصلاة بالجماعة، أما الواحد يصلي في كل مكان. وقال أبو يوسف : يزول ملكه بقوله جعلته مسجداً لأن التسليم عنده ليس بشرط لأنه إسقاط لملك العبد فيصير خالصاً لله تعالى بسقوط حق العبد وصار كالإعتاق والحاصل أن المسجد مخالف لمطلق الوقف عند الكل، أما عند الأول فلا يشترط القضاء ولا التعليق بالموت، وأما عند الثاني فلا يجوز في المشاع، وأما عند الثالث فلا يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي. أطلق الواحد فشمل الباني وهو قول البعض والأصح أنه لا يكفي لأن الصلاة إنما تشترط لأجل القبض على العامة وقبضه لا يكفي فكذا صلاته ؛ كذا في الخانية. وشمل ما إذا صلى واحد بغير أذان وإقامه وهو ظاهر الرواية؛ كذا في الخانية. ولو قال المصنف رحمه الله ومن جعل أرضه مسجداً بدل قوله ومن بنى لكان أولى لأنه لو كان له ساحة لا بناء فيها فأمر قومه أن يصلوا فيها بجماعة قالوا: إن أمرهم بالصلاة فيها أبداً أو أمرهم بالصلاة فيها بالجماعة ولم يذكر أبداً إلا أنه أراد بها الأبد ثم مات لا يكون ميراثاً عنه وإن أمرهم بالصلاة شهراً أو سنة ثم مات تكون ميراثاً عنه لأنه لا بد من التأبيد والتوقيت ينافي التأبيد؛ كذا في الخانية. وأفاد باشتراط الصلاة فيه أنه لو بنى مسجدا وسلمه إلى المتولي لا مسجداً يصير بالتسليم إلى المتولي وهو قول البعض واختاره شمس الأئمة السرخسي لأن قبض كل شيء يكون بما يليق به كقبض الخان يكون بنزول واحد من المارة فيه بإذنه، وفي الحوض والبئر والسقاية بالاستقاء . وقال بعضهم : يصير مسجداً كسائر الأوقاف ؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي فتح القدير : والوجه الصحة لأن بالتسليم إلى المتولي أيضاً يحصل تمام التسليم إليه تعالى لرفع يده عنه فكأنه لم يطلع على تصحيح. وفي الاختيار : والصحيح أنه يصير مسجداً وكذا إذا سلمه إلى القاضي أو نائبه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف. وقيد بإذن الباني لأن متولي المسجد إذا جعل المنزل الموقوف على المسجد مسجداً وصلى فيه سنين ثم ترك الصلاة فيه وأعيد منزلاً مستغلاً جاز لأن المتولي وإن نصه : وبالصلاة بجماعة يقع التسليم بلا خلاف حتى أنه إذا بنى مسجداً وأذن للناس بالصلاة فيه جماعة فإنه يصير مسجداً قوله : (وأفاد الخ) دفع هذا في النهر بأن الصلاة فيه نائبة عن تسليمه إلى المتولي فإذا صار مسجداً بالنائب فبالأصل وهو التسليم أولى فليراجع .
Section: Since the mosque is distinguished by rulings that differ from general waqf rulings, he devoted a separate section to it and the author in his treatise al-Qawl al-Naqi, quoting from al-Tatarkhaniyyah: 'If the imam has a known stipend and they increased it and a judge ruled accordingly, is his ruling enforceable? He said: No.' This is in agreement with what is in al-Hawi. He said in the mentioned treatise: 'This indicates the prohibition of increasing the stipends occurring in our time if they are outside the condition of the endowers, and that the judge's ruling is not effective in it. Whoever gives the matter absolutely to the judge has added to the Shari'ah by his opinion and corrupted the religion by his poor understanding. So it is obligatory upon every judge to fear, and upon every Muslim to prevent it.' I say: It must be restricted to when the mosque is not paralyzed by the scarcity of the assigned amount for the imamate, and the dispute should be regarding one who accepts little while being a knowledgeable and pious person. As for one who is not like that, being ignorant and sinful, he is like non-existent. And it has been explicitly stated in al-Ashbah that it is permissible for the judge to increase the imam's stipend when it is insufficient for him and he is knowledgeable and pious. Section on the rulings of mosques. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said: His ownership ceases by his statement 'I have made it a mosque') meaning, and with prayer in it. In al-Dhakhirah: So when one person prays in it, his ownership ceases. And whoever makes a mosque with a basement or a room above it, and makes... accordingly. His statement: (And whoever builds a mosque, his ownership does not cease from it until he separates it from his ownership in his way and permits prayer in it, and when one person prays in it, his ownership ceases.) As for separation, it is not sincerely for Allah except through it. As for prayer in it, because delivery (taslim) is necessary according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, so the delivery of its type is required, and that in the mosque is by prayer in it, or because when physical possession is impossible, the realization of the objective is substituted for it. Then one prayer suffices because the action of the species is impossible, so the lowest is required. And from Muhammad, prayer in congregation is required because the mosque is built for that generally. Al-Zayla'i affirmed it following what is in al-Khaniyyah, because possession and delivery of everything is by what is fitting for it, and that in the mosque is by performing congregational prayer, while one person prays everywhere. Abu Yusuf said: His ownership ceases by his statement 'I have made it a mosque' because delivery is not a condition according to him, since it is a relinquishment of the slave's ownership, so it becomes purely for Allah by the dropping of the slave's right, and it became like emancipation. The summary: The mosque differs from absolute waqf according to all. As for the first (Abu Hanifah), judgeship and suspension upon death are not required. As for the second (Abu Yusuf), it is not permissible in undivided shares. As for the third (Muhammad), delivery to the trustee is not required. He generalized 'one' so it includes the builder – that is the opinion of some, but the correct view is that it does not suffice because prayer is only required for the possession by the general public, and his possession does not count, so neither does his prayer. This is from al-Khaniyyah. And it includes the case where one person prays without adhan or iqamah, which is the apparent transmission; similarly from al-Khaniyyah. And if the author (may Allah have mercy on him) had said 'And whoever makes his land a mosque' instead of his statement 'And whoever builds,' it would have been better because if he has a courtyard with no building in it and he orders his people to pray in it in congregation, they said: If he orders them to pray in it forever, or orders them to pray in it in congregation without mentioning forever but he intends perpetuity, then he dies, it is not inherited from him. But if he orders them to pray for a month or a year and then dies, it is inherited from him because perpetuity is necessary and timing contradicts perpetuity. This is from al-Khaniyyah. And it benefits from the condition of prayer that if he builds a mosque and hands it over to the trustee, it does not become a mosque by handing over to the trustee – this is the opinion of some, but Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi chose it because possession of everything is by what is fitting for it, like possession of a caravanserai is by the lodging of one passer-by with his permission, and in the case of a pond, well, and water trough, by drawing water. And some said: It becomes a mosque like other endowments; this is from al-Khaniyyah. And in Fath al-Qadir: The correct view is sound because by handing over to the trustee, full delivery to Allah is also achieved by removing his hand from it, as if he was not aware of the correction. And in al-Ikhtiyar: The correct view is that it becomes a mosque, and likewise if he hands it over to the judge or his deputy; this is from al-Is'af. And it is restricted by the permission of the builder because if the trustee of the mosque makes the house endowed to the mosque into a mosque and prays in it for years, then leaves prayer in it and it is returned as a rented house, it is permissible because the trustee... His text: By congregational prayer, delivery occurs without disagreement, to the extent that if he builds a mosque and permits the people to pray in it in congregation, it becomes a mosque. He said: (And it benefits...) This is refuted in al-Nahr by saying that prayer therein is a substitute for handing it over to the trustee; if it becomes a mosque by the substitute, then by the original, which is handing over, it is even more appropriate. So let it be reviewed.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the conditions for a mosque to become a valid waqf. It begins with a discussion on the permissibility of increasing an imam's stipend, then moves to the core issue: when does a mosque become consecrated? The three imams differ on the requirement of delivery (taslim). Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani maintain that delivery of a mosque is achieved by prayer, not by the builder's mere declaration. Abu Hanifah accepts prayer by a single person, while Muhammad insists on congregational prayer because that is the mosque's purpose. Abu Yusuf holds that the builder's statement 'I have made it a mosque' suffices, analogizing it to emancipation which requires no delivery. The text weighs these views: it notes that the majority of later scholars (e.g., al-Zayla'i) prefer congregational prayer as the operative condition. Several subsidiary points are discussed: if a person prays without adhan or iqamah, it still counts; if someone designates land without a building for congregational prayer with perpetual intent, it becomes a mosque; if the builder hands the mosque to a trustee instead of opening it for prayer, there is disagreement – some (like al-Sarakhsi) say it does not become a mosque, while others (in Fath al-Qadir, al-Ikhtiyar) accept the handover to the trustee as sufficient. The passage also clarifies that if the trustee of an existing mosque converts a rented house into a mosque and later abandons it, the mosque status may revert. The final comment from al-Nahr argues that since prayer is a substitute for handover, the original handover should suffice even more, but this is debated.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery or handing over of the waqf property to the beneficiaries or to the trustee; in the case of a mosque, it is achieved by prayer.
إمام (imām): The leader of prayer; in the context of mosques, the person appointed to lead prayers and often receiving stipends from waqf.
جماعة (jamāʿah): Congregational prayer; required by Muhammad for the consecration of a mosque, though Abu Hanifah suffices with a single person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a mosque to become a valid waqf?
A) Only the owner's declaration 'I make it a mosque'
B) Separation of the property and permission to pray, followed by at least one person praying
C) Registration with the judge and appointment of an imam
D) Building a minaret and a mihrab

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school predominantly holds that a mosque becomes waqf only through prayer, with congregational prayer being the operative condition as per later authorities.

Conditions for Mosque and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining three conditions for a mosque and intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for a place to become a mosque according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explain the disagreement of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A mosque becomes a mosque only when prayer is performed; mere words are insufficient.

Making a place a mosque is not simply a verbal declaration. The Hanafi school specifies concrete conditions to ensure the site is exclusively dedicated to Allah. This lesson unpacks those conditions and the scholarly disagreement within the school, especially the view of Abu Yusuf that utterance alone suffices. Understanding this dispute clarifies the legal nature of waqf and the role of delivery (taslim).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
Identify the three conditions: disengagement (ifrāz), permission (idhn), and actual prayer (salāh) by at least one person. This is the majority view.
Note: The builder's own prayer does not count.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi opponent (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds that mere utterance ('I make this a mosque') suffices; no prayer or delivery is needed.
He analogizes it to manumission (isqat).
3
Follow the proofs
The majority relies on the necessity of delivery (taslim) for waqf; for a mosque, appropriate delivery is prayer because physical possession (qabd) is impossible. Abu Yusuf denies that delivery is a condition.
Al-Zayla'i preferred congregational prayer as the standard.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If one only declares without praying, the place is not a mosque according to the majority; if one prays without disengaging, it also fails. Under Abu Yusuf, declaration alone suffices.
This affects inheritance and legal status.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position requires prayer, with preference for congregation per al-Zayla'i. Abu Yusuf's view is considered weak.
Source: al-Khaniya and al-Zayla'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن بنى مسجداً لم يزل ملكه عنه حتى يفرزه عن ملكه بطريقه ويأذن بالصلاة فيه وإذا صلى فيه واحد زال ملكه أما الإفراز فإنه لا يخلص الله تعالى إلا به، وأما الصلاة فيه فلأنه لا بد من التسليم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فيشترط تسليم نوعه وذلك في المسجد بالصلاة فيه أو لأنه لما تعذر القبض يقام تحقق المقصود مقامه، ثم يكتفي بصلاة الواحد لأن فعل الجنس يتعذر فيشترط أدناه. وعن محمد تشترط الصلاة بالجماعة لأن المسجد لذلك مبني الغالب. وصححها الزيلعي تبعاً لما في الخانية لأن قبض كل شيء وتسليمه يكون يليق به وذلك في المسجد بأداء الصلاة بالجماعة، أما الواحد يصلي في كل مكان. وقال أبو يوسف : يزول ملكه بقوله جعلته مسجداً لأن التسليم عنده ليس بشرط لأنه إسقاط لملك العبد فيصير خالصاً لله تعالى بسقوط حق العبد وصار كالإعتاق والحاصل أن المسجد مخالف لمطلق الوقف عند الكل، أما عند الأول فلا يشترط القضاء ولا التعليق بالموت، وأما عند الثاني فلا يجوز في المشاع، وأما عند الثالث فلا يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي. أطلق الواحد فشمل الباني وهو قول البعض والأصح أنه لا يكفي لأن الصلاة إنما تشترط لأجل القبض على العامة وقبضه لا يكفي فكذا صلاته ؛ كذا في الخانية. وشمل ما إذا صلى واحد بغير أذان وإقامه وهو ظاهر الرواية؛ كذا في الخانية. ولو قال المصنف رحمه الله ومن جعل أرضه مسجداً بدل قوله ومن بنى لكان أولى لأنه لو كان له ساحة لا بناء فيها فأمر قومه أن يصلوا فيها بجماعة قالوا: إن أمرهم بالصلاة فيها أبداً أو أمرهم بالصلاة فيها بالجماعة ولم يذكر أبداً إلا أنه أراد بها الأبد ثم مات لا يكون ميراثاً عنه وإن أمرهم بالصلاة شهراً أو سنة ثم مات تكون ميراثاً عنه لأنه لا بد من التأبيد والتوقيت ينافي التأبيد؛ كذا في الخانية.
His statement: (Whoever builds a mosque, his ownership does not leave him until he separates it from his ownership by its way and permits prayer in it, and when one person prays in it, his ownership ceases. As for separation, it is not valid for Allah except by it. As for prayer in it, because delivery is necessary according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, so delivery of its type is required, and that in a mosque is by prayer in it, or because when possession is difficult, the achievement of the objective takes its place. Then one person's prayer suffices because the act of the genus is difficult, so its minimum is required. From Muhammad, congregational prayer is required because the mosque is mostly built for that. Al-Zayla'i validated it following what is in al-Khaniya, because possession and delivery of each thing is appropriate to it, and that in a mosque is by performing congregational prayer, whereas an individual can pray anywhere. Abu Yusuf said: his ownership ceases by his saying 'I made it a mosque' because delivery is not a condition in his view, since it is a release of the slave's ownership, so it becomes purely for Allah by the removal of the slave's right, and it is like manumission. The gist is that a mosque differs from absolute waqf according to all: according to the first, neither court order nor suspension on death is required; according to the second, it is not permissible in undivided shares; according to the third, delivery to the trustee is not required. He used the general term 'one person' which includes the builder – that is the view of some, but the correct view is that it is not sufficient because prayer is only required for taking possession from the public, and his possession is not sufficient, so likewise his prayer. So in al-Khaniya. And it includes the case where one person prays without the call to prayer and establishment – that is the apparent narration. So in al-Khaniya. If the author had said: 'Whoever makes his land a mosque' instead of 'Whoever builds', it would be better, because if he owns a courtyard with no building and commands his people to pray there in congregation – they said: If he commanded them to pray there forever, or commanded them to pray there in congregation without mentioning forever but intended forever, then he dies, it is not inherited from him. If he commanded them to pray for a month or a year then dies, it is inherited from him, because perpetuity is necessary and timing contradicts perpetuity. So in al-Khaniya.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the legal conditions for a place to become a mosque in Hanafi fiqh. The author first states the ruling: the builder's ownership does not cease until three conditions are met: (1) disengagement of the site from his ownership by a proper boundary, (2) permission to pray, and (3) actual prayer by one person. The commentary then explains the rationale: disengagement is necessary because the place must be exclusively for Allah; prayer serves as the appropriate mode of delivery (taslim) for a mosque, since physical possession is not possible. Per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, one person's prayer suffices, though there is a narration from Muhammad requiring congregational prayer. Al-Zayla'i preferred the latter because mosque possession appropriately occurs through collective prayer. Abu Yusuf held that mere utterance ("I made it a mosque") suffices, analogizing to manumission. The passage then clarifies that the builder's own prayer does not count, because the purpose of prayer is to effect possession from the public. It also notes that prayer without adhan is sufficient. Finally, it critiques the matn's wording: using 'builds' is too narrow; making land a mosque without a building also requires perpetual intention, not a temporary one.

Key Terms
إفراز (ifrāz): Disengagement of a specific portion of property from one's general ownership by demarcation (e.g., setting a boundary).
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery or surrender of the property to the beneficiaries or to the designated recipient (for waqf).
قبض (qabḍ): Possession or taking hold of the property; for a mosque, since physical possession is not possible, prayer serves as its substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which of the following is a necessary condition for a place to become a mosque?
A) The builder must recite a specific declaration.
B) At least one person must pray in it with permission.
C) The place must be built with a minaret.
D) A judge must officially declare it a mosque.

Key Takeaway
A place becomes a mosque only when it is physically separated from ownership, permission is given, and actual prayer (preferably in congregation) is performed — mere words do not suffice.

Surrender to Trustee and Conditions for Mosque Validity
Ruling with proof on surrender to trustee and additional mosque rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether surrender to a trustee suffices to make a mosque, and identify the conditions required for a valid mosque waqf.

Core Idea
Surrender to the trustee of a mosque makes it valid – custom equates to explicit declaration.

This passage discusses a critical issue in mosque waqf: does surrendering the building to a trustee (mutawalli) without any prayer make it a mosque? The Hanafi school has an internal difference, but the later preferred view accepts surrender to the trustee. This lesson will also cover conditions derived from custom, the role of land ownership, and rights of third parties like pre-emptors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The text presents two views: (a) surrender to trustee alone does NOT make it a mosque (Sarakhsi’s view) and (b) it DOES become a mosque (preferred later view). Understand the reasoning for each.
Sarakhsi analogizes to caravanserai (possession by stay) and well (by drawing water).
2
Follow the debate and preferred view
Trace the arguments: later authorities (Fath al-Qadir, al-Ikhtiyar) accept surrender to trustee or judge as sufficient. Note that congregational prayer is an undisputed method.
The text says prayer is a substitute; surrender is even stronger.
3
Extract the conditions for mosque validity
Three conditions are implicit: (1) disengagement (takhliyah) – vacating the place, (2) permission to pray generally, and (3) actual prayer or a sufficient substitute (surrender to trustee).
No verbal formula like 'I have endowed' is needed; custom suffices.
4
Apply to related rulings
Consider mosques for funeral/Eid prayer: they are given partial mosque rulings. Land ownership is a condition; if the land is not owned, the sultan's order is ineffective. Pre-emption and reclamation rights survive.
The passage emphasizes that mosque does not cancel third-party rights.
5
Identify the dalil (evidence)
The proof for validity without explicit formula is custom (urf): people act on permission and vacating, which is equivalent to speech, as shown in the examples of food and scattering money.
Hanafi relies on custom (zanni thubut and dalala).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تعالى لرفع يده عنه فكأنه لم يطلع على تصحيح. وفي الاختيار : والصحيح أنه يصير مسجداً وكذا إذا سلمه إلى القاضي أو نائبه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف. وقيد بإذن الباني لأن متولي المسجد إذا جعل المنزل الموقوف على قوله : (وأفاد الخ) دفع هذا في النهر بأن الصلاة فيه نائبة عن تسليمه إلى المتولي فإذا صار مسجداً بالنائب فبالأصل وهو التسليم أولى فليراجع .  كتاب الوقف ٤١٧ عن جعله مسجداً لا مسجداً؛ كذا يصير في الخانية. بعضهم : ما اتخذ لصلاة الجنازة فهو مسجد لا يورث عنه، وما اتخذ لصلاة العيد لا يكون مسجداً مطلقاً وإنما يعطى له حكم المسجد في صحة الاقتداء بالإمام وإن كان منفصلاً الصفوف، وأما فيما سوى ذلك فليس له حكم المسجد، وقال بعضهم : له حكم المسجد حال أداء الصلاة لا غير وهو والجبانة سواء، ويجنب هذا المكان كما يجنب المسجد احتياطاً اهـ. فأفاد بالاقتصار على الشروط الثلاثة أنه لا يحتاج في جعله مسجداً إلى قوله «وقفته» ونحوه لأن العرف جار بالإذن في الصلاة على وجه العموم والتخلية بكونه وقفاً على هذه الجهة فكان كالتعبير به فكان كمن قدم طعاماً إلى ضيفه أو نثر نثاراً كان إذناً في أكله والتقاطه بخلاف الوقف على الفقراء لم تجر عادة فيه بالتخلية والإذن بالاستغلال، ولو جرت به في عرف اكتفينا بذلك كمسألتنا، وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد خلافاً للشافعي. وأفاد أيضاً أنه لو قال وقفته مسجداً ولم يأذن بالصلاة فيه ولم يصل فيه أحد لا يصير مسجدا بلا حكم وهو بعيد . ذكر في فتح القدير أن هذا مقتضى كلامهم ولم يعزه إلى النقل. وفي الحاوي القدسي : ومن بنى مسجداً في أرض مملوكة له إلى آخره فأفاد أن من شرطه ملك الأرض ولذا قال في الخانية : ولو أن سلطاناً أذن لقوم أن يجعلوا أرضاً من أراضي البلدة حوانيت موقوفة على المسجد أو أمرهم أن يزيدوا في مسجدهم قالوا : إن كانت البلدة فتحت عنوة وذلك لا يضر بالمارة والناس ينفذ أمر السلطان فيها، وإن كانت البلدة فتحت صلحاً لا ينفذ أمر السلطان لأن في الأول تصير ملكاً للغانمين فجاز أمر السلطان فيها، وفي الثاني تبقى على ملك ملاكها فلا ينفذ أمره فيها .اهـ. ولذا قالوا لو اشترى داراً لها شفيع فجعلها مسجداً كان للشفيع أن يأخذها بالشفعة، وكذا إذا كان للبائع حق الاسترداد كان له أن يبطل المسجد؛ كذا في فتح القدير.
And he derived from the condition of prayer in it that if he built a mosque and surrendered it to the trustee, it does not become a mosque by surrender to the trustee – that is the view of some, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose it because possession of each thing is by what is appropriate to it, like possession of a caravanserai is by the stay of one passerby with permission, and for a cistern, well, and water trough, by drawing water. Some said: it becomes a mosque like other endowments. So in al-Khaniya. In Fath al-Qadir: the sound view is validity because by surrender to the trustee, complete surrender to Allah is also achieved by his removal of his hand, so it is as if he did not see the correction. In al-Ikhtiyar: the correct view is that it becomes a mosque, and likewise if he surrenders it to the judge or his deputy. So in al-Is'af. And it is conditioned on the builder's permission, because if the trustee of a mosque makes the house endowed to the mosque into a mosque and prays in it for years, then stops praying in it and it is returned to a rented house, it is permissible because the trustee... and his text: 'By congregational prayer, delivery occurs without dispute; so if he builds a mosque and permits people to pray in it in congregation, it becomes a mosque.' His statement: (and he derived...) al-Nahr refuted this by saying that prayer in it is a substitute for surrender to the trustee; if it becomes a mosque by the substitute, then by the original (surrender) it is more appropriate. So review. Page 417: Book of Waqf: regarding making it a mosque – it does not become a mosque; so in al-Khaniya. And he used the unqualified term mosque, so it includes one made for funeral prayer or Eid prayer. In al-Khaniya: a mosque taken for funeral prayer or for Eid prayer – does it have the ruling of a mosque? The mashayikh differed. Some said: it is a mosque, so if he dies it is not inherited. Some said: that taken for funeral prayer is a mosque, not inherited; that taken for Eid prayer is not an absolute mosque, but it is given the ruling of a mosque regarding the validity of following the imam even if the rows are separated; other than that it does not have the ruling of a mosque. Some said: it has the ruling of a mosque only during the performance of prayer, and it is like a graveyard, and this place is avoided just as the mosque is avoided out of precaution. End. So he derived from confining to three conditions that in making it a mosque, he does not need to say 'I have endowed it' etc., because custom operates with permission to pray in general and vacating it as an endowment for this purpose, so it is like an expression, like one who presents food to a guest or throws scattering is permission to eat and pick up, unlike endowment on the poor where custom does not run with vacating and permission for exploitation. If it ran in custom, we would suffice with that, as in our issue. By our statement, Malik and Ahmad said, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And he also derived that if he said 'I have endowed it as a mosque' and did not permit prayer in it and no one prayed in it, it does not become a mosque without a ruling – and that is remote. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that this is the import of their statements, but he did not attribute it to narration. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'Whoever builds a mosque on land owned by him' etc., so he derived that one of its conditions is ownership of the land. For that reason, it is said in al-Khaniya: If a sultan permits people to make land from the lands of the town into shops endowed to the mosque, or orders them to increase in their mosque, they said: If the town was conquered by force and that does not harm the passersby and people, the sultan's order is effective therein. If the town was conquered peacefully, the sultan's order is not effective because in the first case it becomes property of the conquerors, so the sultan's order is permissible; in the second case it remains the property of its owners, so his order is not effective. End. For that reason they said: If one buys a house with a pre-emptor and makes it a mosque, the pre-emptor can take it by pre-emption. Similarly, if the seller has a right of reclamation, he can nullify the mosque. So in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on mosque waqf, addressing several additional issues. First, it discusses whether surrendering the mosque to a trustee (mutawalli) without any prayer suffices to make it a mosque. Al-Sarakhsi and some scholars say no, because each type of property requires its appropriate mode of possession – for a mosque, prayer; for a caravanserai, one traveler staying; for a well, drawing water. Others say yes, like other endowments. The preferred view in later works is that it does become a mosque, even by surrender to the judge. The commentary then notes that prayer in congregation is undisputed. Next, it discusses mosques built specifically for funeral or Eid prayer: scholars differ on whether they have full mosque rulings – some treat them as full mosques, some only for the prayer act. Finally, it states that the three conditions (disengagement, permission, prayer) suffice; no verbal formula like 'I have endowed' is needed, because custom of allowing prayer and vacating the place acts as an implicit expression. However, land ownership is a necessary condition: the builder must own the land. If the land was conquered peacefully, the sultan cannot force it into a mosque. Also, if the property had a pre-emptor or the seller had a right of reclamation, making it a mosque does not cancel those rights.

Key Terms
متولي (mutawallī): Trustee or administrator of a waqf, responsible for managing the property.
شفعة (shuf‘a): Pre-emption right: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property before others.
إسترداد (istirdād): Right of the seller to reclaim the property if the buyer fails to fulfill conditions (e.g., in a sale with right of reclamation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Ikhtiyar, what happens if a person builds a mosque and surrenders it to a trustee without anyone praying?
A) It does not become a mosque until someone prays.
B) It becomes a mosque because surrender to the trustee suffices.
C) It becomes a mosque only if the trustee prays.
D) It becomes a mosque only if the builder prays.

Key Takeaway
A mosque waqf is valid by surrender to the trustee, relying on custom, provided the land is owned and no third-party rights are violated.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
10 min
The Three Core Conditions for a Place to Become a Mosque
Ruling statement on conditions and custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi conditions for a place to become a mosque and explain why custom suffices for permission.

Core Idea
A place becomes a mosque by ownership, general permission, and vacated use; custom replaces explicit words.

This lesson focuses on the foundational Hanafi ruling on what makes a place a mosque. The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes that explicit endowment wording is unnecessary; what matters is the owner's intent, permission, and community practice. The three conditions are derived from the passage's discussion of mosques built for funeral or Eid prayers and the role of custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Conditions
Read the passage and locate the three conditions mentioned: the land must be owned, the builder must grant general permission for prayer, and the place must be vacated for that purpose. The text says 'he indicated by limiting to the three conditions' – find those conditions.
The conditions are not listed in a single sentence but inferred from the commentary.
2
Understand the Role of Custom
The passage explains that custom ('urf) can substitute for explicit permission or endowment wording. The example of offering food or scattering money shows that customary practice implies permission. Note that this is a Hanafi use of istihsan.
Custom is accepted because it indicates the owner's implied consent.
3
Contrast with al-Shafi'i's Requirement
The text mentions that Malik and Ahmad agree with the Hanafi view, while al-Shafi'i requires an explicit endowment formula. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different weights given to custom versus explicit utterance.
The Hanafi position is upheld in this text; the author mentions the dispute but does not fully critique al-Shafi'i.
4
Apply to a Concrete Scenario
Consider a person who builds a room on his own land and allows neighbors to pray there daily for years. Under the three conditions, this room becomes a mosque. If he had only allowed prayer for one day, it would not become a mosque. Test your understanding with the practice tasks.
Temporal permission does not create a permanent mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف عن جعله مسجداً لا مسجداً؛ كذا يصير في الخانية. وأطلق في المسجد فشمل المتخذ لصلاة الجنازة أو العيد، وفي الخانية: مسجد اتخذ لصلاة الجنازة أو لصلاة العيد هل يكون له حكم المسجد؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه قال بعضهم : يكون مسجداً حتى لو مات لا يورث عنه. وقال بعضهم : ما اتخذ لصلاة الجنازة فهو مسجد لا يورث عنه، وما اتخذ لصلاة العيد لا يكون مسجداً مطلقاً وإنما يعطى له حكم المسجد في صحة الاقتداء بالإمام وإن كان منفصلاً الصفوف، وأما فيما سوى ذلك فليس له حكم المسجد، وقال بعضهم : له حكم المسجد حال أداء الصلاة لا غير وهو والجبانة سواء، ويجنب هذا المكان كما يجنب المسجد احتياطاً اهـ. فأفاد بالاقتصار على الشروط الثلاثة أنه لا يحتاج في جعله مسجداً إلى قوله «وقفته» ونحوه لأن العرف جار بالإذن في الصلاة على وجه العموم والتخلية بكونه وقفاً على هذه الجهة فكان كالتعبير به فكان كمن قدم طعاماً إلى ضيفه أو نثر نثاراً كان إذناً في أكله والتقاطه بخلاف الوقف على الفقراء لم تجر عادة فيه بالتخلية والإذن بالاستغلال، ولو جرت به في عرف اكتفينا بذلك كمسألتنا، وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد خلافاً للشافعي. وأفاد أيضاً أنه لو قال وقفته مسجداً ولم يأذن بالصلاة فيه ولم يصل فيه أحد لا يصير مسجدا بلا حكم وهو بعيد . ذكر في فتح القدير أن هذا مقتضى كلامهم ولم يعزه إلى النقل. وفي الحاوي القدسي : ومن بنى مسجداً في أرض مملوكة له إلى آخره فأفاد أن من شرطه ملك الأرض ولذا قال في الخانية : ولو أن سلطاناً أذن لقوم أن يجعلوا أرضاً من أراضي البلدة حوانيت موقوفة على المسجد أو أمرهم أن يزيدوا في مسجدهم قالوا : إن كانت البلدة فتحت عنوة وذلك لا يضر بالمارة والناس ينفذ أمر السلطان فيها، وإن كانت البلدة فتحت صلحاً لا ينفذ أمر السلطان لأن في الأول تصير ملكاً للغانمين فجاز أمر السلطان فيها، وفي الثاني تبقى على ملك ملاكها فلا ينفذ أمره فيها .اهـ. ولذا قالوا لو اشترى داراً لها شفيع فجعلها مسجداً كان للشفيع أن يأخذها بالشفعة، وكذا إذا كان للبائع حق الاسترداد كان له أن يبطل المسجد؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وأشار بإطلاق قوله ويأذن للناس في الصلاة أنه لا يشترط أن يقول أذنت فيه بالصلاة جماعة أبداً بل الإطلاق كافٍ لكن لو قال صلوا فيه جماعة صلاة أو صلاتين يوماً أو شهراً لا يكون مسجداً كما صرح به في الذخيرة، وقدمناه عن الخانية في الرحبة. وفي القنية : اختلف في مسجد الدار والخان والرباط أنه مسجد جماعة أم لا الأصح ما روي عن أبي يوسف أنه إذا أغلق باب الدار فهو مسجد جماعة للجماعة التي في الدار إذا لم يمنعوا غيرهم من الصلاة فيه في سائر الأوقات لأن مسجد الزقاق الذي ليس بنافذ مسجد جماعة فإن صلوا فيه في وقت أغلقوا باب الزقاق كذا هذا وعنه إن كان فيه جماعة ممن في الدار بعد الإغلاق لا يمنعون غيرهم في الأوقات الأخر فهو مسجد جماعة وإلا فلا. (فخ) مثله . وعن محمد الأوزجندي: لا يجوز الاعتكاف في مسجد زقاق غير نافذ لأن طريقه مملوك لأهله إلا إذا كان له حائط إلى طريق نافذ فحينئذ يمكن التطرق إليه من حق العامة فيخلص الله تعالى فيصير مسجداً. قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : والذي اختاره (فخ) أصح. وقد رأينا ببخارى وغيرها في دور وسكك في أزقة غير نافذة من غير شك الأئمة والعوام في كونها مساجد فعلى هذا المساجد التي في المدارس بجرجانية خوارزم مساجد لأنهم لا يمنعون الناس من الصلاة فيها، وإذا أغلقت يكون فيها جماعة من أهلها .اهـ.
The Book of Waqf. Regarding making it a mosque without [explicit] wording: it becomes so in al-Khaniyya. He generalized 'mosque' to include those made for funeral or Eid prayer. In al-Khaniyya: a mosque made for funeral or Eid prayer, does it have the ruling of a mosque? The mashayikh differed: some said it is a mosque so that if the owner dies it is not inherited. Some said: what is made for funeral prayer is a mosque and is not inherited, but what is made for Eid prayer is not a mosque absolutely, rather it is given the ruling of a mosque regarding validity of following the imam even if the rows are disconnected, but besides that it does not have the ruling of a mosque. Some said: it has the ruling of a mosque only during prayer, and it is like a graveyard, and this place is made inviolable like a mosque out of precaution. End. So he indicated by limiting to the three conditions that making it a mosque does not require saying 'I have endowed it' etc., because custom is established for general permission to pray and vacating it as a endowment for this purpose, so it is like expressing it, like someone who offers food to his guest or scatters coins, it is permission to eat or pick up, unlike endowment for the poor where custom is not established for vacating and permission for use; if custom were established we would suffice with it like our issue. And by our statement: Malik and Ahmad said, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And he also indicated that if he said 'I have made it a mosque' but did not permit prayer and no one prayed, it does not become a mosque without a ruling, and it is far-fetched. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that this is the implication of their words, and he did not attribute it to transmission. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Whoever builds a mosque on land owned by him... up to the end, so he indicated that among its conditions is ownership of the land. Hence in al-Khaniyya: If a sultan permits a people to make land from the city's lands as shops endowed for a mosque, or ordered them to expand their mosque, they said: if the city was conquered by force and that does not harm passers-by, the sultan's order is executed; if it was conquered by treaty, the sultan's order is not executed because in the first case the land becomes property of the conquerors so the sultan's order is valid, in the second it remains the property of its owners so his order is not executed. End. Hence they said: if someone bought a house with a preemptor and made it a mosque, the preemptor may take it by preemption; likewise if the seller had a right of rescission, he may annul the mosque; as in Fath al-Qadir. And he indicated by his absolute statement 'and he permits people to pray' that it is not necessary to say 'I permit prayer in it in congregation forever', rather absolute is sufficient. But if he said 'pray in it in congregation for one prayer or two prayers, a day or a month', it is not a mosque, as stated in al-Dhakhira, and we mentioned it from al-Khaniyya regarding the courtyard. In al-Qunyah: There is disagreement about the mosque of a house, inn, and convent whether it is a congregational mosque or not. The most correct is what is narrated from Abu Yusuf: if the door of the house is closed, it is a congregational mosque for the congregation in the house if they do not prevent others from praying in it at other times, because the mosque in a dead-end alley is a congregational mosque; if they pray in it at a time and close the alley door, it is similar. And from him: if there is a congregation of those in the house after closure and they do not prevent others at other times, it is a congregational mosque, otherwise not. (Fakhr al-Islam) said similar. From Muhammad al-Uzjandi: i'tikaf is not permissible in a mosque of a dead-end alley because its way is owned by its residents, unless it has a wall to a through road, then access by public right is possible and it becomes a mosque. Radi al-Din said: the choice of Fakhr al-Islam is more correct. We have seen in Bukhara and elsewhere in houses and alleys in dead-end alleys, without doubt the imams and common people consider them mosques. On this basis, the mosques in the schools at Jurjaniyya Khwarazm are mosques because they do not prevent people from praying in them, and when closed they have a congregation of its residents. End.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the conditions for a place to become a mosque. The author first relates a discussion from al-Khaniyya about mosques built for funeral or Eid prayers: there is disagreement among scholars whether these have full mosque status. Some say they are full mosques (so not inherited), others restrict rulings. The key point is that for a place to become a mosque, three conditions are sufficient: ownership of the land, general permission for prayer, and vacating the place for that purpose. Custom ('urf) plays a key role: if people customarily treat a place as a mosque by praying in it freely, it becomes a mosque even without explicit endowment words. This is the Hanafi view, shared by Malik and Ahmad, but al-Shafi'i disagrees requiring explicit declaration. The text also clarifies that land ownership is essential: a sultan can only make a mosque on conquered land if he has authority; on treaty land he cannot override owners. If a house with a preemptor is turned into a mosque, the preemptor may still take it by preemption. Temporal permission (for a day or month) does not make a permanent mosque. Finally, a mosque in a dead-end alley is considered a congregational mosque if residents allow others to pray, and i'tikaf is valid if there is public access through a wall to a thoroughfare. The author notes that in practice, such places are treated as mosques in many regions.

Key Terms
مسجد (masjid): A place prepared and set aside for prayer with the conditions of ownership, permission, and vacated use.
زقاق غير نافذ (zuqāq ghayr nāfidh): A dead-end alley whose way is owned by its residents.
عرف (‘urf): Customary practice that is accepted as a legal basis in the absence of explicit text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following are required for a place to become a mosque?
A) Explicit endowment words, general permission, and ownership.
B) Ownership, general permission, and vacated use.
C) Ownership, explicit endowment, and a minbar.
D) General permission, a congregational prayer, and a dome.

Key Takeaway
A place becomes a mosque under Hanafi law when it is owned, permission for prayer is given generally, and it is set aside for that purpose; custom replaces explicit wording.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate

Custom ('Urf) as a Legal Basis for Mosque Status
Expansion on the sufficiency of custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how custom ('urf) substitutes for explicit permission in making a place a mosque and contrast the Hanafi view with that of al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Customary permission through action suffices to make a mosque; the Hanafi school accepts 'urf in place of explicit words.

This lesson delves into the role of custom ('urf) in the Hanafi doctrine of mosque establishment. The passage uses the analogy of offering food or scattering coins to show that customary actions imply permission. The dispute with al-Shafi'i, who requires explicit endowment wording, is a key point of difference. Understanding this helps appreciate the Hanafi reliance on 'urf as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Analogies Used
The text gives two analogies: offering food to a guest (implies permission to eat) and scattering money (implies permission to pick up). Grasp how these illustrate implicit permission through custom.
These analogies are from everyday life, showing that custom carries legal weight.
2
Understand the Hanafi Principle of 'Urf
In Hanafi usul, 'urf (custom) is a recognized source of law in the absence of explicit text. Here, the custom of people praying in a place with the owner's acquiescence effectively constitutes permission.
The text contrasts the endowment for the poor, where custom does not normally imply permission to use the property.
3
Analyze the Dispute with al-Shafi'i
The passage states that Malik and Ahmad agree with the Hanafi view, while al-Shafi'i opposes it. Consider why al-Shafi'i might require explicit wording (e.g., stronger emphasis on verbal contracts).
The dispute is methodological: al-Shafi'i requires explicit sighah, while Hanafi uses 'urf.
4
Apply to a Scenario
In a community where people have been using a room for prayer for years without any formal declaration, does it become a mosque? Under Hanafi, yes, because of custom. Under Shafi'i, no. Test this with the practice tasks.
Practical difference: inheritance and sanctity of the space.

نثاراً كان إذناً في أكله والتقاطه بخلاف الوقف على الفقراء لم تجر عادة فيه بالتخلية والإذن بالاستغلال، ولو جرت به في عرف اكتفينا بذلك كمسألتنا، وبقولنا قال مالك وأحمد خلافاً للشافعي. وأفاد أيضاً أنه لو قال وقفته مسجداً ولم يأذن بالصلاة فيه ولم يصل فيه أحد لا يصير مسجدا بلا حكم وهو بعيد . ذكر في فتح القدير أن هذا مقتضى كلامهم ولم يعزه إلى النقل. وفي الحاوي القدسي : ومن بنى مسجداً في أرض مملوكة له إلى آخره فأفاد أن من شرطه ملك الأرض ولذا قال في الخانية : ولو أن سلطاناً أذن لقوم أن يجعلوا أرضاً من أراضي البلدة حوانيت موقوفة على المسجد أو أمرهم أن يزيدوا في مسجدهم قالوا : إن كانت البلدة فتحت عنوة وذلك لا يضر بالمارة والناس ينفذ أمر السلطان فيها، وإن كانت البلدة فتحت صلحاً لا ينفذ أمر السلطان لأن في الأول تصير ملكاً للغانمين فجاز أمر السلطان فيها، وفي الثاني تبقى على ملك ملاكها فلا ينفذ أمره فيها .اهـ. ولذا قالوا لو اشترى داراً لها شفيع فجعلها مسجداً كان للشفيع أن يأخذها بالشفعة، وكذا إذا كان للبائع حق الاسترداد كان له أن يبطل المسجد؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وأشار بإطلاق قوله ويأذن للناس في الصلاة أنه لا يشترط أن يقول أذنت فيه بالصلاة جماعة أبداً بل الإطلاق كافٍ لكن لو قال صلوا فيه جماعة صلاة أو صلاتين يوماً أو شهراً لا يكون مسجداً كما صرح به في الذخيرة، وقدمناه عن الخانية في الرحبة. وفي القنية : اختلف في مسجد الدار والخان والرباط أنه مسجد جماعة أم لا الأصح ما روي عن أبي يوسف أنه إذا أغلق باب الدار فهو مسجد جماعة للجماعة التي في الدار إذا لم يمنعوا غيرهم من الصلاة فيه في سائر الأوقات لأن مسجد الزقاق الذي ليس بنافذ مسجد جماعة فإن صلوا فيه في وقت أغلقوا باب الزقاق كذا هذا وعنه إن كان فيه جماعة ممن في الدار بعد الإغلاق لا يمنعون غيرهم في الأوقات الأخر فهو مسجد جماعة وإلا فلا. (فخ) مثله . وعن محمد الأوزجندي: لا يجوز الاعتكاف في مسجد زقاق غير نافذ لأن طريقه مملوك لأهله إلا إذا كان له حائط إلى طريق نافذ فحينئذ يمكن التطرق إليه من حق العامة فيخلص الله تعالى فيصير مسجداً. قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : والذي اختاره (فخ) أصح. وقد رأينا ببخارى وغيرها في دور وسكك في أزقة غير نافذة من غير شك الأئمة والعوام في كونها مساجد فعلى هذا المساجد التي في المدارس بجرجانية خوارزم مساجد لأنهم لا يمنعون الناس من الصلاة فيها، وإذا أغلقت يكون فيها جماعة من أهلها .اهـ.
The Book of Waqf. Regarding making it a mosque without [explicit] wording: it becomes so in al-Khaniyya. He generalized 'mosque' to include those made for funeral or Eid prayer. In al-Khaniyya: a mosque made for funeral or Eid prayer, does it have the ruling of a mosque? The mashayikh differed: some said it is a mosque so that if the owner dies it is not inherited. Some said: what is made for funeral prayer is a mosque and is not inherited, but what is made for Eid prayer is not a mosque absolutely, rather it is given the ruling of a mosque regarding validity of following the imam even if the rows are disconnected, but besides that it does not have the ruling of a mosque. Some said: it has the ruling of a mosque only during prayer, and it is like a graveyard, and this place is made inviolable like a mosque out of precaution. End. So he indicated by limiting to the three conditions that making it a mosque does not require saying 'I have endowed it' etc., because custom is established for general permission to pray and vacating it as a endowment for this purpose, so it is like expressing it, like someone who offers food to his guest or scatters coins, it is permission to eat or pick up, unlike endowment for the poor where custom is not established for vacating and permission for use; if custom were established we would suffice with it like our issue. And by our statement: Malik and Ahmad said, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And he also indicated that if he said 'I have made it a mosque' but did not permit prayer and no one prayed, it does not become a mosque without a ruling, and it is far-fetched. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that this is the implication of their words, and he did not attribute it to transmission. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Whoever builds a mosque on land owned by him... up to the end, so he indicated that among its conditions is ownership of the land. Hence in al-Khaniyya: If a sultan permits a people to make land from the city's lands as shops endowed for a mosque, or ordered them to expand their mosque, they said: if the city was conquered by force and that does not harm passers-by, the sultan's order is executed; if it was conquered by treaty, the sultan's order is not executed because in the first case the land becomes property of the conquerors so the sultan's order is valid, in the second it remains the property of its owners so his order is not executed. End. Hence they said: if someone bought a house with a preemptor and made it a mosque, the preemptor may take it by preemption; likewise if the seller had a right of rescission, he may annul the mosque; as in Fath al-Qadir. And he indicated by his absolute statement 'and he permits people to pray' that it is not necessary to say 'I permit prayer in it in congregation forever', rather absolute is sufficient. But if he said 'pray in it in congregation for one prayer or two prayers, a day or a month', it is not a mosque, as stated in al-Dhakhira, and we mentioned it from al-Khaniyya regarding the courtyard. In al-Qunyah: There is disagreement about the mosque of a house, inn, and convent whether it is a congregational mosque or not. The most correct is what is narrated from Abu Yusuf: if the door of the house is closed, it is a congregational mosque for the congregation in the house if they do not prevent others from praying in it at other times, because the mosque in a dead-end alley is a congregational mosque; if they pray in it at a time and close the alley door, it is similar. And from him: if there is a congregation of those in the house after closure and they do not prevent others at other times, it is a congregational mosque, otherwise not. (Fakhr al-Islam) said similar. From Muhammad al-Uzjandi: i'tikaf is not permissible in a mosque of a dead-end alley because its way is owned by its residents, unless it has a wall to a through road, then access by public right is possible and it becomes a mosque. Radi al-Din said: the choice of Fakhr al-Islam is more correct. We have seen in Bukhara and elsewhere in houses and alleys in dead-end alleys, without doubt the imams and common people consider them mosques. On this basis, the mosques in the schools at Jurjaniyya Khwarazm are mosques because they do not prevent people from praying in them, and when closed they have a congregation of its residents. End.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the conditions for a place to become a mosque. The author first relates a discussion from al-Khaniyya about mosques built for funeral or Eid prayers: there is disagreement among scholars whether these have full mosque status. Some say they are full mosques (so not inherited), others restrict rulings. The key point is that for a place to become a mosque, three conditions are sufficient: ownership of the land, general permission for prayer, and vacating the place for that purpose. Custom ('urf) plays a key role: if people customarily treat a place as a mosque by praying in it freely, it becomes a mosque even without explicit endowment words. This is the Hanafi view, shared by Malik and Ahmad, but al-Shafi'i disagrees requiring explicit declaration. The text also clarifies that land ownership is essential: a sultan can only make a mosque on conquered land if he has authority; on treaty land he cannot override owners. If a house with a preemptor is turned into a mosque, the preemptor may still take it by preemption. Temporal permission (for a day or month) does not make a permanent mosque. Finally, a mosque in a dead-end alley is considered a congregational mosque if residents allow others to pray, and i'tikaf is valid if there is public access through a wall to a thoroughfare. The author notes that in practice, such places are treated as mosques in many regions.

Key Terms
مسجد (masjid): A place prepared and set aside for prayer with the conditions of ownership, permission, and vacated use.
زقاق غير نافذ (zuqāq ghayr nāfidh): A dead-end alley whose way is owned by its residents.
عرف (‘urf): Customary practice that is accepted as a legal basis in the absence of explicit text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi position on using custom to establish a mosque?
A) Custom is not sufficient; explicit words are always required.
B) Custom is sufficient if it indicates general permission and vacated use.
C) Custom is sufficient only for funeral prayer mosques, not for others.
D) Custom is never considered because it is not a source of law.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) suffices to make a place a mosque under Hanafi law when it demonstrates general permission and vacated use, replacing the need for explicit endowment words.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
8 min
Temporal Permission and the Requirement of Permanence
Clarification on temporal vs. permanent permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between general permission that creates a permanent mosque and temporal permission that does not, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving limited-time permissions.

Core Idea
Temporal permission for prayer does not create a permanent mosque; only general, ongoing permission and vacated use suffice.

This lesson clarifies a crucial detail: if a person says 'pray here for one prayer' or 'for a month', that does not make the place a mosque. The text emphasizes that the permission must be general and ongoing, not limited. This prevents temporary prayer spaces from acquiring the permanent legal status of a mosque, with all its implications for inheritance, sanctity, and endowment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Key Statement on Temporal Permission
Find in the passage: 'but if he said pray in it in congregation for one prayer or two prayers, a day or a month, it is not a mosque' (from al-Dhakhira). Note the contrast with 'absolute sufficient' earlier.
The phrase 'absolute sufficient' means general permission without time limit.
2
Understand the Rationale
A mosque is a permanent waqf, which requires continuity. A limited permission does not demonstrate the owner's intent to permanently dedicate the place.
This protects the owner's rights: a temporary arrangement cannot create an irrevocable endowment.
3
Apply to Examples
Consider a homeowner who allows neighbors to pray in his living room during Ramadan only. This does not make it a mosque. Contrast with a room set aside for prayer all year round with general permission.
The distinction is in the scope of permission: general vs. limited.
4
Relate to the Three Conditions
Temporal permission fails the condition of 'vacated use' because the place is not permanently vacated for prayer. Also, general permission is not given.
All three conditions must be met in a permanent sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوقف عن جعله مسجداً لا مسجداً؛ كذا يصير في الخانية. وأطلق في المسجد فشمل المتخذ لصلاة الجنازة أو العيد، وفي الخانية: مسجد اتخذ لصلاة الجنازة أو لصلاة العيد هل يكون له حكم المسجد؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه قال بعضهم : يكون مسجداً حتى لو مات لا يورث عنه. وقال بعضهم : ما اتخذ لصلاة الجنازة فهو مسجد لا يورث عنه، وما اتخذ لصلاة العيد لا يكون مسجداً مطلقاً وإنما يعطى له حكم المسجد في صحة الاقتداء بالإمام وإن كان منفصلاً الصفوف، وأما فيما سوى ذلك فليس له حكم المسجد، وقال بعضهم : له حكم المسجد حال أداء الصلاة لا غير وهو والجبانة سواء، ويجنب هذا المكان كما يجنب المسجد احتياطاً اهـ. فأفاد بالاقتصار على Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following permissions would create a permanent mosque?
A) 'You may pray here only on Fridays.'
B) 'Pray here for the next month.'
C) 'This space is for prayer whenever you wish.'
D) 'You may pray the Eid prayer here each year.'

Key Takeaway
General permission must be ongoing and unlimited; temporal permission for a limited time or specific occasion does not make a place a mosque.
